Chapter 1

Brock stumbled to a halt beneath the full moon, staring at the view. His breath faltered and his heart raced, but whether from the exertion of his hard climb through Brockenhurst Mountains, or the scene spread out in the valley below, he wasn't sure. Brockenhurst Forest at last; a place of magical promises, a source of all knowledge and wisdom. And nestled within its protective environment, Brockenhurst Sett; birthplace of Boddaert, the greatest Teller of all time; Father of the race.
As Brock's eyes ranged across the forest below, his excitement grew. He sang a sonnet to calm himself, allowing the tensions to flow from his body. His heart slowed, keeping pace with the simple rhythms of the song. As his thoughts turned to the teachings of The Way, he allowed its perfection to refresh his tired muscles.
Brock was the latest in the line of Tellers stretching back into the mists of time. His lineage boasted such names as Evaert and Char, both still talked about on hot summer-cycles, when the crickets sang their songs of lust. He studied the rocky mountain slope for the easiest descent into the valley. To the north, a tall escarpment brought the steady march of the trees to an abrupt halt. Here the only relief from the stark granite wall was a gigantic, flat-topped rock, thrusting its way up out of the canopy. Regularly shaped sides, strangely smooth, with little evidence of weathering, its top flat as a pool of water reflected moonlight in dazzling sparkles of brightness. Reaching into his memory, Brock summoned its name — Fire Rock. Laughing loudly, pleased he had reached the end of his journey at last, he set out on the descent into Brockenhurst Valley.
The stuttering cry of a magpie carried on a gentle southerly breeze. The trek down from the mountains had been hard and dangerous, but Brock stood now on a wide path amongst the hoary trees of the old forest, his eyes widening as he took in the scene.
A vole flicked across the damp forest floor, almost indistinguishable from the dead brown leaves, stirring Brock into motion. He'd rested long enough; inactivity was allowing unpleasant memories to stir. He rubbed the wound on his leg, trying to suppress the echoes of his dying sister's screams, but no matter how hard he tried, he couldn't stop the memories flooding his mind.
*
The fire had been swift and savage, burning everything in its path. The flames jumped from grass to bush, from bush to tree, too fast to outrun. And with the crackling and roaring came another unforgettable sound: the screams of the dying. The thick acrid smoke had coiled its oily tentacles into the deepest sleeping chambers, suffocating those not already overwhelmed by the flames, and only Brock's knowledge of The Way had saved him. He was the sole survivor, and it left him feeling a deep shame.
Since starting out on this journey, Brock had reproached himself many times. He was a Teller of The Way, the Keeper of their History; trained to predict the future and read the past. Yet the fire had come as a complete surprise.
Standing in the moon-dappled clearing, fighting his feelings, Brock tried to push his tortured thoughts aside. Overhead, two starlings watched him warily from their nest, wondering what threat he might pose.
Brock shook his head. "Enough of this," he scolded himself. "Find the Custodians."
*
Resuming his journey, Brock took only a few steps when a loud voice hailed him.
"And who's this dreamer? Certainly an ill-mannered landloper to ignore me so diligently!"
Brock frowned, studying the old badger standing fore-square on the path. The stranger nodded, settling his plump body into a more comfortable position. The moonlight sparkled from silver hairs sprinkled liberally throughout his coat.
Lowering his snout in respect, Brock hailed the badger. "Greetings friend. Forgive me, I was lost in my thoughts and didn't see you. I'm looking for Brockenhurst Sett. Can you tell me if this is the right path?"
The old badger's eyes narrowed before he slowly nodded, obviously reluctant to share such information. "Indeed, it is. But tell me, what business takes you there?"
Brock narrowed his own eyes.
The boar dipped his head. "Ah, I see I might have offended you with my curiosity, but if you intend spending time in Brockenhurst Sett, you'll get used to that." The old badger's chest expanded proudly. "I'm a Custodian, so it's my duty to be nosy." He winked and grinned.
Brock's heart beat a little faster. Could it be just a coincidence the first badger he met in Brockenhurst was a Custodian?
"So, who are you stranger and where from?" The Custodian's deep set eyes glinted in the moonlight, loaning him an impish look, despite his obvious age.
"I'm Brock, out of High Green. Ten moons walk beyond the Brockenhurst Mountains."
"By Homer!" The Custodian nodded his enormous head, obviously impressed. "Ten moons, you say?" Giving this information some thought, he moved closer, scrutinising Brock closely. "And what brings you on such an arduous journey?"
"I must speak to the Council. I bring important news. Fire destroyed my sett, and…"
"Destroyed!" interrupted the Custodian, the shock of Brock's words reflected in his expression.
"There was a dreadful fire." Brock lowered his gaze, adding in subdued tones. "A fire so swift and fierce that none but myself survived."
There could be no mistaking the bitterness clouding the young badger's eyes, and the old Custodian fidgeted uncomfortably.
*
Sharing his despair brought back images of the dreadful fire. Brock was back in the sett, digging furiously into the packed earthen floor of his sleeping chamber so the heat would pass overhead and do him no harm. Satisfied he was deep enough, he lay down, scrabbled a layer of earth over his body, and using the power of The Way, slowed his breathing; a technique taught to neophyte Tellers during their training. He hoped it would let him survive the coming conflagration. He blanked out the shrieks of his dying friends, concentrating all his energy on surviving. Closing his eyes, he implored the Prime Mover to save him.
Buried safely in his hiding place, Brock survived the intense heat as the fire passed harmlessly overhead. He emerged to a scene of complete devastation, spending the rest of the moonlight wandering through the blackened tunnels, searching for survivors. Brock called in vain, but there was no badger alive to hear him.
*
Brock suddenly realised the Custodian was speaking. "Sorry, what did you say?"
"My name is Grey," the old badger repeated patiently, favouring Brock with a quizzical look. "Are you alright? You seem preoccupied?"
"I'm tired and I hurt my leg in the fire." Brock shrugged. "But tell me, is this the path to Brockenhurst Sett? I must see the Council at once."
Grey nodded slowly, looking along the path. "Yes, this is the path, but there's no point rushing. If you want to see the Council, you must seek permission first."
Brock sighed impatiently, touching the wound on his leg. "But there's no time. When the fire destroyed High Green, I used the powers of The Way to escape." He paused, looking uncomfortable for a moment. "During the fire I saw a vision."
The Custodian's nose twitched, his eyes widening. "Then you're a Teller of The Way?"
Brock nodded, his eyes glazing as he stared across the wide path into the trees. "Yes, but that's not the point," he answered. He swayed back and forth, as though having trouble standing. "What I saw in the vision…" He paused, not sure how best to continue. "It's… you see…" He faltered again, eyes rolling as he collapsed onto the path.
"By Homer, badger!" Grey exclaimed, bending over the prostrate boar and shaking him. "Come on, let's get you back to the sett. We've a Healer there who'll know what to do with you."
Grey helped Brock to his feet, and they staggered along in silence through the moon-washed trees, the older supporting the younger, their progress a series of disjointed stumbles. Grey quickly realised he didn't have the strength to drag the young badger all the way back to Brockenhurst Sett himself, so he gently lowered the half-conscious boar onto the dark soil, looking down at him, concern puckering his snout.
Brock's eyes unexpectedly opened in a wild stare. "Run, Dana, run!" he shouted. "There's smoke in the tunnels." His feet jerked wildly, and he let out a long, woeful groan, then passed out.
Grey frowned, wondering what to do. Finally he gathered a mound of leaves and carefully covered Brock, making sure he left the young badger's mouth uncovered. He stood back and nodded. It was the best he could do. Turning back to the path, Grey headed off towards Brockenhurst Sett. If anyone could help this unfortunate badger, it was their Healer, Soffen.
*
Deep beneath Fire Rock, in chambers known only to himself, a deformed old badger sighed. At last, The Messenger had come. Now his plans could progress. Reaching out with his mind, he searched the stranger's thoughts, then frowned. Uncertainty sent a shiver through his body, but his twisted features broke into a smile. He was secure in his own power; no badger could threaten him, not while he had the power of the Dark Healing to help him.

Chapter 2

aaaSoffen glanced at the sky, wrinkling her snout at the glow on the horizon. The sun was rising. Time they got back to the sett. The remaining herbs could be collected tomorrow. She smiled affectionately, watching Raffen sniff at a plant, giggling when the pollen made her sneeze.
"Is this Baneberry?" Raffen asked, dislodging the pollen with a shake of her head.
"No Raffen, that's Ground Elder. Look, there's some Baneberry over there. By that rotting stump."
They'd been collecting herbs for most of the moon. Hemlock, Wormwood, Hyssop, and many other plants Soffen needed to restock her dwindling herbaria. Raffen fetched the Baneberry, studying the unusual colour of Soffen's coat and eyes, which were much lighter than other badgers. Soffen looked back over her shoulder at Raffen, a feeling of warmth suffusing her body. She felt lucky to have such a loyal friend. Most other badgers avoided her, pretending to be busy when she appeared. They were frightened and distrustful of her powers, but that made little difference to the pain such rejection caused. They thought a Healer had no feelings.
Soffen realised, better than most, the Council fostered this distrust, but she could do little to change it. When her father first trained her in the secrets of The Healing, he hadn't explained how lonely her life would be. How her peers would shun her, how even the older badgers would mistrust her. He should have told her what she would endure. If he had, she might well have chosen a different path.
She sighed, trying to shake off the feeling of foreboding overshadowing her spirit. Being a Healer had its compensations, she couldn't deny it, but having close companions was not one of them. She smiled at Raffen again, a tightness closing her throat. Apart from this one sow, the only other badgers she had contact with were those seeking help for some illness or injury, and they quickly disappeared once she treated them.
"Soffen?" Raffen's voice was thick with concern. "You seem so serious. Is something wrong?"
"Sorry, did you say something?" Soffen, still distracted by her inner turmoil, had missed her friend's words. Raffen repeated the question. Soffen shrugged, trying to appear indifferent. "Oh, it's nothing really. I was just thinking about which herbs to gather tomorrow."
"But you look so sad. Are you worried about leaving your cubs on their own?"
Soffen inhaled sharply, her heart fluttering. Raffen knew about the cubs! But how was that possible?
A tingling sensation ran the length of her spine. "How do you know about my cubs? I've told no one."
With a toss of her head, Raffen smiled mischievously. "I know that silly, but you didn't need to tell me. It's been so obvious. I've got eyes, you know. I'm not stupid. Did you really think you could hide being in-cub from me? I spotted it ages ago, before you moved out of the main sett. And look at you now, so slim, so sleek, your coat and eyes all shiny." Making a mock-serious face, Raffen wrinkled her snout. "You may be a Healer, Soffen, but I really wonder about you sometimes." Placing a gentle paw on her friend's flank, she giggled. "You've been the talk of the sett for ages."
Soffen turned away, scrutinising a distant point high in the trees, a sad, almost lost expression clouding her eyes.
Raffen moved closer, rustling the leaves beneath her paws, her playful mood dispersing. "I'm sorry, Soffen, I didn't mean to upset you. Come on, tell me what's troubling you."
Soffen turned back, a half-smile on her lips, torn between wanting to share her secret and the realisation that doing so may place her cubs in mortal danger. Struggling with her conflict, she stared down at the ground. Being a Healer, Soffen knew better than most how the collective mores of the sett far outweighed any individual rights, but that didn't change the turmoil in her mind.
Seeing the strain on her friend's face, Raffen nuzzled the soft fur just behind her ear — a gesture of friendship and comfort all badgers recognised from cubhood. "Whatever it is, you can tell me Soffen, I'm your friend. I love you, nothing can change that."
Soffen stared deeply into her friend's eyes, suddenly overpowered by the need to share, to lighten the burden she was carrying. "You must promise me you won't repeat this to any other badger, Raffen," she blurted,
"Well, if it means that much to you, of course I won't. I promise not to say anything to any badger."
"Even the Custodians?" Soffen stared hard at her friend, then spun away, her words carrying an inflection that was half anger, half regret. "No, it's not fair of me to ask that. I'm sorry, just forget what I've said."
Raffen wrinkled her snout, smiling, coaxing Soffen back to a better mood. "Oh, tush to the Custodians and their silly ways." She giggled mischievously. "Just tell me. I won't repeat anything you say to those fools."
Relieved by her friend's promise, Soffen responded with a smile. "Really Raffen, you shouldn't talk that way about the Custodians. If they overheard you…"
Raffen laughed loudly, shrugging expansively. "Well, what good are they anyway, sitting up there full of their own self-importance. A fine bunch they make, debating what tunnel should go to which badger. Just who do they think they are, that's what I'd like to know? I mean, what use are they if you cut your paw, or need help cubbing? None, that's what. All right when giving orders, but ask them to do anything else." Raffen tutted and winked. "Now you? Well, badgers come from far and wide for your healing powers, don't they? You're worth more than any ten Custodians put together. Oh, I feel so angry about the way they treat you sometimes."
"They're just a little frightened of The Healing," Soffen replied through a grin, even though bitterness tinged her words. "You know, sometimes I really think they see me as a threat and wish I wasn't here."
"Well, if that's true, they're more stupid than I thought!" Raffen retorted. "What threat could you be to anyone? And who would heal us all if you weren't here? Why, we'd be in the most terrible trouble, wouldn't we?"
Soffen lowered her gaze, not wanting her friend to read her expression. She knew Raffen, like most badgers in Brockenhurst Sett, failed to see the significance of the Council in the hierarchy of things.
Soffen patted the ground. "Come and sit next to me. I've something I want to tell you."
Her friend's serious tone troubled Raffen. She could usually dispel Soffen's moods, but this was different. Clearing a space amongst the dead leaves, Raffen settled down next to Soffen, looking at her expectantly.
Soffen poked at an old half-buried pine cone, searching for the right place to begin. "It's true," she acknowledged, picking up the cone and tossing it at nothing in particular, "that I whelped some time ago. Two cubs, in fact." Another cone followed the first. "I've dug a temporary burrow for myself in Low Meadow, by the edge of the big mud pit. That's where my cubs are now."
Raffen shivered. "But it's so cold and wet in Low Meadow. Why didn't you stay in your nice warm sleeping chambers in the main sett?"
Soffen shook her head. "No, I couldn't do that Raffen. You see… well, I just couldn't." Taking a deep breath, she stared earnestly at her friend. "I…" Soffen licked her lips, trying to ease the sticky dryness suddenly filling her mouth. "Well, one of my cubs is…" Stumbling over her words, she let the sentence hang on a long silence.
Concern lit Raffen's eyes. "Soffen, what's the matter? Is one of your cubs ill?"
"Well, it's more than an illness, really." Another long pause, then quickly, urgently, "It has pink eyes," Soffen blinked her own heavily, "and a pink nose." Her next words were a whispered undertone. "Its fur is white, not the silver-grey it should be."
Raffen looked startled. "Your cub's disfigured?" she squealed in a rising voice, shaking her head, eyes wide with fright.
A sob caught in Soffen's throat. "Yes." Looking away, she hid her face. "I know that I should have killed it at birth, but I just couldn't bring myself to do it." Sniffing back her tears, she searched her friend's eyes for a sign of understanding. "I'm a Healer, I couldn't kill my cub. They can't expect that of me."
"But you must!" Raffen's voice cut across the space between them with a sharp, hard edge. "When the Custodians find out what you've done, they'll kill it anyway, and probably banish you from Brockenhurst Sett as well." Placing a paw on Soffen's flank, Raffen emphasised her next words with gentle shakes. "Please Soffen, you must go and tell the Custodians at once, for your own sake. They'll understand."
Soffen shook her head vehemently. "No, I can't do that." She stared into her friend's eyes. "And you, Raffen?" she asked. "Can I trust you to say nothing?"
Raffen looked away, studying the ground, an expression of discomfort creasing her snout. "It's such a big thing to ask," she whispered.
Soffen's stomach lurched as she realised the terrible mistake she'd made. She should have kept her own counsel. Seeking the approval of her friend had been wrong, Raffen would eventually blurt the secret out.
"Soffen, what's happening?" Raffen's voice edged with fear as she looked up at the rapidly darkening sky.
A deep, unnatural calmness unexpectedly gripped the forest. Nothing stirred, even the usually restless leaves hung silently from their branches. The atmosphere was loaded with an urgency; a heaviness that brought a shortness of breath, a tingle of expectation.
Soffen scented the air. "Quickly Raffen, we have to find shelter. There's a storm coming and no ordinary one."
The two friends collected their plants as the storm grew in strength, its heavy energy swirling in and out of the boiling clouds. Soffen, through her training as a Healer, and attuned to the forces of nature, felt the threat gathering overhead.
The unnatural stillness swiftly building around them shattered as a wind howled in from nowhere, and the entire forest shook with its rage. Branches began rattling insanely, and it was impossible to hear anything above the clacker-clacker-clacker rebounding all around them. The sky darkened, its blackness shrouding the billowing clouds. Wind-whipped leaves swirled angrily about their heads, tossed high by the screaming blasts of air.
"Come on," Soffen shouted.
Deep within the forest, a tree groaned, torn from the ground, slamming into a smaller neighbour, snapping it like a twig. The earth trembled as the stricken giant smashed its way downwards, thrusting its mud covered roots at the angry sky in a last futile gesture of appeasement.
The terrified badgers hurried through the rapidly building tempest, battling against the wind, thrown first one way, then another. Soffen did her best to fend off the branches and small bushes swirling around, urgently pulling her friend along the familiar pathways. Fighting the wind, she concentrated her mind on her training, gaining strength from the inner calmness the Healing always gave her. The wind built to an undulating scream, so loud it drowned out the swelling rumbles of thunder shaking the ground. Bright bolts of lightning flickered and hissed overhead.
They pushed their desperate way through the shaking undergrowth; the storm battering them so remorselessly that Soffen, fearing for their lives, almost used her knowledge of the Dark Healing to protect them. A large bush, torn free by the rampaging wind, buffeted into the pair, knocking Soffen from her feet. Raffen screamed, breaking away from the path, running headlong into the storm. Soffen scrabbled upright, running after her friend, almost losing sight of her bobbing figure in the swirling leaves.
She finally caught Raffen, grabbing onto her tail, pulling her into the shelter of a nearby tree. She tried to calm her, stroking her mud-streaked fur as they lay amongst the tangled roots. The old tree groaned and trembled above them, its rough bark trilling as the wind raged across its indentations. It shifted, as if taking its first tentative steps, the straining roots singing and vibrating as they tightened under the strain. Soffen, realising what was about to happen, shouted a warning, and with a mounting panic, hauled Raffen away from the thrumming roots.
They lurched their way out into the full force of the storm, but before they'd taken more than a dozen steps, a long dark shadow loomed overhead. The tree seemed to reach out, reluctant to let them go. For the briefest of moments it hesitated, its long flailing branches writhing in the wind, then slammed down, burying the fleeing figures beneath its tremendous weight.

Chapter 3

After setting out to get help for the stranger, Grey got caught up in the most ferocious storm. It sprang from nowhere, forcing him to shelter beneath a fallen tree, where he heartily cursed the wind as it tried to suck his breath away.
Curling into a tight ball, he did his best to shelter his sensitive snout from the harsh grittiness of the wind-whipped soil, covering his ears against the howling of the wind, trying to think. What should he do? Carry on and fetch the Healer, or go back and stay with the stranger until the storm blew itself out?
 Going back to the sick boar would be of little use; what did he know about the art of Healing? Cursing his luck in running across the badger in the first place, Grey's mind whirled, trying to find a solution to his dilemma.
The old boar finally decided his only choice was to carry on, and hope that he could reach Brockenhurst Sett quickly. As he left the lee of the tree, the full rage of the storm hit him, and it was only the thought of the young badger lying helpless under the mound of leaves that kept him going.
Bent low against the fury of the squall, the old boar thrust his way along the path, battling hard to make any progress against the strong wind. A gust caught him off-guard, buffeting him so violently, it plucked him from his feet, tumbling him along with its fury. A thick bole brought his flight to an abrupt and painful halt. He lay panting in a heap at the base of the tree, soil and small stones pounding his body. Gathering his strength, he staggered to his feet, stumbling into a shallow depression. He lay groaning amongst the sodden roots, trying to recover his breath.
Fighting hard to bring his reeling senses back under control, Grey tried to make sense of the whirling scene raging all round him. Shaking the stinging rain from his eyes, he peered out into the torrent, looking for a way forward through the downpour, heart hammering in his chest.
The tree above him trembled, and all too quickly the trembling turned into wild gyrations, snapping its roots. One flailing end caught Grey a stunning blow across his exposed flank, tossing him high into the air. He landed on his back with a mind-numbing thump. Clawing his way to his feet, he squinted into the lashing rain, trying to ignore the pain lancing his side.
A passionate anger seized him and he screamed at the black clouds. By Homer, he'd beat this storm if it was the last thing he did! He pushed on, time ceasing to have any meaning, as round him the wind shook the giant trees with as much ease as a foraging bird might shake a slender plant in its search for food. The branches were alive with terrifying noises — rattling claws stretching out for him, bringing life to terrors best forgotten. It felt like the entire forest was uprooting itself to march against him, but he persevered, pushing himself hard, slowly winning out against the horrendous forces snapping at his heels.
The wind dropped for a moment, easing the lashing rain, allowing him a brief glimpse of two badgers on the pathway ahead. He set out after them, but the rain renewed its fury and they disappeared from sight.
Not sparing his aching muscles, Grey forced his body forward, adopting a mind-numbing routine that took over his whole being. Struggle a few steps, pause for breath, struggle a few steps, pause for breath — over and over until his actions had no meaning. Grey's legs ached almost beyond endurance, his feet constantly slipping in the sticky mud, the muscles driving him forward weakening, slowing his pace to a crawl. He wouldn't be able to carry on much longer.
Still no sign of the two badgers he'd glimpsed earlier. He could have passed right by them in this murky half-light. Tears of frustration filled his eyes. Somewhere nearby, a tree groaned. Grey paused, ears cocked, trying to locate the direction. Rain streamed from his sodden fur. His skin itched. He trembled with fatigue.
Out of the gloom branches loomed overhead, rattling loudly, threatening to impale him. The tree fell, pulling a smaller neighbour with it, the disjointed staccato noise making him wince.
Breath faltering, Grey shook the rain from his eyes. Had he really seen two badgers break from the base of the falling tree?
Dodging through the undergrowth, their outline hazy in the downpour, the badgers made a mad dash for safety. What the pair didn't see was the tree twisting in their direction. Grey's warning shout went unheard, and he watched, horrified, as the giant trunk split lengthwise before crashing down on them.
Stunned, he gulped wet, earthy air, unable to move. Small branches and leaves cascaded down around him. A branch hit his rump, breaking his inaction. Unmindful of his cuts and bruises, he pushed his way into the heart of the fallen tree, and began a frantic search for the badgers.
Hearing a soft cry, he wriggled under a large branch, ignoring the cold mud oozing into his coat. Struggling to his feet, his breath caught. A young sow lay in her death throes, mewling like a newborn cub. A jagged branch pierced her body, pinning her to the ground. Blood bubbled through her lips as she laboured to fill her lungs. She stared straight at him, her eyes reflecting a terrible pain. Grey recognised her. It was Raffen; for a moment, he'd feared it was the Healer. Pushing aside the relief, Grey rushed to her side, tears stinging his eyes. He nuzzled her neck, trying to comfort her with whispered words.
Raffen coughed, splattering Grey's coat with bright blood. She took a deep, shuddering breath through trembling lips. "Tell Soffen," she whispered. "Tell Soffen — I'm sorry."
Grey patted her flank with a clumsy paw, and called her name, not wanting to admit she was dead, but unable to deny the evidence of his own eyes. He stood by the dead sow for a long time, paw lightly resting on her snout, head bowed in silence, paying his last respects. Finally, with one last glance at the cruelly violated body — the half-closed eyes, delicate snout, small perfect ears — he turned away.
As Grey struggled his way out of the clinging undergrowth, a voice called. "Please… Please help me." Grey tried to pinpoint which direction the voice came from when the voice called again. "Please… I'm hurt. Please help me."
There, under the fallen trunk, on his right.
Grey pushed through the twisted branches, following the weak cries until he located the other badger trapped beneath a thick branch. Working his way closer, he found it was Soffen. "Are you all right? Can you move?" he asked.
Soffen shook her head, her snout wrinkling in pain. "No, my leg's caught. I can't move it."
Grey scrambled under the thick trunk. Soffen's leg lay trapped between the branch and a large rock. He began digging, his thick stubby claws thrusting the earth aside in large scoops. Finally, he loosened the rock enough for Soffen to wrench her leg free. She winced in pain as he helped her up.
"Can you walk? We've got to get you back to the sett."
Soffen took a few tentative steps, limping badly, looking back at him. "Perhaps, if you help me."
Struggling clear of the tree, the pair stood in the lee of a bush for a moment. Soffen's eyes suddenly widened. "Where's Raffen? She was right behind me when the tree fell. Did you see what happened to her?" Taken by surprise, Grey failed to hide his reaction. Soffen clutched at him, digging her claws into his side. "Where is she? Is she hurt? Tell me!"
"She's dead, Soffen. There was nothing I could do. The tree crushed her."
Grey's harsh words cut through her, lancing her heart like a sharp stone. She shook her head wildly, denying the words, her enormous eyes studying Grey's face, imploring him to say it wasn't true. Grey cradled her against his flank, whispering words of comfort as she cried. Eventually, wiping away the last of her tears, she looked up at the Custodian.
"Where is she?" she asked.
Grey nodded towards the twisted branches and silently watched her disappear into the entangled interior. He waited patiently, thoughtfully, lost in his own grief. Raffen had been a happy, well-liked badger; they would miss her laughter.
When Soffen finally reappeared, a hard determination burnt in her eyes. It was apparent something had changed deep within her — something that stirred an uneasy feeling in the pit of Grey's.
"Help me back to my burrow," Soffen said in a quiet voice. "I don't think that I can manage it on my own."
*
After a long and tiring struggle, Grey and Soffen reached the safety of her burrow on the outer edges of Low Meadow, and pushed their way down the narrow entrance tunnel, Grey wondered why any badger would choose such a desolate place to live; the air smelt damp and cold.
Entering the main chamber, he looked about in distaste. "Soffen, why have we come here. Whose burrow is this?"
"Mine," she answered, ignoring his disapproving stare.
He turned to her, bewilderment on his face. "But surely your tunnels are in Bell Clearing, just off the main sett?"
Soffen exhaled deeply. "Yes Grey, but this is where I live now. At least for the present."
He looked about with a sinking sensation. The sett, so unwelcoming, was a terrible place to live. It made no sense. "But why have you moved to such an appalling place?"
Soffen tipped her head, sniffing the air. "Can't you scent them, Grey?" A look of defiance flickered in her eyes.
Grey raised his sensitive snout and there, just beyond the pungency of damp earth and rotting vegetation, he made out a familiar scent. "Cubs," he said, a questioning look flooding his eyes. "But why have you hidden yourself away here and not told the Council? Unless…?" He studied her quizzically, a serious expression creasing his snout.
"Unless there's something wrong?" Soffen finished in a caustic tone. "Is that what you're thinking, Grey?" When the old badger failed to respond, she plunged on recklessly. "Well, you're right, there is something wrong. At least, with one of them." Standing taller, a challenging tilt to her head, she continued in a defiant voice, "He's disfigured."
Grey's breath hissed across his teeth at her bald statement. "And you haven't informed the Council? You've hidden them away here instead?" He looked about in anger, catching her with a piercing stare. "You of all badgers should know better. By Homer, you're a Healer. You use The Way like the rest of us breathe. Surely you're aware of how important it is to follow the creed." Grey's shouted the tenet at her, his voice growing in volume. "You will kill all disfigured, malformed, or aberrant cubs at birth. That's the immutable law, Soffen. You know that. Think of what would happen if we did as we pleased. We must keep ourselves pure to protect our future. It's not open to debate."
Soffen's answer whipped across the enclosed space, and Grey felt its full impact. "Now you listen to me." She took a deep breath to steady her trembling voice. "This goes far beyond the limited knowledge of you, or your precious Custodians. Further even than the ancient laws of The Way!"
Grey's eyes flared at such blasphemy, the fur along his back rising.
"Something dark and powerful happened out there. Something …" Soffen hesitated, searching for the right words, "far beyond our understanding. Something stretching back into our ancient past." Slapping her chest in defiance, she let her voice swell. "I am a Healer, and I know The Way. I have a deep insight into its intricacies. I know the obvious path is not always the right path; the traps that wait for the unwary traveller. And that insight tells me, with no room for doubt, that I should not kill my cub." Then, in a softer but no less challenging tone, "It bids me to do all in my power to find a cure."
"Cure!" Grey's voice boomed off the walls of the small chamber. "Cure? Have you gone completely mad, female? You can't cure a disfigurement. You forget yourself. You're a Healer, not the Prime Mover."
Soffen's voice overflowed with indignation at his attack. "You doubt me, Grey? Knowing my powers as a Healer, you doubt me?"
"Of course I doubt you," he snapped back. "You're too near this thing to realise what you're saying. I have no choice. I will inform the Council at once. I just can't imagine what…" He sputtered to a stop, shaking his head. By Homer, this infuriating female had made him forget why he'd come searching for her. The stranger Brock was still lying out there in the forest!
"Grey, you can't tell the Council." Soffen's eyes blazed with anger. "If you do that, then Raffen will have died for nothing." Confusion clouded the old badger's eyes, but before he could answer, she hurried on. "Raffen threatened to tell the Council, just as you do. The storm killed her, Grey. Don't you understand? Can't you see? It was no accident. The storm sought her out and killed her. She died because she was going to tell the Council."
"ENOUGH!" Soffen jumped as the old Custodian reared up at her. "Enough, I say. I have no time for this arguing. There is something more urgent to do." He hurriedly explained about his meeting with the stranger on the forest path, and how he left the badger to the mercy of the storm. Grey ordered Soffen to accompany him back to the boar.
Soffen heard the old Custodian out, her thoughts swirling. Finally, she shook her head. "No Grey, I won't go."
"Now listen female, he's injured, maybe dying. You're a Healer, he needs your help. It's your duty to attend him."
"And why should I help a Teller of The Way, when The Way commands me to kill my cub? Tell me that, Custodian!"
"Soffen, where's your compassion? This badger has seen his whole sett perish. Would you deny him your help as well?"
Soffen's emotions boiled over into a deep anger. She reared back, spitting her words at Grey with great bitterness. "How dare you! How dare you question my ethics? You… you,,," Taking a deep breath, she steadied herself. "You come here, order me to kill my cub, and then you have the audacity, the insolence, to question my compassion. If I weren't so offended, I'd laugh in your face."
Grey drew himself to his full height, staring hard at Soffen. "We waste time arguing female, and in the meantime the badger suffers. You're a Healer and your sworn duty is to help those in need. Are you turning your back on your responsibilities?"
Soffen studied the old boar for a moment, the angry glint in her eyes subsiding a little as she realised she had a lever. A slight advantage that may save her cub. "If I come with you, Grey, I want your sworn word that you'll delay telling the Council about my cub." Holding up a paw to forestall any objections, she pushed on. "Just two moons. That's all I ask. Two moons. Do you agree?"
Grey hesitated. Being a Custodian, his word bound him. There would be no going back if he agreed. Seeing little harm in the Healer's request, he nodded. "Very well, get yourself ready."
*
The journey back to the Teller was slow and dangerous, the storm constantly lashing them with rain and winds. Soffen was near the end of her strength when Grey finally stopped.
He pointed to a slight hollow in the ground. "I left him there."
"Well, he's not there now. Are you sure this is the place?"
Grey nodded, looking about for signs of the missing badger. Stumbling off the path, he scouted out the wet foliage. Soffen heard a shout. "Over here. Quickly, I've found him."
Hurrying to Grey's side, Soffen spotted a badger lying under the ferns, his fur streaked with mud, sodden from the heavy downpour. Pushing Grey aside, she examined the unconscious boar, poking and prodding him until satisfied she knew what was wrong. He had a nasty wound on his leg; the skin blackened and hard. Although she'd never seen such an injury, she'd heard about them; a burn caused by contact with fire. Along with the burn he had many cuts and bruises, but most were superficial. More serious was the fact he was in deep shock. Soffen knew he might die if she didn't get him back to her burrow, where she could treat him properly.
Leaning close to Grey, she shouted above the roaring wind. "He's in a pretty bad way. We have to get him back to my burrow. There's a nasty wound on his leg and he's suffering from shock. Watch him, I won't be long."
When Soffen reappeared, she carried a piece of fungus and a strange root between her teeth. Telling Grey to hold the boar's mouth open, she quickly chewed the root, letting the juices to flow from her mouth to his. It was a slow process, but she persevered until the last drop. Then she set about treating the burn on the Teller's leg with the fungus she'd gathered. Satisfied she could do no more, she tilted her head, studying the unconscious badger intently, a puzzled expression lining her snout.
"What have you given him, Soffen?"
"A special root. It's very potent. Hopefully, it will stimulate him enough to make the journey back.
"It'll make him better?" Grey prodded at the remnants Soffen had spat onto the forest floor.
"No, but it should help us get him back to my burrow. I can treat him properly once we're there."
Grey looked up into the storm, and the black turbulent clouds above them. "It's a long way." 
Soffen smiled. "Don't worry about the storm, it won't harm us now."
Brock moaned, his eyes flicking open. He looked about in confusion, his gaze settling on Soffen. She stroked his head. "Come on badger, that's it. We can't stay here. You've got to get up now. Come on." Slowly, she coaxed him to his feet. He was unsteady, so she moved closer, supporting him. "Slowly now, there's no hurry."
As the anodyne circulating through the Teller's body took full effect, a wave of vigour swept over him, easing the aches and pains. Shaking the water from his fur, Brock laughed loudly, tossing his head back and forth.
Grey gave Soffen a worried look. "What's he doing? What's going on?"
She smiled confidently. "Don't worry, it's just the effects of the root I've given him. Come on, let's get him back to the burrow before it wears off."
The trio staggered along the slippery path, Soffen's thoughts in a whirl. Ever since the stranger regained consciousness, she'd felt they had met somewhere before, but knew that hadn't happened.

Chapter 4

Grey's gaze wandered back to the cubs. One looked normal, its coat already changing from the early silver-grey of a newborn to the dull brownish-yellow of a youngster. It would take some time yet for the darker blue-grey coat and the black cheek stripes to develop, marking its passage into adulthood.
Grey flicked his gaze to the other cub, turning it over onto its back for a closer inspection. It wriggled, giving a high-pitched whicker, paddling its feet in the air. He studied the white coat intently, then turned his attention to the unnatural pink colouration of the cub's nose and eyes. It was an abomination! Grey had heard of such cubs. The stuff of tales and warnings given to young badgers who did not behave, but he'd never had the misfortune to see one.
Watching the tiny creature squirming on its back, Grey felt affronted, a flicker of unease running along his spine. Unsheathing his claws, he placed one on the tightly rounded belly. A smile touched his lips. It would be so easy to correct this filth. One quick slash would restore the balance. Grey reluctantly turned away, shaking his head at the Healer's actions. What was she thinking of? Whatever, he'd given his word and could do nothing about it for now, but in a few cycles…
Soffen's return interrupted his thoughts. "Is everything alright, Grey?" she asked, as she entered the small chamber in a bustle. Not waiting for an answer, she crossed to her cubs, smiling down at them. "I've treated Brock's wounds and fed him a grouse egg and a few acorns. He'll probably sleep for some time now, until the effects of the Henbane I gave him wear off."
Grey chuckled. "I thought he was going mad out there in the forest." He cocked his head at the entrance tunnel. "Did you see him trying to climb that tree?" Another chuckle, but less prolonged, bitten off with a short bark as a touch of scorn slipped into his voice. "Flying indeed! Who ever heard of such a ridiculous thing?"
Soffen turned from her cubs, her eyes widening. "The root I gave him alters the way we feel things. It's like having a dream where you see and hear things that aren't there." The old badger almost missed her next words, leaning forward to catch them. "I tried it once." Shaking her head at the memory, Soffen continued in a subdued voice, "It was very frightening." She looked away self-consciously, as the bare patch just above her nose turned bright pink. "You know how it feels when you finally corner that adder you've been hunting?"
"When it turns, ready to strike, you mean?"
"Yes, that's it." She paused, gathering her thoughts. "Well, that's the sort of feeling I had when I ate the root, a feeling of exuberance and strength. Total power, but an uneasy awareness of how frail we really are." She hesitated again, staring at the roof of the chamber, beyond such confines in her mind's eye now, out amongst the forest canopy. "I've always thought it must be like how the kestrel feels when she swoops down to make her kill." Dropping her gaze, Soffen stared at the damp floor. "Or perhaps the acorn as it falls to the ground, knowing it will eventually grow tall enough to touch the moon."
Grey shifted uncomfortably, breaking the mood. "That's all very well," he said, nodding at the sleeping cubs, "but let's talk about them. You've forced me to keep your secret for the time being, and I had no choice because I needed your help. But I want you to know that you've put me in a very awkward position with the other Custodians. The sett's power is built on trust and you made me break that. By Homer sow, it doesn't sit easily with me."
Soffen frowned, studying the old Custodian closely, unsure whether the creases furrowing his snout were anger or frustration. "And the other Custodians, do they share your touching preoccupation with trust?"
Grey's eyes narrowed. "And what exactly is that supposed to mean?"
"You know very well, Grey. The Custodians have been abusing their powers for many seasons now." Her stubby tail flicked angrily. "Why, only this winter, Harbrock used his position to get his brother moved to a better sleeping chamber."
"That was a special case."
She barked a short laugh. "Yes, just like all the other special cases." There could be no mistaking the contempt in her voice.
"Enough!"
Grey's retort carried an edge of anger, the hackles rising along his back. Soffen realised she may have pushed him too far. Swinging his head towards her, the old badger growled threateningly, his snout wrinkling in agitation. "You're on hazardous ground, sow. That really is quite enough."
Carefully avoiding eye contact, Soffen went to Grey, dabbing him on the flank. "You're a good badger, Grey, and I respect you for that. But sometimes you're too trusting for your own good." Holding up a paw to forestall any protest, she moved away, then turned back to face him, a sudden determination surging through her. "I have something I must do now, away from here. It'll take some time. Will you look after my cub while I'm gone?"
Grey's anger subsided, and he nodded in sullen agreement. "I can hardly leave them here to fend for themselves, can I?" He surreptitiously studied the small white creature asleep on the bed of leaves, flexing his claws slightly. As much as I'd like to, he thought.
Soffen picked up the object of Grey's scorn by its scruff, making ready to leave the sett.
"But surely you will not risk your cub's life in this terrible storm?" Grey objected, missing the irony of his statement.
Seeing the old Custodian's concern, Soffen put her cub down, answering him slowly, her voice carrying a conviction that surprised both of them. "No Grey, the storm won't harm him." Gazing down at the wriggling youngster with a tenderness that belied the emotions raging in her mind, she smiled. "When he dies, it will be at a time of his own choosing. Not yours, not mine, not the Council's."
With these words still ringing in the chamber, Soffen picked her cub up again and padded out into the storm, leaving Grey to reflect on her words.
*
Grey sat at the entrance to Soffen's burrow for a long time after she'd left, allowing her after-image to fade from his mind. He realised the Healer was a fine-looking badger, even though her coat was lighter than usual. The thought came as a surprise because, like others, he shunned the Healer, only acknowledging her existence when he needed her help for some mishap or other. He smiled, recalling the time — last winter, was it — when he'd gone to her with a sore foot?
Grey was helping block the side tunnels of the sett with dried grass — an early duty undertaken to keep out the winter's raw winds — when a vicious thorn buried itself deeply between the pads of his foot. No matter how hard he tried, he couldn't dislodge it. After much probing and nibbling, he could stand the pain no longer, so reluctantly visited the Healer. She welcomed him warmly, openly, chatting about the things happening around the sett. She led him to a comfortable bed of bracken, enquiring what the problem was. For all the years he was her senior, she sounded like his mother, tutting softly beneath her breath as she went about her work. She gently probed his foot, removing the thorn, treating the wound with a soothing paste made from crushed Hemlock leaves.
Soffen asked Grey to stay awhile, and the pair talked for a long time, just as old friends might. Grey had been grateful for her help, and as he hobbled away up the entrance tunnel, he turned back to face her. "I'll bring something for you, as a thank-you for what you've done," he promised.
But when the pain subsided, so did his gratitude, the 'thank-you' forgotten.
*
Because Soffen used the powers of The Way in her healing, Grey, like most badgers in Brockenhurst Sett, felt uneasy around her. The Council discouraged magic, and it was only because the Healer was so skilled it allowed her such latitude. Pushing the disquieting thoughts aside, Grey returned to the sleeping chamber, looking about for something to do. Soffen's unexplained departure made him edgy. Picking up a stray leaf, he dropped it onto a pile already neatly stacked in one corner, then sat back on his haunches, sighing.
Even though the burrow was obviously a temporary one, Soffen kept it tidy, unlike his own, which was always in a mess. He could see the Healer had done her best to make the burrow comfortable, working the packed earthen floor with deep grooves to draw off any water percolating into the sett. The walls themselves had strange patterns scratched into their surfaces, a reminder that this was the burrow of a Healer. Grey looked away, turning his back on the carvings, exploring instead, the two short tunnels leading off the main one.
One, lined with leaves and dried grasses, contained the sleeping form of the stranger, Brock. Soffen's remaining cub snuggled between his forefeet. Grey's turned to the other tunnel, filled with herbs and strange plants he couldn't identify. He wrinkled his snout as the different fragrances caught his attention. He wandered over, absent-mindedly poking at the collection.
The cub mewled in its sleep, attracting Grey's attention. He wandered back, studying it. Whoever had sired these cubs was keeping silent, and no surprise. Who in their right mind would confess to mating with a Healer? The surprise was the Healer's attitude. He could make no sense of it. Why hadn't she followed the mores of the sett? And what was all this about destiny? The cub mewled again, interrupting his thoughts. Not wanting to disturb the sleeping badgers further, he left the cramped chamber. He would lie in the entrance tunnel and wait for the Healer's return.
The wind howled across the narrow opening, echoing down the tunnel with an undulating groan that set Grey's teeth on edge. Making himself comfortable, he lay in the entrance, half dozing, unaware of the lashing rain and howling winds blowing small bushes and shrubs through the falling sheets of water.
Grey's thoughts turned to where the Healer might have taken her cub. Perhaps she'd killed it? He considered the idea at length. Yes, it made sense. She'd come to her senses and had taken the cub out to kill it.
*
Soffen made excellent progress through the storm and now stood on the higher reaches of Fire Rock. With her cub dangling limply from her mouth, she looked for the best assent. Her feelings were in turmoil. The certainty that had driven her so far waned, so too her confidence that the storm was her ally. She felt small, alone and terrified.
During the scramble over the slippery slopes forming the lower regions of Fire Rock, darkness had fallen. A cold moon mottled the landscape, picking out the pathway ahead with bold shadows, causing foreboding phantoms, which adding to her unease. Reaching the upper slopes, another hazard awaited. Cascading water from the higher escarpments made the going treacherous. It forced her to make many detours, pushing herself to the limit, aware that time was running out. If she was late in reaching her goal —. Soffen quickly discarded the thought. That outcome was far too alarming to contemplate. The higher she climbed, the louder the thunder became, mounting in intensity until its echoes crashed and pounded through her head. She struggled on, clawing her way up the slippery slope, driven upwards by a force that she only half-understood.
Soffen finally staggered onto the summit of Fire Rock, collapsing onto the hard surface in a heap. Painfully finding her feet, she carefully picked up her small, sodden cub. Reeling her way out across the plateau, she ducked as another peal of thunder crashed directly overhead. Squinting her eyes against the harsh lightning now constantly searing the top of the mountain range, she carefully lay her cub at the very centre of the ancient rock.
Struggling to keep her feet in the buffeting wind, she pulled a cord of twisted grasses from around her neck, examining the lodestone threaded onto it. Her father had given it to her, just before his death. It was a powerful and dangerous device; one of the keys to the Dark Healing. Holding it always brought back bitter-sweet memories of her father. Turning it over, she recalled the time she'd listened in rapt fascination as he'd explained its magical powers.
The lodestone sparked so brightly when he'd struck it against another stone, a miniature version of the sheet lightning cascading about her right now. Soffen had watched in awe when he displayed how the lodestone always turned to face the same direction when floated on a piece of bark in water. Now, other than dim memories, the loadstone was her only link with her dead father; the last of the powerful tools he had used during his years as a Healer.
Rolling her cub onto its back, Soffen placed the lodestone between his tiny paws, flinching as another clap of thunder crashed over the plateau, shaking the ground beneath her feet. The loud, rolling rumbles swept overhead, tossing surges of bright light from sky to earth with an eye-stinging brightness. Satisfied, she forced her weary way back to the rim of the plateau and lay huddled in the downpour, anxiously waiting for the Dark Healing to work its magic.
Nothing happened for some time, and she began to doubt she had the strength to finish what she'd begun. It came so quickly she almost missed it. A jagged brightness hurtled from the clouds, engulfing the lodestone and her precious cub. A fierce blue-white light, crackling and dancing over the tiny juddering body. Even from where she lay, at the very edge of the plateau, she could feel the enormous surge of heat thrown out by the aura dancing over the plateau. Eyes wide with terror, Soffen screamed.
The storm ceased. Not slowly, as is usual with such tempests, or even intermittently, as is sometimes the case, but instantly. Fom rage to calm, violence to stillness, as though suddenly frightened by the enormity of what it had done on Fire Rock. Soffen's ears rang with the sudden, stunning silence that fell over the plateau.
As the clouds broke, and the moon washed the scene with bright light, Soffen trembled, too scared to move or think. She could only stare at the spot where a moment before the life force of the angry storm had caressed her cub.
Then, spurred on by a desperate need to know, Soffen ran, shuffling and unsteady at first, but rapidly gathering speed, until she was running flat out, streaking towards the smoking remains that had been her cub.

Chapter 5

Brock woke with a start. He lay on a soft bed of moss, a sleeping cub between his forefeet. Wrinkling his nose, he carefully withdrew his paws from beneath the small cub nestled on top of them and got up. Dismissing the remnants of the dream still lingering in his mind, a strange dream in which he'd been flying through a bright moonlit sky, he looked around.
The chamber was damp and cold, and he had no clue who the owner might be. The last thing he remembered was being in the forest, so how had he got here? Checking that the cub was still asleep, he headed for the surface, seeking some answers. Moving up the sloping entrance tunnel, he heard a storm raging outside. It raised memories of the old badger he'd met on the forest path and the sow who'd given him a horrible tasting potion, and the feeling of euphoric feeling that had followed. They all came flooding back in a rush, crowding in on him, a kaleidoscope of confusing emotions.
Rounding a corner in the tunnel, Brock saw the same old badger he'd met on the path. "You're awake then," the badger greeted him. "I was about to come down and check on you. Are you feeling better now?" Brock nodded, watching narrow-eyed, as the old badger cocked his head. "Can you hear that?" he asked.
Brock's ears twisted towards the entrance. "I can hear the storm," he answered.
Grey frowned "Perhaps I felt it rather than heard it, then. Didn't you hear anything at all?"
"Something," Brock acknowledged reluctantly, "Yes, perhaps something."
Grey nodded. "I'm sure it's got something to do with Soffen."
Brock tipped his head, studying the old badger. "You're the Custodian I met in the forest, aren't you?" Grey nodded. "It's Grey, isn't it? Yes, I remember now. But who's Soffen?"
Grey smiled. "Yes, I'm sorry, you probably don't remember her. Not surprising really, the state you were in. She's our Healer. She helped get you back here, then treated you. This is her burrow."
"Soffen is the female who gave me that strange tasting herb back in the forest?"
Grey barked a short laugh, his snout creasing with fine lines. "Yes, that's right. You remember then?"
A bolt of lightning tore through the dark sky, and they jumped. Brock blinked the after-image away, scenting the ozone on the air. They stared out into the forest, amazement widening their eyes. In the time it had taken the lightning to flicker and die, the storm had vanished, the only reminder, a muted split-splat of raindrops falling from leaf to leaf.
"But this is impossible!" Grey's voice was full of awe.
Brock followed Grey out into the calm air, looking about in amazement. "How can this be? A storm can't just stop this way. " Tipping back his head, he scented the air. It was full of strange aromas. "Do you think this has something to do with your Healer?"
Grey nodded slowly. "Yes, I'm sure it has."
"Where did she go?"
"I don't know. She just asked me to look after you and her cub, then went off out into the storm. That reminds me, I'd better go down and check if the cub's alright."
Once Grey had disappeared, Brock made his way out amongst the trees of the ancient forest. Raising on to his rear legs, he rested his forepaws on the trunk of an elm. Directing his thoughts into the tree's essence, he used the powers of The Way to seek a connection. He stood that way, without moving, for a long time, snout furrowed in concentration. Funnelling his energy into the tree, he moved from ring to ring, hunting through the elm's memories. And there, near the centre, he glimpsed fleetly, the forest's communal life force.
At first it was hesitant, disjointed, channelled as it was through the slender trunk, but it quickly became clearer. In the dim and distant adumbration, Brock finally detected the dying energies of the storm. This was no ordinary storm, linked as it was to The Way. The Prime Mover had fashioned it to fulfil a task as yet unknown.
Brock dropped to his feet, shrugging off the feeling of doom that unexpectedly enveloped him. He made his thoughtful way back to the burrow, wondering why the Healer's image still floated at the back of his mind.
Grey stopped playing with the cub when Brock entered the chamber. He looked a little embarrassed. "The cub is fine," he said, answering an unasked question. "Frightened by all the thunder, that's all."
Brock ignored Grey's remarks, stopping just inside the entrance as a sudden thought struck him. All the things that had been happening — the fire, the meeting with Grey, the peculiar storm, even his treatment by the Healer — were all bound, preordained and outside his control. He faced the old badger with a serious expression. "Grey, I'm sorry to have to ask this, but there's something private I have to do. Would you mind leaving me alone for a while?"
Giving Brock a thoughtful look, Grey nodded, then left the chamber. Out of sight, he slipped back to watch what the young badger was up to.
Once Grey had gone, Brock dropped into a light trance by regulating his breathing, as taught when a neophyte. Calming his thoughts, he used a special breathing technique to circulate air in and out of his lungs in one continuous motion, which saturated his blood with oxygen, allowing a rapid deepening of his trance.
Feeling the familiar light-headedness that preceded Union, Brock channelled his thoughts into the complex patterns necessary to enter the First Path of The Way. In his mind's eye, he joined his being with the Prime Mover, expanding his consciousness until She filled him with Her essence. Welcoming Her vastness, he immersed himself into Her wholeness, falling deeper into his trance, until he became one with the cosmos.
Entering the next path, Brock shook off his links with the physical world. His breathing faltered, almost ceasing altogether. Unmindful of his collapsed body trembling on the damp floor, beyond his control, he continued to travel the paths of The Way.
From his hiding place just outside the chamber entrance, Grey watched Brock collapse. Hurrying to the Teller's side, he saw the young boar was in a deep trance. He lent closer, fascinated by the strange way the young badger was breathing. Along with his fellow Custodians, Grey had spent many a long winter-cycle discussing this very phenomenon, but had never witnessed it. Taking advantage of this unique opportunity, he studied the trembling Teller closely, aware that the young badger's mind was roaming the legends and experiences that were Boddaert's continuum.
Reaching the stage known as Shar, where the mind is free from all physical sensations, existing only as pure thought, Brock tried to lock away his fear. The next step would cast him adrift into an apogee from which there would be no return, and his last tenuous link with the physical world would slip away. He let it come, entering a mindset where all events fused together into six paths, known as, Now.
Brock floated over the collective memories of his race, dipping his mind into the passing elements, as a badger might dip a grass-stem into a wasp's nest to extract the honey hidden there. Immersing himself deeply, he tried to locate a time-line, but the elements were a jumbled madness. This had never happened before.
He gathered strength to cross the threshold to the next path, but something blocked him, a shadow on the fringes of his consciousness. Slipping back to a lower path, he collected himself for another try. Tellers experienced such confusion when slipping from pathway to pathway during training, and many neophytes became disorientated, some so severely they never recovered. Many had likened the feeling to that of a spider riding a twirling sycamore seed in a summer storm.
Grey studied the unconscious Teller closely, searching for small clues that might help him understand the process at work. The Custodians had tried to uncover the techniques used by the Tellers many times in the past, believing such knowledge would give them better control over the destiny of Brockenhurst Sett. Grey was in a unique position to gain control of knowledge that would help him build his own power base. He leant closer, tension building in his chest.
Brock's eyes snapped open, targeted on Grey's. They drew the old boar into a deep pool of blackness, both fascinating and terrifying. The pupils of the Teller's eyes grew in size until they encompassed the whole of Grey's world. He fought to tear his gaze from the emptiness yawning before him, but couldn't. His breathing became more laboured, until he became dizzy, Shaking his head, he tried to make sense of the writhing ribbons of redness licking at the corners of his mind with a harsh hunger.
Grey unexpectedly fought for his sanity, beating at the tenuous images swirling within his brain. Jostling for attention, they sped around his thoughts with a frenzy that churned his stomach. Whispering seductive promises. They beckoned him nearer to the chasm, slipping him away from reality, merging him with their blackness. In those few moments, he relived parts of his life that he'd thought banished forever. Memories he'd no wish to reawaken; memories that should stay buried until his final meeting with the Prime Mover.
Suddenly contact ceased and Grey staggered back, rapidly blinking his eyes. Brock returned from his self-hypnosis, too disorientated to notice the Custodian's distress. He turned to Grey, a red tinged darkness still glazing his eyes. "I need to see the Council. At once," he growled.
*
Soffen reached the centre of the plateau, terrified at what she would find. She'd been wrong trying to evoke such a dark force; to place such faith in her dead father's powers. She'd paid the ultimate price: her cub's life.
Bright moonlight reflected from the smooth surface of the plateau, highlighting the sheer rock wall to the north. The jagged peak threw a dark shadow across the cold surface. Soffen squinted through the smoke-filled air, desperate to catch sight of her cub. The lodestone lay shattered in tiny fragments. Alongside them, a small body lay unmoving.
As the harsh reality bit into her churning stomach, an immense weight bore down on Soffen. A terrible trembling overcame her, tears began streaming down her snout. Then, to her utter astonishment, her cub moved, raising its head to mew at her.
Picking her cub up, Soffen gasped in delight as it squirmed in her mouth. Moving towards the edge of the plateau she examined it, and there, beneath the blackened fur, saw a lighter layer of soft silver-grey. Heart thumping, eyes full of tears, she reached out a trembling paw, touching the black nose, the black pads of the tiny feet. Blinking back her tears, she finally stared into the liquid-brown eyes.
Halfway along the tortuous path leading down from the high plateau, a tiredness suddenly overcame her. Taking shelter by a large rock, she rested, her cub snuggled between her forepaws. Even though she was weak and exhausted, she groomed her cub's new coat, sighing when it whickered and snuggled into her side. Humming a song that her mother had taught her long ago, she continued to comfort her cub with soft caresses and tender words.
"And what shall we call you, my little one, with those beautiful bold stripes?" A name popped into her mind, and she nodded. "Yes, Darkburst, that's it! Darkburst it shall be then."
Soffen was whole and content at last, unaware that she had started a chain of events that would shake the very foundations of Boddaert's Realm itself.

Chapter 6

"The Council will attend to business." The Custodian's booming voice floated out to Brock waiting in the antechamber.
Unable to hide his impatience, Brock paced back and forth while the badgers inside the Grand Chamber discussed the affairs of the sett. Wrinkling his snout in irritation, he calmed himself, realising he could do nothing to hurry the process taking place just a few steps away in the main chamber.
What sort of badgers were these to treat him in such a manner? Back home we would have made a visitor welcome, have offered some worms and a comfortable burrow in which to rest. Brock quickly pushed the thoughts aside, bringing as they did, too many painful memories. Ceasing his agitated pacing, he sat on his haunches and rehearsed what he was going to tell the Council when they finally summoned him. It was important to get this right.
After an interminable wait, came the words he was waiting to hear. "Custodians, a visitor to our sett is outside. He has asked permission to speak to the Council." Brock did not miss the note of contempt in the speaker's voice and wrinkled his snout in puzzlement. "He is a Teller of The Way from the far beyond our mountains."
The announcement caused a buzz of interest amongst the Custodians. Brock's heart beat faster when he realised he was about to address the Council; an undertaking that would intimidate even the bravest of badgers.
"Usher, fetch this Teller before us," the gravelly voice ordered.
A small badger appeared at Brock's side, urgently pulling at his coat. Taking a few deep breaths to calm himself, Brock followed the usher through the short tunnel leading into the Grand Chamber. Entering, he stumbled to a halt, not hearing the usher's urgent whispers to keep moving, overawed by the view.
The magnificent chamber was excavated beneath a gigantic oak tree. Its domed roof so high, it was lost in the darkness far above Brock's head. Countless roots entwined the walls, coiling and twisting through one another in such a complicated pattern they appeared alive. Carved along these roots were intricate patterns that he instantly recognised as ancient symbols of The Way.
As did all Tellers, Brock had memorised the fables and tales of Boddaert's Realm, and as he made his way across the vast chamber, the chronicle of the building of Brockenhurst Sett unexpectedly popped into his mind.
*
Boddaert, first and most powerful Keeper of The Way, and a group of Magi especially trained for the task, constructed the Grand Chamber
Boddaert used his exceptional powers to command the roots of The Chosen Tree to coil about each other until they became an impenetrable mass; a cradle for this most sacred of places, henceforth known as the Grand Chamber. Once completed, he ordered his Magi to carve the Eternal Symbols along each root, using claws sharpened on their master's Lodestone. They toiled non-stop during two moon cycles until the complicated patterns were complete. Then Boddaert sanctified the Grand Chamber with an incantation from the Ancient Rites.
Following the completion of the Grand Chamber, Boddaert oversaw the digging of Brockenhurst Sett, and the forest echoed with the frenzied activity of badgers constructing the deepest sett ever created. The living chambers of this colossal structure were warm and snug, ensuring freedom from the hard winter frosts. The interconnecting tunnels radiated outwards from the imposing Grand Chamber, ensuring a constant supply of fresh air reached even the remotest parts. At regular intervals along the outermost tunnels, internal latrines were dug, an unusual feature then and now.
When the work was complete, Boddaert took his Magi to the top of Fire Rock, and from this high plateau, overlooking Brockenhurst Forest, they undertook a ceremony to mark the beginning of Boddaert's Chronicle — a ceremony lasting five full moons. Many badgers died during this self-imposed fast, giving their lives willingly, knowing they were sacrificing themselves for the good of all, and that the Prime Mover would repay such dedication a thousand-fold.
Finally, at the height of the winter solstice, Boddaert cast his last spell, delving deeply into his knowledge of The Way. Standing tall, he coalesced with the natural order. There, at the very centre of the plateau, surrounded by his remaining Magi, the great badger threw back his head, his now sightless eyes searching the dark skies. Taking a deep breath he sang, and from his lips rose the beautiful sounds of Crom's Elegy for the Dead.
He sang for three moons, ignoring the pain racking his body; the thirst cracking his lips; the surrounding dead. He poured forth the complicated notes until, on the fourth moon, it rewarded his faith.
She appeared to him on a slim column of fire, undefined and insubstantial, growing in strength with every stanza of Her song. The fire that was Her essence pulsated and swirled with such intensity it stung the eyes of all who beheld Her. So fierce was Her being that even Boddaert's sightless eyes saw the mythical light. She thrust upwards from the smooth surface of the plateau, a shimmering energy that splintered into a myriad fragments against the low clouds. Lightning rent the boiling greyness with great splashes of bright light. Primeval forces flowed from Her deep cradle in the ground to Her high sett in the sky, and with them flowed Boddaert's spirit, leaving his body a cold, empty shell. Here began the Legend that foretold a new beginning born of the old; a new challenge that would break loose from the very heart of Fire Rock itself.
*
"Come nearer, badger!" The harsh voice dragged Brock back from his reflections. Surreptitiously studying his surroundings, he followed the usher's bobbing back across the open space.
At the far end of the Grand Chamber, the oak's taproot thrust downwards through the roof, covering a vast distance before ramming into the packed earthen floor. High above his head, Brock spotted an opening carved into the taproot from where the speaker addressed him. The boar carried an unmistakable air of authority. Glaring down, he beckoned Brock forward with an impatient gesture. The usher hustled him into position before the assembly. Brock's gaze traced the gnarled old taproot upwards until he was staring at the roof far above, overwhelmed by its sheer size.
The Preceptor spoke again from his high perch, and such was the structure of the Grand Chamber that every word was distinct. "Grey informs me you have demanded a hearing, Teller."
The curt manner offended Brock, but he ignored it, swallowing his nervousness. It came as a shock to realise he'd forgotten what he wanted to say. For many moons, he'd cajoled and pleaded with Grey to get him a hearing, and now here he stood, his mind a complete blank. Something buzzed at the back of his mind like an angry wasp, confusing his thoughts. Why was his attention wandering this way?
Shaking his head, he looked about, studying the Grand Chamber. It was a beautiful place, no badger could doubt that, but lacked the special spark that had been the life force of High Green. No, even with all its beauty, this place would never fill the terrible emptiness gnawing away inside him. The sadness of unfulfilled dreams, shattered hopes and lost loved ones.
"Teller, you demanded a hearing. You insisted you had something of import to tell us, yet you stand there like some tongue-tied cub!" The Preceptor's sigh of annoyance was audible to all in the chamber.
Brock stared up at the shadowy figure above him, struggling to order his thoughts. Biting back a sharp retort, he bowed his head. Using the ancient title, as Grey had advised, he answered. "Preceptor, I have journeyed here from High Green, my home sett. A terrible fire destroyed it. It lies… lay, across the Brockenhurst Mountains. We had no Council like yours, our sett being smaller but…"
The Preceptor's voice whipped down, thick with sarcasm. "Teller, we have already heard all this trivia from Custodian Grey, so I suggest you dispense with protocol and get on with it."
Surprised by the unexpected reprimand, Brock looked at Grey for support, but the old boar wrinkled his snout, glancing away uncomfortably. Brock swung his gaze back to the Preceptor, glaring up at him angrily.
"Well, Teller," the Preceptor prompted again. "We're waiting."
Narrowing his eyes, Brock took a deep breath. "I came here because I saw…" pausing, he gathered his courage, "a vision that…
Once more the Preceptor's voice lashed down, interrupting him. "Yes, we were told how you hid away like some half-wit coward while the rest of your sett perished." The pause was just long enough for the barb to bite home. "So perhaps you would be kind enough to explain why we should waste our time listening to tales of visions?"
Brock trembled, his anger welling up almost beyond control. The fur along his back rose in a ridge, and without thinking, he unsheathed his claws. Ignoring the murmurs this hostile act drew from the Custodians, he shouted back at the Preceptor, "How dare you address me in such a manner!"
A glint of satisfaction lit the Preceptor's eyes as he studied the Teller below. "Never raise your voice here, badger," he warned quietly. "Not even a Custodian has that privilege, let alone a badger such as you. When I speak, you listen. When I question, you answer. That and no more. Now wait outside while we discuss this matter."
Turning his back to dismiss Brock, The Preceptor disappeared into the interior of the taproot opening. The usher reappeared at Brock's side, nudging him urgently when he continued to stare open-mouthed at the empty chamber far above him. Fighting the temptation to brush the annoying badger aside, Brock gathered his dignity as best he could, and stalked from the Grand Chamber. Ignoring the usher's urgent whispers to wait within the antechamber, Brock made directly for the exit tunnel. With a mounting sense of frustration and anger, he burst from the sett, heading out into the bright moonlight. He needed to talk to Soffen.
*
Brock found Soffen in her special glade, hidden deep within the remotest part of Brockenhurst Forest. It was here that she came when she wanted to be alone. The sun was breaking, and he stood quietly amongst the tall bracken fronds watching her, only half-conscious of the nearby Redstarts and Hawfinches going about their business. He was close enough to hear her quiet sobs. Embarrassed by this unintentional intrusion, he turned to leave, disturbing a nesting Blackcap. The bird shrilled an angry warning as it flew into the trees on the far side of the clearing.
"Who's there?" Soffen's light voice asked.
Pushing the bracken aside, Brock stepped into view. "It's only me, Soffen. I'm sorry if I disturbed you."
She smiled shyly, sniffing back her tears. Then, wrinkling her snout in an attempt at light-heartedness, she cocked her head. "Were you spying on me, Brock?"
He felt the small patch of bare skin just above his nose grow hot, and wriggled uncomfortably under her stare. "I'm sorry, Soffen, I didn't mean to intrude on your privacy. I was just…" He faltered to a stop.
The Healer's gentle laugh echoed across the glade, and she dabbed his flank. "Why, you look so flustered," she taunted playfully. "I believe I've embarrassed you."
Brock nodded once, then sighing heavily, settled down beside her.
"What is it, Brock?"
"I've been to see the Council." His voice was flat, bitter.
Soffen nodded. "And they didn't listen to you." It was a statement, not a question.
Brock shrugged. "The Preceptor treated me with utter contempt. It was so humiliating." He glanced at her, noting the concern deep within her eyes. 
"You still don't understand, do you?" she berated him lightly. "The Preceptor and his Custodians are frightened of you." She tapped his temple lightly. "Up here, you carry our history. All the facts and happenings that make us what we are." Glancing away, she absentmindedly flicked her stubby tail, dislodging a foraging ant that had slipped through the coarse guard hairs to nip at her skin. "That knowledge is power," she whispered. "When you go to them with stories of death and rebirth, it's no surprise they're suspicious."
"I didn't mention rebirth," Brock protested.
Soffen wrinkled her snout. "But your vision did Brock. It described the start of a new cycle. What's that, if not rebirth?"
Brock glanced at the tall trees, uncertainty lining his snout, considering Soffen's statement. "Well, perhaps you're right," he conceded after a few moments.
"And what role do the Custodians have in this vision of yours?"
"I don't know."
"Exactly," Soffen said, as though Brock had made her point for her. She moved closer. "Look, Brock, the Custodians are unsettled. At present they control Brockenhurst Sett, and through that, all the other setts in Brockenhurst Valley. Something they've done for generations. They've worked hard to make this a safe place to live, and in return we've given them the power to rule over us. Now you come along, with your stories of death and destruction." Furrowing her snout, Soffen looked at him. "I'm sorry to say this Brock, but it's no wonder they don't want to hear what you have to say."
"But ignoring the facts won't change them," Brock protested. With a headshake, he quickly apologised. "I'm sorry, it's not your fault. I shouldn't be taking it out on you like this. It's just that every instinct tells me Brockenhurst Sett is in real danger."
"Have you explained your concerns to Grey?" Soffen asked.
Brock nodded as he answered. "Well partly, but I thought it would have more impact when he heard the whole thing at the Council Meeting." Barking a derisive laugh, he wrinkled his snout. "But they gave me no chance to explain. Instead, the Preceptor treated me like a two-moon cub."
Soffen slapped her paw on the ground, giving a grunt of satisfaction as she caught a beetle scuttling from beneath a nearby stone. Putting it in her mouth, she chewed for a time, lost in her thoughts.
Brock, reluctant to interrupt the Healer's private musings, watched the antics of two squirrels chasing one another up and down a nearby tree.
