When Soffen finally spoke, her voice was more assured. "You know Brock, Grey's not like the other Custodians. He cares deeply about Brockenhurst Sett, and if he really thought it threatened, I'm sure he'd do all in his power to help. We must make him realise the importance of your vision."
Brock poked aimlessly at the ground for a moment, the gentle breeze ruffling the guard hairs on his ears, wondering what else he could do to win the old Custodian over. He looked up, a determined glint in his eyes. "I must convince him somehow. I must make the Council see the danger."
Soffen shook her head impatiently. "Brock, why do you insist on involving the Council in this?"
"What else can I do? I can't do this on my own. I need the Council's help."
"But I can help you," she replied, touching him lightly to stop his protest. "No, hear me out. We're both practised in the art of The Way. You're a Teller, I'm a Healer. That's a powerful combination. Your vision hints that Boddaert's Magic can help protect Brockenhurst Sett. Well, who stands the best chance of finding it, us or the Council?" Soffen paused, studying Brock closely. "Think about it. It's like it brought us together for this very purpose. Can't you feel it? The affinity of our first meeting?"
Brock shook his head in confusion. "I don't know. It's not that simple."
Soffen grabbed his paw excitedly. "But of course it's that simple. Together we can do this. You know we can."
"No Soffen, I really don't think so. The Preceptor guards the Sacred Roots, and we need those to guide us to Boddaert's Magic. Without the Sacred Roots, we wouldn't stand a chance."
Soffen nodded in agreement. "But don't you see? That's where Grey comes in. He's got access to the Sacred Roots. He can get them for us."
Brock looked dubious. "Do you think Grey would do that?" Considering the possibility for a moment, Brock shook his head. "No, I don't think he would."
Soffen tilted her head, a distant look in her eyes. "You leave Grey to me."
"And what about your cubs? You can't just go off in search of Boddaert's Magic and leave them behind."
"For goodness' sake, Brock! They're more than old enough to come with us."
"It's not just that," he countered, placing a paw on her flank, pointing to the clearing in which they stood. "It's all this. If they discover we've taken the Sacred Roots, the Custodians would never allow us back. Could you live with that?"
Soffen exhaled deeply, gazing at the familiar trees. "And what has life to offer me here? I'm a Healer. Few badgers will talk to me, and I've lost the only friend I ever really had." She shivered in the fading moonlight, staring up at the stars with bright, unfocussed eyes, remembering Raffen's laughter as they'd collected plants in the forest — memories best forgotten. "You told me once that your sett differed from this. That badgers there didn't shun each other just because one was a Healer, or a Teller of The Way. Well, that's what I want for my cubs. Friendship and companionship, and perhaps someone to share my life with."
As Soffen lapsed into silence, Brock shifted uncomfortably. It was some time before Soffen spoke again, but when she did, her voice held a wistful note. "There must be another sett out there somewhere," she whispered softly, "where badgers live together with tolerance and understanding. Help me find a sett like that, Brock, and I'll help you find Boddaert's Magic."
Seeing the tears suffusing Soffen's eyes, Brock moved closer, trying to comfort her, patting ineffectually at her flank. Soffen finally managed a self-conscious half smile. "I'm all right," she said.
Brock nuzzled gently at her neck. "Come on, let's get back to your sett and find some worms. If we're going to invite Grey over, we'll need plenty of those. You know what a greedy old badger he is." They laughed in unison, breaking the black mood that had enveloped them.
As Soffen followed Brock's broad back on the path, she deliberately trod in his footsteps, trying to come to terms with the feelings that were welling up inside her. Feelings that centred more and more around the badger ambling along in front of her.

Chapter 7

Grindel tapped his claws on the stone floor, frustrated at being kept waiting so long. Glancing at the sweating rock walls, he shivered, ruffling his coat against the cold. No matter how many times Skelda summoned him, he was always unprepared for the sombre experience of this dreadful place. Coughing quietly, he wrinkled his snout against the foul smells. Settling down to wait, he passed the time going over what he would say, determined that, this time would be different. When finally admitted to the inner chamber, there would be no fawning or deferential adulation, no flattery or false praises. This time he would be in control.
Grindle glanced about the filthy charnel house, bile rising in his throat. Unsuccessfully, he tried to ignore the heaps of bones and rotting carcasses laying in the dark corners. Black liquid oozed from one pile of putrefying flesh, running across the floor to collect in a dark pool, busily attended by carrion beetles. Eyes widening, he studied the familiar shape tossed carelessly on top of the sickening mass. The black and white stripes were plainly visible through a thick coating of congealed blood. Stumbling forward, repelled and fascinated, he tentatively reached out a trembling paw towards the severed head. Raffen? Could this be Raffen?
"Grindel!"
Grindel's name rebounded from the dank walls. He froze, paw still outstretched.
"Come here, badger."
Turning away from his grisly discovery, Grindel hastily entered the inner chamber, all thoughts of rebellion vanishing once he stood before the bent and twisted old figure dominating the small space. Lowering his snout, he touched it to the slime-coated floor in the expected gesture of subjugation.
"Have you carried out my instructions?" The voice was harsh and gritty.
Keeping his gaze on the floor, Grindel nodded. "Yes, Skelda. I gave the Teller no chance to speak. He became disorientated, as you said he would."
The gnarled head bobbed slowly. "Good. That's good. And what was his reaction?"
Grindel studied the misshapen badger surreptitiously, not daring to look directly at him, but ever watchful for signs of approval. "He left the chamber in confusion. He appeared upset."
"And where is he now?"
"With the Healer. The one called Soffen." A brief pause, followed by, "But…" Skelda raised his snout slightly, giving Grindel permission to continue. Grindel took a breath before plunging on, "I was wondering how you did that at such a distance."
The distorted head bobbed again. "The Dark Healing works well under my command, Preceptor. You would do well to remember that."
The gaunt, twisted figure studying Grindel with such intensity, carried about it the smell of death. Patches of discoloured skin were visible through the dull, sparse coat. A deformed spine made movement more a shuffle than a walk, and a cancerous growth, glistening in the dim light, covered most of the head. The boar's one seeing eye stared with such obvious ill humour, it terrified those unlucky enough to attract his attention. No matter how hard he tried, Grindel could not bring himself to think of this creature as anything other than pure evil.
"Even as we speak," the gruff voice continued, "the Teller and Healer are planning a journey to find Boddaert's Magic. To undertake such a trip, they'll want access to the Sacred Roots."
While in no position to question this statement, Grindel didn't doubt its validity. The badger facing him had proved repeatedly his access to powerful magic.
Skelda smiled. Twisted his features into an even more grotesque mask. "They'll enlist Grey's help to get the Sacred Roots. He will be the one who betrays us."
"But he would never do that." Grindel immediately lowered his gaze, realising the terrible mistake he'd made. Bitter experience had taught him Skelda brooked no contradiction.
Moving with astonishing speed, the deformed badger pushed a claw deep into the Preceptor's ear, twisting it savagely. Grindel, overwhelmed by pain, dropped to the floor. He begged Skelda to stop the sadistic attack. His screams echoed off the walls, and he could do little more than find some small corner of his mind in which to escape the torment. As suddenly as it had started, the pain stopped.
"Grindel," Skelda's voice dripped with the honeyed tones. "I believe I've warned you before about questioning my judgement?"
The Preceptor could only manage a hoarse whisper. "Yes."
"Then I trust you will not repeat it?"
"No, Skelda."
Skelda smiled, nodding benignly. "Good. Very good." Settling his bloated body into a more comfortable position, he stared hard at the fawning badger. "Now listen carefully, because I want no mistakes. Allow Grey access to the Sacred Roots, but do it in such a manner that it won't arouse his suspicion. Tell him you're going away on a trip or something. That should do it. Tell him you want him to take over your duties while you're gone." Skelda smiled again, his eyes blazing with inner excitement. "Once they have the Sacred Roots, they'll be able to begin their search."
"And when will that be?" Grindel asked sulkily, still favouring his injured ear.
"Use your head, idiot. They'll hardly leave just as winter is making ready to set in. They'll delay until spring brings new life to the forest."
The Preceptor lowered his head in respect. "Forgive me for being so stupid, Skelda. But why can't I just find out from the Teller what he so obviously wants to tell us and save all this subterfuge?"
Skelda studied the cringing Preceptor carefully. Was this badger really so stupid, or playing some game of his own? Had Grindel worked out it was impossible for him, caught as he was in a deformed body, to leave these dank tunnels? That, without Boddaert's Magic to make him whole, he'd be trapped here until he died? He shuddered at the thought of what might happen should the Preceptor ever gain control of Boddaert's Magic before he did.
Finally, curling his upper lip in contempt, he snapped, "You try my patience, badger!" The underlying threat was implicit in his tone.
"I'm sorry, Skelda," Grindel purred. "Forgive me. I'm but a simple badger, and like all simple creatures, I follow the most obvious path."
Skelda sighed impatiently. "If we allow the Teller to convince the Council that Brockenhurst Sett is in danger, they must help him. Should that happen, we'll have no chance of keeping the magic for ourselves. This way, he must get together a party of like-minded badgers to help him seek it out. Given half a chance, the Council will interfere, and neither of us want that."
"But why can't I go instead?"
"Because only one badger can survive direct contact with Boddaert's Magic, and that badger isn't you."
Grindel wrinkled his snout. "I see Skelda."
"I doubt that," the deformed old boar snapped back. "Go on. Get out!" Grindel turned to leave. "No wait, there's something I want you to do."
After receiving his instructions, Grindel backed from the inner chamber, heaving a silent sigh of relief to have survived yet another meeting with Skelda. Each time the meetings were harder to take. Pushing aside such thoughts, he headed for his sleeping chambers to plan his next move. The move that would put him in possession of Boddaert's Magic.
*
Grindel backed out of the chamber, and Skelda's features relaxed into something that might have been a smile. On such a deformed countenance, it was hard to tell. Scratching at a suppurating patch of bare skin near his tail, he grunted softly. Not because the wound hurt, that had stopped long ago, but because every new malaise only reminded him of how little time it left. Leaving the chamber, he made his way along tunnels known only to him. He mumbled softly to himself, a habit that was growing more frequent of late. He barked a short laugh, recalling Grindel's past attempts at trying to outwit him. The Preceptor would never accomplish that. "Not so long as I'm alive, my wily friend. Not so long as I'm alive."
Entering his sleeping chamber, Skelda exhaled, glad to be out of the oppressive tunnels. The walls were too straight, the floors too smooth, the unnatural smell offensive. Settling himself down on a bed of moss, he dismissed the tunnels, turning his mind to the future. A future where he would run through the tunnels like a young badger; a future when Boddaert's Magic would return his failing body to the youthful and vigorous thing it had once been.
As Skelda dreamt of his future, savouring his dominion over all badgers, the sun slid behind the horizon, bringing the moon's dark shroud across Brockenhurst Forest. The falling temperature stirred badgers in their warm chambers into readying themselves for the moon's foraging.
*
Over the following moons, the darkness lengthened and chill winds turned the last of the heather brown. Throughout the sett, badgers hurried about their business, fattening themselves for harsher times ahead. Mists gathered between the trees, swirling about with inquisitive fingers that touched every surface. The first snowflake hit the ground, disappearing before any badger saw its descent. Shortly the air filled with drifting flakes, covering the dormant shrubs, branches and tree trunks. Trees donned their frosty mantle and the coldest season cupped Brockenhurst Valley in its chilly embrace. Snow turned the sun's cycle into white swathes, the moon's cycle into reflecting points of sparkling light. It was time to stuff the entrance tunnels with grass and retire until the warm cycle returned.

Chapter 8

The winter was harsh and cold, with most badgers semi-dormant in their snug sleeping chambers. During the prolonged cold period the sett took on its usual familiar smells, brought on by the blocked entrances and fermenting leaves. The musty scent spread through the tunnels and chambers, making them a secure and pleasant place to be. The occasional throaty purr of a mating adult, or the deep warning growl of an aggressive encounter echoed through the tunnels, but mostly the sett settled into the quiet, slow rhythm of winter.
Everywhere life slowed, taking on a less hurried tempo, keeping pace with the growing icicles; long teardrops hanging from bare-limbed trees. Deep within Brockenhurst Forest, the Aro Brook wound its slow way through the trees, gurgling and muttering to itself when the ice encrusted banks widened to flow onto the flat plains of Low Meadow. And so winter passed, as had many winters before.
*
Spring was Grey's favourite season. A time when daffodils thrust aside dead leaves, splashing the dull-brown accumulation with vivid yellow reflections. A time of new growth, new life, new hope.
He stood now, just outside the sett entrance, taking a brief break from the chores of chasing out the rabbits, foxes and other small creatures that had taken advantage of the sett's warm interior during the winter-cycle. Breaking open a snail's shell, he nibbled the delicate flesh, pondering what had happened to Soffen and Brock during the long winter months.
During the harsh winter, Soffen's cubs had grown. Broshee, the image of her mother, had an impish manner, endearing her to everyone. Darkburst, who'd kept mostly to himself, appeared surly and moody. Both cubs had visited the sett frequently during the winter-cycle, Broshee making several new friends. Darkburst hadn't fared so well. The only friend he made was Grindel, The Preceptor. Their friendship became so close that Darkburst used the Preceptor's name, a rare privilege.
Grey scratched his snout, watching a large beetle scuttle its way under a nearby stone, then glanced up to study the piles of earth thrown up around the sett. His father always said the earth-works told the size of the sett below. From the proportions of the embankment fronting Brockenhurst Sett, the area it covered would impress any badger. Back in the upper tunnels, Grey could hear other badgers moving about. It was time he returned to his work. He sighed gently, settling into a more comfortable position. He would go shortly. First, he had some thinking to do, and there was always the question of that fat beetle.
During Soffen and Brock's only winter visit with Grey. The trio discussed Brock's vision at length, exploring it in every detail. Brock's interpretation was part fact, part revelation, so the conversation was stilted and difficult. Soffen accepted Brock's vision without hesitation, convinced that the events foretold would happen. Grey remained sceptical, finding such a catastrophe impossible to accept, especially as there were no hard facts. To him, it was inconceivable that Brockenhurst Sett could erupt into an expanding fireball, devouring all before it — that badgers would die horrible deaths, beating at flames that sprang into life on their fur. To him, Brock's vision was madness.
To help make his case, Brock dropped into a trance, using his powers to reach back through time and discover what history said about Boddaert's Magic. Recovering from his trance, he told them how, following the last spell cast by Boddaert, the surviving Magi had discovered their master's dead body. Frightened by the magical powers it still contained, they hid it deep within a crevasse on the Brockenhurst Plains.
The body lay for generations, until Evaert, twenty-third in line of succession, found it. This puissant badger, hopelessly lost to the forces of the Dark Healing, planned to use the powerful magic of Boddaert's remains to further his own ambitions. What followed was a dark period in badger history. With the power given him by the relic, he set out on a campaign of butchery and destruction, bent on conquering all of Boddaert's lands, until the intervention of Bawsen, a fabled fighter from Badachro, finally put an end to his tyranny.
After Evaert's defeat, Bawsen determined that such a thing would never happen again and assembled the first Custodians of The Way. He ordered them to form a Council, which he then instructed on the history of the badger's race, starting the first line of Tellers. Bawsen split Boddaert's remains into three parts — the Circle of Claws, the White Coat, and the Fire Soul — hiding them in separate places. The Fire Soul he buried beneath Fire Rock, but the White Coat and Circle of Claws he hid far from Brockenhurst Forest. Before he died, Bawsen carved the whereabouts of Boddaert's remains on the Sacred Roots, knowing that only a badger expert in using The Way could ever decipher the locations and unify Boddaert's body again.
Grey listened to Brock's account with intense concentration. He had heard the story before as a young badger, but it carried more weight coming from a Teller's lips. After Brock had finished, Grey wandered off on his own to ponder on what he'd heard.
In the end, after much consideration, the old Custodian returned and reluctantly agreed to join their search.
*
Once winter had eased its frigid grip on Brockenhurst Valley, Brock was keen to begin his search for Boddaert's Magic. The three conspirators, rightly cautious about their plans, met in a secluded glade.
While waiting for the others to arrive, Grey dug around in the earth for a bluebell bulb. Tutting at his failure, he dug up a grub instead. The sounds of the forest surrounded him. Rustling leaves; the shrill 'ke-wick' of a tawny owl; the steady tap of a wood-boring beetle searching for food. He revelled in the sounds, loving the forest with a passion deeper than mere feeling. It was an empathetic and intimate bonding with the Prime Mover that could find no expression in words.
He exhaled loudly. He'd spent a lot of time since Brock and Soffen's visit going over the arguments in his mind, unsure they were doing the right thing. They were asking him to gamble all this on a vision with no more substance than a cub's dream. If caught, they faced banishment from this wonderful place forever.
Soffen's greeting dragged Grey back to the present, and he carefully put the half-eaten grub to one side so he could finish it later.
"Look," he began as soon as Brock appeared, "I'm sorry if I'm less than enthusiastic about all this, but I've been thinking. I don't think Boddaert's Magic really exists, let alone that it's the answer to saving Brockenhurst Sett. I mean, how do I know your vision has any substance at all and isn't remorse?"
Brock glanced at Soffen, then back at Grey. "We discussed this the last time we met. I don't know for certain, I've admitted that. Visions aren't…" Casting about for the right words, he shrugged. "Well, a certainty." Gesturing, he frowned. "They're a mixture of fact and fiction, stories, fables, happenings and dreams. All coming together in a crux. Nether-the-less, they hold the kernel of truth. Even when I travel the paths of The Way, the truth remains elusive. You know this."
"You feel the vision to be genuine!" Grey responded with sarcasm. "And on that fallacious evidence, you expect me to chance everything. On the foundation of this fantasy, you expect me to throw away all the advantages I've built up over the seasons." The stinging retort hurt Brock, but he kept silent as Grey continued. "Toss it away on some search that will prove utterly futile?"
Soffen stepped between them, trying to defuse the growing tension. "Grey, the only way to save Brockenhurst Sett is to find Boddaert's Magic. Listen to Brock, he's a Teller of The Way. He knows."
Grey turned away. "Yes, he's a Teller alright, but that doesn't make him infallible."
Soffen tried to reason with the old Custodian. "Please Grey, listen to him. He's trying to help us."
Grey frowned. "So why involve me in this mad scheme of yours? If you already know what you have to do, do it and leave me out of it." Grey didn't miss the look that flashed between Brock and Soffen.
"Because the Legends only tell what happened to Boddaert's body, not where his remains are. We don't know where to search." Brock stared Grey straight in the eyes. "Those secrets lay on the Sacred Roots."
Grey shook his head, the rolls of fat down his flanks shimmering in response. "By Homer, Brock, no!. You ask that of me? I won't do that."
Soffen placed a paw on Grey's flank, gazing up at him. "We can't do this without you, Grey. We need your help. You're the only one who has access to the Sacred Roots."
Grey backed away. "I've already taken a significant risk on your behalf. Now you ask me to steal the Sacred Roots." His voice dropped to a whisper. "By Homer, if I do that, there'll be no future for me here, ever!"
Soffen stamped her foot. "And what future do you think there'll be for you if we don't stop Brock's vision from becoming reality? Tell me that badger!"
Brock's hard voice thrust between them. "And what would the Council say if they found out that a certain Custodian had kept information about a disfigured cub from them?" His eyes bored into Grey's. "How do you think they might react to that news?"
Grey glowered back at him. "You'd do that? After all the help I've given you? You'd really do that?"
Brock nodded slowly, glaring back at the Custodian intently. "If you forced me to, yes."
The old Custodian exhaled deeply, sitting back on his haunches. Sniffing the light breeze, he wrinkled his snout at the crisp scents. Spring had come, heralding new beginnings. Maybe this was such a new beginning. Feeling cheated, he shuddered, wondering if this would be the last time he'd see his beloved Brockenhurst Forest shake itself free of its winter mantle.

Chapter 9

"And this is the Grand Chamber where I oversee the Council Meetings." Darkburst heard the ring of pride in the Preceptor's voice as he paraded Brockenhurst Sett's seat of power.
They'd climbed the long sloping tunnel leading to the taproot chamber, talking animatedly as they went. Darkburst, a touch overawed at the prospect of seeing the legendary enclosure, stumbled to a stop at the edge of the opening, gazing out into the colossal space spread out below. Head slowly turning from side to side, he drank in every detail. The enormous expanse of floor still holding the Magi's teeth-marks, even after the generations of badgers who'd walked across its sanctified surface; the walls covered with deliciously delicate patterns; the vaulted ceiling disappearing above his head. Closing his eyes, he breathed deeply, imaging how it must feel addressing the Council from such a position of power.
The Preceptor stood beside Darkburst, pointing at the vast chamber below. "Wherever you stand down there, you can hear every word spoken from here. Such was the skill of Boddaert, even the quietest whisper will carry to the furthest corner."
Darkburst turned his back on the Grand Chamber, his gaze wandering over the taproot chamber walls. They were covered with innumerable small marks carved into the hard heartwood, the rich patterns dazzled his eyes with a confusion of interesting shapes. Staring at them, he felt dizzy.
"Come, stand here, Darkburst." The Preceptor beckoned the young badger to the very centre of the chamber. "Now, look carefully at the carvings on the wall over there." Grindel pointed at a tight-knit group of images. They flowed upwards from the floor, following the gently curving grain of the taproot. Darkburst stared at the carvings and his dizziness increased. "Concentrate now. Concentrate really hard. That's it, let your mind take in the carvings," Grindel whispered behind him.
Darkburst gasped when the carvings unexpectedly coalesced into a view of Brockenhurst Forest. He blinked in astonishment, and the view disappeared. "A vision," he whispered through dry lips. "I saw a vision of the forest."
The Preceptor chuckled in delight, nodding his head eagerly. "Legend has it that Boddaert himself carved these. They possess magical properties which produce illusions if you stare hard enough. Though try as I may, I've never seen them."
Darkburst's eyes widened. "But yes, that's exactly what happened. I saw a scene of Brockenhurst Forest."
Grindel's smile broadened. He winked. "Yes, I had an idea you might."
"But why? Why would I see something that you cannot?"
"Because you're the son of a Healer, with the power of The Way running in your blood. If it would work for any badger, it would work for you."
"Can I try again? Please?"
The Preceptor nodded. "Of course, youngster. Try a different carving. Look, that one over there, perhaps you'll see something different."
"Is that possible?"
"It's said each carving holds a different illusion. Though why that should be, I'm not sure."
Darkburst stood in the centre of the chamber, staring hard at the carvings, eyes narrowed in concentration, excitement tightening his chest. Even though he expected it, the illusion springing out made him gasp. He studied the small forest glade, quickly realising he'd seen it before. He'd played in this glade as a cub. To one side, the rotting tree stump where he'd so often hidden from his mother when there were chores to do. And there the tall elm he'd used to sharpen his claws, the long scratches still plainly visible in the bark.
Darkburst willed himself forward, moving further into the forest clearing, and even though he knew it was impossible, every sense told him he was walking on soft grass. Concentrating harder, he urged his body upwards. He rose into the air, above the canopy of Brockenhurst Forest, swooping and gliding like a buzzard, delighting in the wind's sensation against his face. He swept low over Fire Rock, heading towards the sparkling waters of Migaro Lake, where he chased shadows over the gentle swell of the water, skimming the surface. Turning back, he laughed loudly, diving back and forth over the forest pathways, totally immersed in the thrill of flight.
"Darkburst!" A muffled voice called from somewhere nearby. "Darkburst! Darkburst!" The voice held such urgency, it snapped him back. Vision swirling, Darkburst tried to hold on to his illusionary world, but it slipped away. The feeling of overwhelming loss crushed him.
The Preceptor stared at Darkburst, concern flaring in his eyes. "What happened? I couldn't wake you. You were in some sort of trance."
Darkburst laughed his delight, stumbling over his words. "It was so… so amazing." He paused, unable to describe what had just happened. "I flew above the trees, and down over the water." But the pathetic description fell far short of the ineffable journey he'd just undertaken.
"Well, that's strange." Grindel said, patting the young badger's flank. "But don't make too much of it. After all, it's only an illusion."
"But I flew like a bird," Darkburst cried excitedly, still caught up in the wonder of it all. "Over Fire Rock, to a lake far away. Its surface sparkled in the moonlight. I was there!"
The Preceptor closely studied the young badger. "You hallucinated. You just imagined you were flying." Grindel relaxed, barking a short laugh. "That's some imagination you have there, youngster." Pointing at the carvings, he continued, "But these are just a collection of clever illusions. Don't let your imagination over-rule your sense."
Darkburst worried at his lower lip, thinking furiously. He knew what had happened, and it was no illusion. The Preceptor was wrong. As unthinkable as that was, he was wrong! He had flown above the forest, even though his body was stationary in the taproot chamber. He knew it to be true, because during the flight he saw his mother and sister talking in the forest. Swooping low, he heard their words. It was no illusion. He'd been in two places at once. Lowering his gaze, he studied the floor. He needed time to think this through.
 "Well, perhaps you're right," he finally responded. "My mother's always telling me I've got an over-active imagination."
The Preceptor smiled and nodded. "Tell me something, Darkburst. How would you like to be Preceptor?"
"Me? Preceptor?" Darkburst could hardly speak at the thought. Too much was happening too quickly.
Grindel stared hard at the young badger, as though seeking some clue. "I could make it happen, you know. Come on, what do you say? Would you like to be Preceptor?"
"Yes, of course I would. Who wouldn't?" The question threw Darkburst. "But me? Preceptor?"
"You'd have to become a Custodian first, but I could arrange that easily."
"Why would…" The young badger stopped, staring at the Preceptor with a new understanding. "You're leaving, aren't you? You're going away somewhere."
Grindel smiled, a tight self-satisfied smile. Shaking his head, he replied, "No, I'm not going anywhere. I have other plans to pursue. Plans that leave no room for the responsibilities of being Preceptor."
"But I've no experience. Besides, there's no opening for a Custodian on the Council."
A smile flickered across Grindel's lips as he settled his gaze on some distant point visible only to him. "Oh, I think there'll be an opening for you before too long, Darkburst."
"And you would train me?" Darkburst asked, wrinkling his snout in excitement, sensing the power he was being offered. But then another doubt crept into his mind. "Won't the other Custodians object? Surely one of them will expect to take over from you?"
"It's traditional for the Preceptor to select his own replacement. The Custodians have no right of objection. It's up to me who I choose." Grindel tilted his head. "You know, from your objections, one could think you don't want to be Preceptor."
Darkburst shook his head, bemused at the stunning offer being made. "I really don't know what to say."
"Thank you, might be a good start," Grindel answered with a chuckle. "But before you fall over yourself with gratitude, I think I should warn you about something. There are certain conditions attached to my patronage." The Preceptor nodded at the uncertainty filling the young badger's eyes. "Oh, don't worry, it's nothing you'll find too objectionable."
Grindel beckoned Darkburst, leading him down onto the floor of the Grand Chamber. Standing at the very centre of the vast space, he studied the youngster with a serious expression. When he finally spoke, his voice was grave, and Darkburst had to lean very close to catch the words.
"Darkburst, your mother and the badger called Brock are about to embark on a journey. They're going on a quest and their search will take them far from Brockenhurst Valley. Your mother will want you and your sister to go too." He paused for a moment. "You must go with her. The journey will be long and arduous and very dangerous, and it's crucial you're there to protect her." He paused again, adding more weight to his next words. "The Teller, Brock. You can't trust him. He's a danger to your mother."
Darkburst fidgeted uncomfortably as the Preceptor's eyes pierced him with an intensity that made his head spin.
"He wants your mother dead!"
The bald statement shocked Darkburst, his breath catching in his throat. "What do you mean?".
"Exactly what I said. Don't repeat this conversation to anyone. Doing so will place your mother in great danger. Do you understand? Say nothing." Darkburst nodded, and Grindel relaxed. "Your mother is going to undertake a search for something very special. A dangerous treasure that has the power to destroy her and any badger who touches it. It's imperative you find this treasure first." Grindel's expression softened a little at Darkburst's apprehension. "Don't worry, you are under my protection, and will come to no harm. You will bring this treasure back here, where I will make it safe. Only I can do that. No other badger. If they try to, they'll die. Do you understand?" Darkburst nodded silently. "Good," Grindel said, "it will be your first step to becoming Preceptor."
"You want me to steal from my mother?" Darkburst asked in a tremulous voice.
Grindel shook his head. "Not steal, protect. I want you to protect her."
The young badger looked confused. "What is it? This thing that's so dangerous?"
"Don't concern yourself with that for now. When the time comes, you'll know. You'll need no telling."
Darkburst thought hard, going over all that Grindel had told him. The Preceptor saw the questions forming in the young boar's eyes, even before he asked them.
He moved closer, a grim expression creasing his snout. "Listen carefully," he growled, thrusting his face so close the young badger could smell the sour odour of his breath. "Under no circumstances are you to tell your mother that we have talked about this. Nothing you can say will stop her making this journey, it's pre-ordained, and forewarning her of its dangers will almost certainly lead to her death." Grindel stepped in front of the pacing youngster. "Now, I have things to attend to. So quickly, tell me. Will you do as I ask?" Darkburst nodded distractedly and Grindel smiled. "I think you're going to make an excellent Preceptor, Darkburst. You have a quick and adaptive mind. Now go to your mother and see she's protected."
As Darkburst turned to leave, Grindel called to him. "Here, take this." He handed the young badger a small piece of root threaded on a length of twisted grass. "It's a Talisman, for good luck. Keep it close to you at all times. It will help you protect your mother." The Preceptor watched Darkburst leave the Grand Chamber, pleased with the results of the meeting. Such a simple badger. So trusting. He chuckled quietly, recalling Darkburst's response to the carvings in the taproot chamber. What an imagination, though. Flying indeed!
Grindel, still chuckling when he left the Grand Chamber, was so engrossed with the image, he didn't see the dark figure skulking in the shadows of a side tunnel. The shadowy figure growled low in his throat, scratching at his suppurating tail as he watched Grindel disappear around a bend in the tunnel.
*
"But we need the Sacred Roots to know where to start our search," Brock argued heatedly.
Grey stared at him, his snout puckering. He leant forward. "It's all very well for you Brock, but you're not the one who has to steal them, are you?"
"But we can't afford to miss this opportunity. How often is a chance like this going to present itself? The Preceptor probably won't leave the sett again this season."
The old Custodian shook his head. "I know that, but I still don't like it."
Brock nodded his understanding. "But this is our only chance. We must take it."
"And what's the Preceptor going to do when he returns and discovers that I've stolen them?" Grey shot back angrily.
"Don't worry, we'll have them back in place long before he even knows they're missing. We only need them for a short time. Just to start us off."
Soffen nodded her agreement. "He's right, Grey. Brock will use them to find out where we need to search, and then you can put them back."
Brock smiled at Soffen, thankful for her support. "Have you told Broshee and Darkburst about the trip we're making?" he asked, effectively dismissing any further objections from Grey.
Shaking her head, Soffen returned his smile. "No, not yet. I almost told Broshee when we were in the forest earlier, but decided it would be better to wait until I had them both together." She sighed, looking around as though searching for something. "As usual, Darkburst has disappeared again. He really tries my patience."
Grey plucked a tick from his leg and examined it, cracking the hard insect with his teeth. "I think I saw him with the Preceptor earlier on." He smiled at the reaction his words produced.
Soffen looked at Brock with a frown, obviously ill at ease.
"What are you going to tell them about the trip, Soffen?" Brock asked.
"The truth. There's no point in lying. They'd find out soon enough, anyway."
Brock shrugged. "I wasn't expecting you to lie to them. I'm just concerned that the Custodians will hear about our plans and stop us before we have the chance to leave. The fewer badgers who know what we're up to, the better."
Grey wrinkled his snout. "You know, I really don't understand you, Brock. First you do everything in your power to inform the Custodians about your plans, then you're hiding everything from them." The old badger shook his head. "I hate all this subterfuge, I really do."
Brock flicked his tail. "As do I Grey, but my vision shows how to save the sett. Nothing must impede that."
"But why lie all the time?" Grey retaliated.
"Because the Preceptor would kill us, rather than let us gain control of Boddaert's Magic." Soffen's clear tones cut across the argument with a ring of authority. "There's no way he would allow any badger to gain such power. Think about it for a moment. Think of the power that the holder of Boddaert's Magic will have."
Grey's snout wrinkled as he considered her statement. Yes, perhaps the Healer was right. At the very least, any badger having the strength of Boddaert's Magic behind him was a force to reckon with.
"Hello, mother."
The group fell silent as Darkburst entered the chamber. Soffen smiled at her cub. "Hello Darkburst, and where have you been all this time? I've been looking for you."
"By the rookery mother, looking for fallen squabs. I thought I saw you there earlier with Broshee, talking by the nettle patch."
"Yes, you could have. We were there for a while. I was telling Broshee about a trip we're making."
Darkburst nodded to himself, as though her words confirmed something he already knew. "Yes, I overheard you." He looked uneasy at Soffen's sharp glance.
"I didn't see you," she replied, consternation clouding her face.
Darkburst looked away for a moment, but quickly recovered. "I was practising my stalking mother, that's why you didn't see me. I was hiding in the long grass, but I was only there for a moment."
Grey passed Darkburst a worm. "Your mother wants you to come on a trip with us, youngster. What do you think about that?"
"Where to?"
Soffen touched her cub's flank. "We're not sure exactly, but we might be away a long time. That's why I want you and your sister to come with us."
"As protector?" 
"What?" Grey's sharp eyes searched the young badger's face.
"Oh, nothing, nothing. I was just thinking aloud, that's all. So when are we leaving, mother?"
"Grey has one or two things to arrange first. So probably in two or three moons."
"I've got something that I must do too," Darkburst called over his shoulder as he turned away. "I won't be long."
Soffen stared after her cub, an uneasy feeling filling her chest.

Chapter 10

A thick evening mist swirled around the five badgers as they moved through the undergrowth, muting their voices. Brock gave occasional orders in a low growl, as though afraid the forest might overhear. The dew glistening on their fur, made them appear as phantoms gliding over the pathway in the moonlight. Brock led, followed by Darkburst, and close on their heels, Soffen and Broshee. Grey brought up the rear. They travelled fast, putting distance between themselves and Brockenhurst Sett before badgers noticed their absence.
Their immediate aim was to reach the Andith River and find a crossing before the sun pierced the darkness. Once there, they would feel safe enough to take a rest and plan their next move. They walked in silence, each lost in their own anxieties. All had doubts about the journey they were making, but none wanted to raise them. The only sounds, other than the sharp rustle of undergrowth being brushed aside, was the slap of a paw on stone, or the occasional cough.
Darkburst's thoughts returned to the small Talisman tucked beneath the fur on his neck. Grindel had given it to him to help protect his mother, but from what, he still didn't know. The adults hadn't discussed the journey, so he didn't know where they were heading. He'd examined the Talisman when Grindel first gave it to him, fascinated by the tiny marks covering its surface. They were so like the carvings on the taproot chamber walls.
Brock's thoughts were centred on a different puzzle; how to decipher the Sacred Roots and locate Boddaert's Magic hiding place. Having studied the roots when Grey first got them, Brock quickly admitted defeat, unable to make any sense of the miniature carvings running from tip to tip. It would take time to unravel the secrets hidden there, time they didn't have.
After much debate, Brock had persuaded the others that the only option was to take the Sacred Roots with them, in the hope they'd be able to return them before Grindel noticed their absence. Grey had protested violently, and Brock's nose twitched in vexation as he recalled the remarks the old badger had thrown at him. Fortunately, Soffen's diplomatic skills calmed things enough for them to form a plan of action.
Soffen caught up with Brock and walked in his footsteps, something she'd done as a cub when out with her father. It made her feel safe then, and it made her feel safe now. With each passing cycle, Soffen's feelings grew stronger for the badger, and she wondered if he felt the same. Unlike the others, Soffen's concerns centred more on her cubs than the journey — Darkburst, who, but for the Dark Healing, would now walk in the shadow of the Prime Mover, and Broshee, carefree Broshee, who wanted nothing more than to mate and raise cubs. Soffen smiled, quickening her pace to walk alongside Brock.
Of the five badgers walking the path that moon, Grey was the least happy. The long walk had given him time to reflect on the enormity of his actions. When they discovered the theft of the Sacred Roots, it would cost him his place as a Custodian, and probably his right to live in Brockenhurst Sett. By Homer, why had he allowed himself to become involved in this madness? Snout creasing with anxiety, he wondered how long it would be before the Preceptor discovered the theft of the Sacred Roots and sent out a search party. The Preceptor might even resurrect the ancient rite of Rock Piling, especially for him! Grinding his teeth in agitation, he contemplated his fate, his anger quickly building. He'd been weak to let the others take advantage of his tolerant nature. He should have reported them to the Council when they'd first suggested this scatterbrained scheme. A grim determination overcame him. It wasn't too late to save himself. He would slip away at the earliest opportunity, return the Sacred Roots to Brockenhurst Sett, and throw himself on the Preceptor's mercy. Satisfied he'd found a suitable solution, the old Custodian plodded along with a fresh spring in his step, and new hope in his heart.
As the small group made its way along the path, a skulking figure followed them. Hidden in the shadows of the thickening mist, Grindel watched the badgers leave the confines of Brockenhurst Forest. Satisfied they were well on their way, he turned back towards the sett, ready to report to Skelda. Flicking his tail, he tried to ignore the sour taste welling up in his mouth at the thought of having to meet the deformed old monster again.
*
Back in the Grand Chamber, Skelda did not need Grindel's report to know the search was well underway. He had his own method of following the group's progress. He'd only set Grindel following the group so the Preceptor wouldn't see him using the special carvings. Through that medium, and the Talisman carried by Darkburst, he saw all that happened in the locality of the young badger. He chuckled, happier than he'd been for some time. Chewing on a piece of rank flesh, pleased at his own cunning, he considered his solution. The ancient ones had viewed the forest without the aid of the Talisman, their powers being far more potent than his. The carvings alone would have been enough to see everything in the great forest and surrounding district. Luckily, the Talisman gave him a direct connection to the carvings. He hoped it would be a strong enough connection to cover the distances involved.
*
A keen breeze cleared the mist, and the sky filled with a myriad twinkling points of light. Brock allowed the group only one abrupt break for food before resuming the punishing pace. The path they travelled meandered through open countryside, and the moon shone down with an intensity seldom experienced beneath the canopy of Brockenhurst Forest.
Grey quickened his pace, drawing level with Brock. "How much further do you intend going before we stop?"
Brock halted, cocking his head. He smiled. "Hear that?" The others formed a circle around him, listening.
"It's running water, isn't it?" Broshee asked.
Brock nodded. "Yes, I think it's the Andith River. We need to cross it as soon as possible. I'd like to push on." Not waiting for their agreement, the Teller put his head down and set off again.
The sky lightened with the first streaks of dawn, as the tired badgers finally reached the source of the running water. Brock sighed his disappointment when they discovered it was not the Andith River, just a small tributary. Now exhausted, the group agreed to stop for food and a rest. Being so close to Brockenhurst Forest, Brock suggested they post a lookout, volunteering to take the first stint himself. Digging a small burrow under a fallen tree, the foot-sore band settled down to sleep.
Brock was glad of some time alone. It gave him a chance to examine the Sacred Roots undisturbed. He studied the enigmatic pieces of wood from every angle, even trying to use his knowledge of The Way to unlock their secrets. Finally, frustrated and angry at his failure, he sat back on his haunches, turning his thoughts to recent events. Maybe Grey was right, and the vision was the product of his own guilt. Tossing the Sacred Roots aside, he took a walk to clear his mind. Crossing the small stream, he wandered aimlessly up the gentle slope of the bank and stood on the brow.
From the high vantage point, Brock spotted the Andith River curving gently away in the valley below. Squinting for a better view, he frowned. Swollen by the spring rains, the river splashed froth and foam high into the air. It would be impossible to cross when in full spate like this. Turning aside, he headed back to the temporary burrow, responsibility hanging heavily on his mind.
Darkburst woke with a start, looking up at Brock with sleep-clouded eyes.
"Your turn to keep watch," Brock whispered, not wanting to wake the others. As soon as Darkburst crawled from his sleeping space, he flopped down in his place, curled into a tight ball and dropped asleep.
Rubbing his eyes, Darkburst made his way outside. The sun was high on the horizon, colouring the sky a brilliant red. Settling down with a collection of worms, beetles and grubs, he ate. The rising sun warmed his back as he savoured each bite. Contentedly crunching his way through the last of a beetle, he sucked the soft meat from its plump body, before casting the hard wing cases adrift. Using a nearby tree, he cleansed his claws with long sweeps. Turning from the tree, a glint caught his attention. Sunlight reflected from an object half-hidden in the grass. Moving closer, he squinted against the glare, a sudden fullness filling his chest when he spotted the Sacred Roots.
Reverently picking up the five pieces of ancient wood, Darkburst beamed, eyes widening when he saw the same carvings used in the taproot chamber. With mounting excitement, he willed the Sacred Roots into life, but they remained five pieces of inert wood.
Darkburst thought hard, studying the carvings on the Roots, comparing them to those on the Talisman Grindel had given him. Then he remembered the carvings in the Grand Chamber interconnected in a circular pattern, layered one on the other. With trembling paws, he arranged the Sacred Roots into different circular patterns, hoping the right combination would unlock their secret. He kept at the task; the sun rising higher and higher, all thoughts of waking his relief now forgotten. Time after time he rearranged the pieces into unique patterns with no success.
The sun was now high, and Darkburst at the end of his patience. Throwing the Sacred Roots on the ground, he turned away. A bright light flashed over his shoulder. He looked back, wrinkling his snout. Returning, he separated the roots, still seeing their previous pattern as an afterimage. Carefully pushing the roots back together, he gasped in delight when a bright point of light flickered between their ends. He repeated the pattern over and over until the bright light hurt his eyes. Closing them, he sat quietly, letting his sight recover.
Ready to try again he extended a claw, but hesitated, breath faltering. He lent closer, carefully counting the Roots. Shaking his head, he counted again. How could that be? There were eight pieces; before there were five. He counted them again; eight. A thought nagged at the back of his mind. Could it be that simple?
Holding his breath, Darkburst carefully arranged the roots, so the ends touched each other in the shape of an eight-pointed star. As the last root slipped into place, a searing light exploded upwards. He staggered backwards, rapidly blinking his eyes, standing transfixed before a swirling multi-coloured layer of light. Spinning into itself, it became a sphere, inside which flickered a landscape. The sphere span faster, until deep within the bluest of blue, the moon-swept landscape solidified. The panoramic view was a large flat meadow, its smooth grass undulating away to the horizon, drawing his gaze with it. And there, outshining the icy moon where the dark sky met the darker ground, were the brightest stars he'd ever seen. Trapped between low clouds and the ground, they moved across the horizon at an astonishing speed. Almost too fast for the eye to follow, they streamed along in an unending line, slashing a white swath across the landscape.
Here was something frightening and far beyond his comprehension, but never-the-less exciting. Forcing his attention away from the strange stars, Darkburst let his gaze encompass the large lake nestled in a low hollow. Its source was a meandering river stretching across the landscape as far as the eye could see. His heart leaped when he realised it must be the Andith River.
"What are you doing?"
The unexpected question made Darkburst jumped, his paw knocking the Sacred Roots apart. The ball of light collapsed. Darkburst glowered at Grey. His heart pounded so hard, speech was impossible.
"What are you doing?" Grey repeated.
"I was watching the stars."
"Watching the stars? What stars, the sky is cloudy, I don't understand."
Darkburst nodded. "No, I don't suppose you do. Here, let me show you." Leaning forward, he went to rearrange the Sacred Roots into the star pattern. Picking up the first one, his blood ran cold. The Sacred Roots were burnt beyond recognition. He gulped, looking up at Grey in a panic.
"What's wrong?" Grey demanded.
"What's happening?" Broshee called, emerging from the burrow.
"Broshee, get mother and Brock!" Darkburst shouted at her.
"What?" The young sow stretched and yawned, sleep still clogging her eyes.
"I said get mother. NOW!"
Broshee's eyes widened. "Well, there's no need to be so rude about it," she shouted back.
"What's the matter with you, youngster?" Grey scolded Darkburst. "Why are you taking that tone with your sister?"
Darkburst fixed Grey with an icy stare, and the old badger shifted uncomfortably. "I thought I'd found the key to the Sacred Roots," he whispered.
Grey reached over, picking up one of the short, blackened sticks. After studying it intently for a moment, his features shifted from inquisitiveness, to puzzlement, and finally, to rage. "By Homer," he whispered hoarsely, "this is one of the Sacred Roots!" Turning on Darkburst, the old boar berated him, "You've destroyed the Sacred Roots. LOOK AT THEM!. How am I supposed to return to Brockenhurst Sett now? What possessed you? How could you have done this to me? You… you IDIOT!"
Brock thrust his head out of the burrow. "What's all the shouting about, Grey?"
"Ask him," the old boar roared, nodding at Darkburst.
Brock hurried over, a concerned look on his face. "What's happened, Darkburst? Why's Grey so angry?"
Darkburst explained how he'd used the Sacred Roots, and how he'd seen a sphere of light, in which bright stars raced across the horizon beyond the Andith River.
Grey snorted at Darkburst's explanation and turned away. He wandered off into the undergrowth, his anger hardly suppressed.
"No, leave him be," Soffen said, as Brock made to follow him. "he'll come back when he's calmed down."

Chapter 11

"What's wrong, Grey?" Broshee dropped back to check on the old Custodian when she saw how far he'd dropped behind the others. He'd become very morose since Brock's decision to push on towards the lake.
Grey shook his head, smiling at her. "Nothing's wrong, Broshee, I'm fine. Just feel a bit tired, that's all." He blew out his cheeks. "It must be all this extra weight I'm carrying around."
They were travelling a barely discernible path that meandered along the bank of the Andith River, searching for a place they could cross. Broshee wondered if they would ever find one. She stopped, cocking her head towards the river. "What's that splashing noise?"
Grey listened for a moment, then winked. "Unless I'm very much mistaken…" The old Custodian walked to the edge of the bank and looked down into the water. The river was calmer here, quietened by a large sand-bar on the curve of the bank. "Ah, just as I thought," he whispered, beckoning Broshee closer. "Come and look, but stay quiet. See, there."
Broshee gasped in delight as a lithe silver body sped away from her with a flick of its tail.
"You're shadow frightened it," Grey explained quietly. "Stand back from the edge a bit."
"But what is it?"
"Hush, not so loud. It's a fish, and if we keep still and quiet, it should come back."
They waited patiently, staring down into the water. Suddenly there it was again, swimming gently in the sandbank's lee. Grey, moving with a speed that caught Broshee by surprise, plunged his paw deep into the river, hooking the fish out onto the bank. It landed with a wet thwack, flipping its body in urgent arcs, trying to re-enter the water. Holding the fish between his paws, Grey bit into its back, killing it with a swift twist of his head.
Broshee sniffed dubiously at the soft white flesh. It looked appetising enough, but she was not quite brave enough to try it. After Grey began eating the fish with obvious relish, Broshee nibbled at a small piece. Pleasantly surprised by the flavour, she quickly set about finishing her portion. After completing their unexpected meal, Grey buried the remains, and the pair set out after the others. Following the trampled grass through the gently undulating landscape, they walked on in silence for some time.
"Grey?" Broshee finally broke the quiet mood.
"Yes?"
"I know mother and Brock are looking for Boddaert's Magic, but what is it exactly?"
"That's a little difficult to explain." Grey was silent for a moment, then said, "The Legends tell us that a powerful magic lived within Boddaert and it remained in his body after he died. So, I suppose it must be his body."
Broshee shook her head. "But that's silly. I mean, his body would have rotted away to nothing by now, wouldn't it?"
Grey smiled at the young sow and nodded. "Yes, you're right, but perhaps we shouldn't take the Legend so literally."
"You mean it might just be a story and the magic doesn't really exist at all?" Broshee hesitated, placing a paw on Grey's flank. "But then what is it that mother and Brock are looking for? I mean, if it's all just a story, what are we doing here?"
Grey shook his head and walked off. "By Homer, Broshee. Will you stop asking questions and get a move on? Your mother will worry about what's happened to us."
Broshee frowned, trying to make sense of what Grey had told her as she followed his swaying figure.
*
At that moment, Soffen had other things on her mind. Along with the rest of the group, she was staring into the dark opening of a tunnel. The ground behind plunged to the river, the bank covered with large clumps of nettles. They would have missed the tunnel completely if Darkburst hadn't disturbed a field mouse, causing it to dart into its dark interior.
Brock shouted into the opening, listening to the echoes. "It sounds as if it goes a long way, maybe right under the river to the other side."
"Where are Broshee and Grey, Darkburst?" Soffen demanded.
"I don't know mother, perhaps they stopped for a rest or something."
Soffen frowned. "Brock, Grey and Broshee are missing, we have to go back up the rise and see where they are, otherwise they'll walk right past us amongst all these nettles. We can explore the tunnel later."
Brock nodded, but Darkburst, showing the impatience of youth, didn't want to delay his exploration of this exciting find. "Mother, why don't I take a quick look to see if the tunnel reaches the other bank, while you look for the others? It will save time later if I do."
Soffen glanced at Brock, who shrugged.
"Well, if you promise you'll be quick," she replied.
Darkburst nodded eagerly, setting off into the tunnel, already creating exciting adventures in his mind. Perhaps he'd find a monster living under the river, or some ancient lost treasure, or a beautiful sow needing rescuing. Maybe even Boddaert's Magic itself!
*
The tunnel was unnaturally straight, its walls smooth and unblemished. Scratching at the concave surface, Darkburst grunted in annoyance when the tip of one claw chipped. Ignoring the uneasy fluttering in his stomach, he made his way further into the darkness, pulled along by his excitement. With the whispering echoes of his claws on the hard surface as company, he constantly stopped, looking back over his shoulder, ready to run at a moment's notice. Was that something following him?
Stepping up his pace, Darkburst convinced himself he did so because he wanted to reach the far side of the river as quickly as possible — not because some imagined monster might follow behind, ready to jump out at him. He pushed onward, the eerie echoes lending an extra urgency to his movements. The surface of the tunnel began oozing small droplets of water, which gathered into small wriggling rivulets, trickling down to the floor, where they collected in large puddles.
A little later, the walls got rougher. Here and there, small cracks appeared, growing in number until they crazed the whole tunnel. Further in, the floor sloped downwards, making the puddles run together in a steady stream. He pushed on, ignoring the cold water moving higher up his legs. By the time it reached halfway up his body, he was feeling cold, tired, and dispirited.
Pulled along by alluring whispers somewhere ahead, Darkburst quickened his pace. The whispers began quietly, almost unheard, like a soft wind blowing through grass. As time passed, they took on a distinct sound, not that of voices, but something close. Growing in volume, they caught his imagination with promises of hidden delights. The water, deeper here, continued to rise until it almost filled the tunnel, forcing him to swim. Darkburst rested, floating, his nose brushing the roof. As the water slopped up and down his snout, he considered returning to the others, but quickly pushed the thought aside. He couldn't do that. If he gave up now, he would look weak. He had no choice but to carry on to the other side. With a thumping heart, he took a deep lung-full of air and ducked beneath the surface, staring at the lighter patch of water marking the place where the tunnel rose again. It was tantalisingly close. He could make it. Why was he hesitating? Poking his nose back into the air space, he took another deep breath and set off through the murky darkness, concentrating all his efforts into his flailing legs.
Darkburst swam with powerful strokes, his back bumping along the roof, guiding him through the darkness. Concentrating on the glow ahead, he paddled through the cold water, relieving the pressure in his lungs by trickling air. The swim was taking much longer than he expected. A buzzing sensation started in his ears, so he quickened his stroke. With bulging eyes and swirling vision, he struggled on.
The tunnel walls pulsed in time with his heartbeats. Thrashing his way forward, he swam as he never had before. Digging his paws deep into the cold liquid, he fought against the water, trying to gain speed, but with each passing moment his lungs became tauter, heavier, his throat bulging with the effort of not breathing.
The compulsion to breathe became so overpowering, he thrashed about in desperation. Heart hammering, he rolled onto his back and scrabbled at the roof. A claw tore loose from his foot, a thin line of blood lacing the water. The blood drifted away, along with his strength. His last thoughts were a collection of fleeting images of his mother. She was standing in a clearing, deep within Brockenhurst Forest, her head tilted to one side as she listened to the liquid, switt-witt-witt-witt of a goldfinch singing in a nearby tree.
Slowly, silently, Darkburst's body sank to the mud-covered floor.
*
Worried voices overlapped with echoes, made it difficult to talk. "But he must be in here. If he'd come out, we'd have seen him."
Brock placed a paw on Soffen's flank, doing his best to calm her. "Perhaps he swam right through to the other side," he suggested. "He might be there now, waiting for us, so he can boast about how clever he's been."
"Do you really think so?" she asked, grasping at the hope.
"Yes, I'm sure of it. Come on, let's go back outside and see if we can spot him on the other bank."
Soffen shook her head, knowing from the tightness in her chest that something was terribly wrong. "No, Brock," she whispered. "You go, I'm staying here, just in case he swims back."
Left on her own, Soffen listened to Brock's footsteps dying away up the tunnel, castigating herself for allowing her cub to explore this place unaccompanied. Something happened to him, she knew it with a mother's certainty. Sitting at the water's edge, she patted the cold dark surface, whispering her cub's name over and over, lost in a grief which threatened to crush her.

Chapter 12

Brock waited a further moon before suggesting they resume their journey, not so they could find what happened to Darkburst — that hope had now gone — but because he couldn't bring himself to ask Soffen to leave her lonely vigil.
The Healer had lain by the water's edge throughout the rest of the long moon and the following sun, shivering in the cold, waiting for her cub to return. Brock had gone to Soffen that first moon, suggesting that he might swim through the tunnel to see if he could find any sign of her young cub, but she became so agitated he quickly dropped the idea.
"Isn't it enough that Darkburst drowned," she shouted at him, "without you doing the same?" Brock rejoined Grey on the riverbank, leaving her to continue her solitary watch.
A little way off, Broshee huddled into a ball, sharing her mother's anguish. She'd matured quickly during the winter, no longer the self-centred youngster who'd romped through Brockenhurst Forest. She lay watching Soffen rock back and forth in an endless ritual of grief. Sighing heavily, she clenched her teeth, trying to keep the tears from filling her eyes. Her feelings of grief, and longing for her mother's comfort, offset by a rising anger at being shut out.
Soffen knew from an early age that Darkburst was the favourite, but now she needed her mother's warmth to fill the dark emptiness growing inside. She called, her soft words echoing through the darkness. "Mother, its time to go."
Soffen shook herself. "Yes, Broshee, you're right. I must be strong for Darkburst, mustn't I?"
Broshee felt an ice shard pierce her heart. "Come on, mother," she urged, "the others are waiting for us."
Soffen gazed at the water, tears spilling down her snout. Tearing her gaze away, she looked at Broshee. "Yes. I suppose there's no point waiting any longer. Darkburst has gone and…" she faltered, too overwhelmed to continue.
Broshee shook the tears from her own eyes, running to her mother's side, nuzzling at her neck, trying to comfort her. Getting no response, she ran from the tunnel, wondering when the pain would stop.
"How's your mother?" Grey called from the riverbank as Broshee ran past. "Broshee — Broshee wait!"
Brock stopped Grey as he started after the young sow. "Leave her be. She's upset. I expect she wants to be alone."
"Do you think Soffen will be alright?" Grey turned back to stare at the tunnel. "Perhaps it would be better if we just gave up this ridiculous search and went back to Brockenhurst Valley?"
Brock frowned. "And you want to suggest that to Soffen? Tell her that Darkburst has died for nothing? That we should give up the search and creep back to Brockenhurst Sett in defeat?"
Turning away, Brock studied the starlit sky, pushing his anger away. The moon broke through the thin covering of clouds, bathing them both with its silvery embrace. It felt wrong that it should be so beautiful.
*
It was a long, hard trek until the group found a place to cross the Andith River. A tree on the opposite bank had fallen into the water, almost spanning the fast torrent. It stopped short of where they stood, leaving an impassable gap.
"We can't chance wading across to the tree in this," Brock shouted above the noise of the raging spume-flecked water. "If we're swept away, we'll drown. We have to find something to reach from the bank to the tree."
A short time later they gathered back on the riverbank with three thick branches, a collection of thin switches, a pile of strong grasses, and a large piece of bark. Laying the branches in a row, they wove the switches through, tying them in place with twisted grass. Hoping the makeshift structure would be strong enough, they eased it out until the end rested on the tree. Pushing the bark on top, they stood back, examining their work with a critical eye.
Brock was the first to cross, weaving extra sticks into the structure as he went. Soffen and Broshee were next, almost running, hearts in their mouths. Finally, Grey took a deep breath, stepping out onto the rough surface. The platform bobbed under his weight and, not for the first time, he wished he wasn't so fat. As he reached the middle, the structure sagged, bouncing in time with his paw steps. His progress became a series of slow, uncoordinated lurches. Twice he nearly lost his footing, only to recover and stagger on.
Grey's last panicky scramble proved his undoing. With a loud crack, a supporting branch snapped, and the structure slewed sideways into the river. He slid across the bark, scrabbling for a foothold, bellowing in terror as it catapulted him into the icy water.
Brock shot out a paw, grabbing Grey's scruff, his claw tearing through the old badger's skin. With another crack, the structure disappeared into the torrent, leaving Grey dangling on Brock's claw, screaming in agony. Dragged forward by Grey's weight, Brock fought to pull him from the river's icy embrace. Broshee ran to help.
"Pull harder, Broshee, pull harder!" Brock shouted.
Redoubling their efforts, they hauled for all they were worth, Brock's features twisting with the effort. Unexpectedly, his claw tore loose, and they watched in horror as he plummeted backwards into the raging torrent.
"Greeeeey!" Soffen's scream echoed across the river. "Help him, Brock. He's drowning."
Bounding along the tree-trunk, Brock jumped onto the bank, chasing after Grey alongside the swirling water. The fierce current swept the old badger away and Brock lost sight of his bobbing head. Rounding a thick bed of reeds, he slid to a stop, heaving a sigh of relief when he saw Grey clinging to a rock in the middle of the river. The old Custodian was struggling to keep his grip as the pounding water tried to wash him away.
"Hang on, Grey, I'm coming," Brock shouted from the river bank, desperately searching for something to help him reach the drowning badger.
Grey's strength weakened, and he slid further down the wet rock. His screams, high pitched and panicky, carried across the river to Brock, who watched helplessly as the old badger finally lost his grip, sliding into the water. His last glimpse of the terrified Custodian was his snout disappearing beneath the foam.
Shouting Grey's name above the roar of the pounding river, Brock beat at the bank in helpless frustration. If only there was something he could do. Grey was dying, and it was his fault. He'd been the one who'd insisted on bringing the old boar on this dangerous journey. Surely there was something he could do to help him now. He couldn't just stand by and watch him drown!
In desperation, he turned to the powers of the Dark Healing. Sending out his anima, he sought the old Custodian's aura, locking his thoughts into the tenuous contact, flooding Grey's mind with his own determination. Don't breathe! Don't breathe in the water! Brock pounded the message into Grey's mind. Don't breathe! Don't breathe in the water!
Brock paid a high price for his desperate use of the Dark Healing. Slowly, from the depths of his mind, the pernicious tentacles of the ancient black art slithered into his consciousness. Having had no formal training in using the Dark Healing, he could do little to protect himself against the Guardian of Blackness, and the dark entity lay down new pathways through his mind — pathways that would have far-reaching consequences.
The oxygen levels in Brock's blood fell. His head pounded, and his ears rang. A black cowl crept over his vision, but still he sent out his message, holding his own breath to produce a symbiosis of minds. Brock's desperation outweighed his common sense, but he was far too guilty over the deaths of his sister and friends, and now the old Custodian, to pay any heed.
"Brock! Brock! What are you doing?" The voice was far away; from another time.
Poised on the Fifth Path of Darkness, Brock hesitated, balanced on the very edge of a deep emptiness — on the point of melding himself with the Guardian of Blackness; of giving himself to the swirling darkness.
The voice came again, hard, insistent. "Brock! Brock, take a breath. Take a breath!"
Senses spinning, Brock broke free from the comforting blackness, reeling from the chaos swirling through his mind. Opening his eyes, he sucked in lungfuls of cool air. The oxygen hit him with such force, he sat back on his haunches. "If you hadn't stopped me, I would have suffocated," he managed through dry lips. By Homer, how could he have forgotten the seductive nature of the Dark Healing, after all the warnings he'd received during his training?
"Are you alright?" Soffen wrinkled her snout, studying him with a worried expression.
"Grey…?" Brock left the question unfinished.
Soffen shook her head, staring at the floor.
*
Broshee looked at the bright moon hanging low in the sky and sighed. She got up, shook some earth from her coat and joined Brock, who lay on a small hillock, staring at the stars.
"How's your mother?" he asked as she settled beside him.
Broshee said nothing for a moment, then shook her head slowly, annoyed. "Much the same."
Brock fell silent, reliving his conversation with Soffen three moons earlier. "It's my fault Darkburst and Grey are dead," Soffen had whispered.
"Don't be silly. Of course it isn't."
She turned away, looking at some distant spot. "If we hadn't come on this journey, none of this would have happened."
Brock tried talking her out of the black mood, but she didn't respond. If she felt guilty because she'd agreed to come, wasn't he just as guilty?
Soffen wandered off towards the river where Brock found her later. She lay beside the remains of the plant she'd eaten, snout slick with vomit, legs curled tightly beneath her. Neither Brock nor Broshee could wake her, or identify the plant she'd eaten. They could only stand helplessly by, watching as she slipped into a deep coma.
Later that moon, Broshee placed a paw on Brock's flank. "You must stop blaming yourself. It's not your fault."
Brock turned to the young sow, a strange look in his eyes. "Did I tell you about the stars?" Broshee shook her head. "I've been thinking about the Legends. I know where they hid the Circle of Claws now." He began reciting from the Legends, adopting the Teller's flat monotone. "They say there's a place where the stars fall to earth, and here the trees reach out to touch one another. It is a mystical place between the earth and the sky. A place where monstrous beasts roam and magical powers reign. Where a strange energy leaps from treetop to treetop when the stars fall to earth." He turned, staring so intently, Broshee stepped back, frightened by the fanatical look in his eyes. "That is where they concealed it. High in a tree, looked over by a fearsome creature who guards it with fulgent light."
"They hid the Circle of Claws in a tree?" Broshee's voice was barely audible.
Brock pivoted, pointing at the star-splashed sky, his voice swelling to a shout. "Look there."
"Where? What are you pointing at?"
"The horizon. Look hard. Can't you see them? Can't you see? Those are the stars that Darkburst saw in his vision."
Broshee squinted her eyes, but could see nothing except the darker shapes of the trees against the lighter sky. She wondered what Brock was trying to show her — the sky and the trees — but what else? Then a movement drew her attention. Far away, so faint that she almost missed them, two stars skimmed across the horizon. When her eyes adjusted to the distance, she saw more. Her heart quickened when she realised it was an entire line of stars moving low across the horizon.
"You see them," Brock stated flatly.
Broshee nodded silently, unable to speak, her eyes locked on the display. "What are they?"
"I saw them first two moons ago." His voice, flat and unemotional, came to Broshee as though from a great distance. "I studied them for a long time, trying to make sense of them." He flicked an ear when a breeze ruffled the guard hairs along its edge. "Then last moon, while you were watching over Soffen, I went to see if I could discover what they were. From a distance I saw the trees where they hid the Circle of Claws, just as the Legend foretold. And it's true, they reach out and touch each other, with the thinnest of branches."
"You went to where the stars fall to earth?"
Brock nodded. "Yes, I went there. I saw the mystical place." Tone changing, he spat words, as though they were painful. "I heard them. The stars. I heard the stars talk. They call to each other. Harsh, incomprehensible sounds. They frightened me."
"The stars talk to each other?"
Brock nodded slowly. "They howl and they moan."
"Are you going back to get the Circle of Claws?"
Brock shook his head. "No. There's been enough heartache and death already." He looked at her and she saw the despair in his eyes. "I'm going to stay with Soffen until…" Turning away, he sighed.
"You think mother's going to die, don't you?" Brock didn't answer, just stared into the distance. Broshee crept away, trying to ignore the empty feeling welling up inside her. She sat with her mother, but quickly grew restless and took a walk.
The black sky, ablaze with stars, reminded Broshee of their earlier conversation. Since she'd seen the stars sparkling on the horizon, something was nagging away at the back of her mind, pulling at her, tugging urgently. "I hear you calling," she muttered. "I hear you." With no power to resist the invisible force, she gave herself to the persistent entity. "I'll come. For my mother and Grey; for Brockenhurst Valley and its ancient forest; for my dead brother. I'll come." Joining her mind with the vitality of the stars, she smiled, feeling complete for the first time in her brief life.
Broshee returned to the burrow, to tell Brock where she was going.

Chapter 13

Skelda woke with a start, struggling to his feet. He shook his head, trying to clear the last vestiges of the dream from his mind. Taking a deep breath, he wrinkled his snout. It'd been a long time since that dream had troubled him. In the dream, he was a young cub, playing by an old tree stump, from which the middle had rotted away. The stump was full of rainwater, and the reflection shimmering in its depths fascinated him. Leaning over to get a better view, he slipped, plunging headfirst into the cold, scummy water. Struggling only made matters worse, and he wedged himself tightly. Panicking, legs thrashing, he thought he would drown; until he was pulled free. Unceremoniously dumped on the ground, he lay coughing and gasping for breath.
The large badger who'd pulled him from his plight, glared down, wrinkling his snout with agitation. "What have I told you about leaving your studies?" his father chastised him. "Let that be a lesson. The next time I catch you away from your studies, you'll not get off so lightly. Go on, get back to the sett."
Expecting a blow to land across his back, Skelda scuttled away before his father changed his mind. Beatings were an integral part of his upbringing. He'd learned to live with them, but the constant punishments built up a smouldering hatred for his father, which one cycle exploded into an attack that surprised them both, leaving his father seriously injured. From that moon forward, his father never laid a paw on him again.
Shaking himself back to reality, Skelda hissed his annoyance at the emotions the dream aroused. Absentmindedly rubbing at the growth on his head, he dislodged the grubs feeding there. He paced, trying to understand why the dream had returned after such a long absence. It always forewarned of some danger, and he'd learnt to ignore it at his peril. He continued pacing, his one good ear laid flat in concentration.
The answer suddenly struck him; something had gone wrong with the search for Boddaert's Magic. That was what the dream was telling him.
Leaving the comfort of his sleeping quarters, Skelda hurried along the tunnels leading to the Taproot Chamber. He stood before the carvings, breathing hard from his exertions.
