Over many seasons Soffen begged and pleaded with her father not to use the Dark Healing when preparing his palliatives, but he wouldn't listen, boasting how his potions were the finest and most powerful in Brockenhurst Valley. She had to admit she couldn't produce anything to match the potency of his specifics, but remained too frightened to use the Dark Healing as an aid. One moon, after an absence of almost three seasons, he'd returned to tell her he was dying. His limbs trembled with the effort of keeping on his feet, and his head hung low. He asked her to help him get to the base of Fire Rock, not having the strength to manage the journey alone. On their stumbling walk, he told her about the secret chambers beneath Fire Rock, and how he wanted to spend what little time remained in their confines.
Following his instructions, she dug out an entrance tunnel and helped him inside, imploring him to let her stay and comfort him while he died. He would have none of it, instead making her promise to hide the entrance once he'd entered. She reluctantly agreed, and with tear-filled-eyes, watched him struggle into the dark interior. She could see him now, turning to say goodbye, his body swaying from side to side as he tried to keep his footing; the fur on his back, patchy and thin, with the scabby skin showing through.
Soffen's eyes widened when she made the connection. There was the similarity she'd been searching for as she'd watched Brock. It was her father! That time beneath Fire Rock, when he'd entered the tunnel. The vacant, troubled look in his eyes, the uncertain gait, the mumbling talk to a badger who wasn't there. She shook the thought aside. She had enough to worry about without an overactive imagination making things worse. Shaking Slikit and Brock awake, she led them out into the wilderness. They still had a long way to go.
Walking through the darkness, they struggled on. Brock fluctuated between bouts of energy and lethargy; Soffen between hope and deep despair. As the sun tinged yet another sky, they dug a burrow, crawled inside and immediately fell into an exhausted sleep.
*
Waking from a deep sleep, Slikit rose to relieve himself. Seeing that Brock was missing, he hurried outside and scouted around, spotting tracks leading into the undergrowth. Hurrying, he followed the trail until it petered out on stony ground. Arriving back, he paused at the entrance, sure Soffen would blame him for not keeping a closer eye on the Teller. Now would be a good time to slip away and return to his life of foraging and sleeping, but in the short time they'd spent together he'd come to admire her. The way she put others first, and her powerful will and gentle strength, reminded him of his mother.
"Soffen, wake up." Slikit shook the sleeping badger carefully. "Soffen come on, wake up!"
Soffen yawned loudly, squinting up, eyes still clouded with the vestiges of sleep. Getting stiffly to her feet, she yawned again and shook herself, looking around the burrow, snout furrowing when she saw Brock was missing. "Where's Brock?"
"I don't know," Slikit admitted. "He'd gone when I woke up." Turning his head, he nodded at the entrance. "I followed his trail as far as I could, but lost it when the ground turned stony."
Soffen left the burrow at a trot, Slikit right behind her, doing his best to keep up as she ran through the undergrowth. They reached the point where Brock's trail disappeared and Soffen cast about in frustration, her nose quivering urgently as she scented the ground. Slikit stood off to one side, watching the Healer's frantic search.
Looking back at Slikit, she shook her head. "I don't understand," she complained. "His scent just vanishes." Slapping a paw on the ground in frustration, she exhaled loudly. "There's fox and stoat aplenty here, but no badger, not one trace. How could he have just disappeared this way?"

Chapter 18

Brock woke with a start, his mind still echoing with unintelligible words. Tossing and turning he tried to get back to sleep, but finally gave up and left the burrow so as not to disturb the others. The sun blazed down from a clear blue sky and a heat-haze shimmered on the horizon. Hunting up some worms, he sat and ate them in a despondent mood. His head hurt and his back felt as though someone had been repeatedly jumping on it. His cough had disappeared, and he silently thanked Soffen and her powers of healing for that. But now there was something else wrong. Raising a paw, he touched the tender patch of skin on his head, feeling a hard lump beneath the surface, just behind his ear. Sitting back on his haunches, he finished the last of the worms and sighed dejectedly.
"Brock!" the pervading, now familiar voice spoke seductively from within his head. "Brock, you cannot deny me."
The voice had grown stronger over the past few moons, accompanied now by spurious memories. Memories of a strange cubhood that didn't belong to him; memories weaving themselves into his own recollections, until he wasn't sure which were real and which imagined. Another badger's memories! Throwing back his head, he bellowed at the madness invading his mind.
"Don't deny me, Brock," the insidious voice came again. "You're not strong enough." Screwing his eyes shut, he tried ignoring it. Acknowledgement was acceptance of his insanity.
When the voice first made itself known, Brock thought it a symptom of the Yellow Cough, but no matter how hard he tried, he couldn't rid himself of the annoying whispers. In frustration, he turned to the powers of The Way. After falling into a trance, he stood amongst the familiar pathways, but this time a shimmering shadow emerged from the depths of his psyche. Though insubstantial, it emitted an aura of great evil. The blackness swirled nearer, filling his mind, its pernicious tentacles freezing the core of his being. The powers of The Way, wrested from his control by the shadow, were fragmenting his mind. Balanced on the point of insanity, he snapped open his eyes, forcing himself out of the trance. Gulping great breaths of air, he collapsed onto his haunches, trying to control his trembling body.
Recognising how close to madness he'd been, Brock thought hard. Something frightening and dangerous had happened, but what? Was this the Dark Healing they'd warned him of during training? In his attempts to cast the insidious voice from his mind, had he somehow activated it? The voice had gone, but it would return. The whispers would rise again, tempting him with promises of power; all he had to do was become one with it. Struggling to his feet, Brock shook himself. He must tell Soffen what had happened, she'd know what to do.
As Brock hurriedly retraced his steps back to the burrow, a blinding pain suddenly lanced through his skull. "You are mine, Brock," the voice cried triumphantly. "I am Darkgrass; mother of Soffen: Fernbreak; father of Darkburst: Rockstay; creator of the Cimmerian Moon: Skelda; Master of the Dark Healing. You cannot cast me aside as you would a worrisome insect, I am too strong for that. Hear me. You cannot deny me."
Slowly, unremittingly, Brock felt his mind slipping from his control. One-by-one, each layer withered, until he could only retreat into the foulest recesses, where the darkest tenets lay, crouching in a terrifying darkness, surveying the world from another badger's eyes.
*
Darkburst thrashed about in deep clinging mud. As he sank beneath the stinking surface, his mouth filled with cold, cloying slime. His cries went unheard. The harder he fought, the deeper he sank. He was drowning. He sprang awake, heart hammering, legs flailing wildly. Taking a deep shuddering breath, he tried to calm himself. It was a dream. Just a dream.
Clambering from the shallow burrow, Darkburst shook the last vestiges of the nightmare from his mind and looked about. The moon shone brightly through breaks in an overcast sky. A dog barked in the distance, and for a moment his eyes flickered with fear. Smiling to himself, he gave a short laugh. The creature was too far away to be of any concern. Tipping his nose to the breeze, he scented the air. Fox and rabbit, but little else, just the soft, cloying aroma of the nearby river.
It had swept him a long way downstream from where he'd fallen in, and he didn't know where he was. Grooming the tangles from his fur, he thought back over this second brush with death. The fish had saved him, buoying him up with their silvery bodies until he'd been able to clamber out onto the sandbank. Not knowing what to make of it, he pushed the mystery aside for another time.
Darkburst studied the clouds, pondering what to do. He could follow the river, which would eventually lead him back to Brockenhurst Sett, or he could strike out overland, using the stars as his guide. He'd done so often enough when a small cub playing on the forest paths. It would be the quickest way, but he was reluctant to take it, especially as the sky was so overcast. He suddenly felt small and frightened. He was alone in a strange land, reliant for the first time in his life on his own skill. The sudden realisation almost overwhelmed him. For no reason, other than he had to go one way or the other, he struck out overland.
*
After walking for half a moon-cycle, Darkburst climbed to the top of a steep rise to get his bearings. As he looked out over the vista, his breath caught in his throat. Blinking, he looked again, expecting the view to have disappeared; just a figment of his imagination. But there it was, the vision he'd seen within the Sacred Roots: the lake reflecting the moonlight from its calm surface; the tall stand of trees marching down to the water's edge; further off, above the edge of the silver water, a line of stars moving swiftly across the horizon. It was an incredible sight, just as it had been when the ball of light erupted between the Sacred Roots, allowing him a brief glimpse into its secret world. All thoughts of returning to Brockenhurst Sett vanished, as with a growing sense of wonder, he studied the landscape. This was where his destiny lay, beyond the shimmering lake where the stars fell to the earth. It was where Boddaert's Magic lay.
*
Brock's mind swirled with memories of what had happened over the past few moons — the pains in his back that forced him to walk with a shuffling gait; the growth on his head, now weeping a foul smelling pus; the voice constantly pursuing him into the furthest recesses of his mind. It could mean only one thing - he was going mad!
He didn't know how long he lay under the bush while his memories disappeared, overlain with another badger's memories. He gave up the struggle, realising he'd lost the battle, and could do little more than peer out from his prison with an acceptance born of hopelessness. Strangely, with acceptance came relief. It wasn't his fault the dark shadow — so much quicker, so much stronger — had crushed him so completely.
Beginning with his earliest recollections — those of his birth and the first opening of his eyes as he stared about in fright and fascination at this new existence — each moment slipped away, fluttering towards the blackness like a leaf on a summer breeze. As the process continued, more and more memories followed, each blinking from existence like a firefly's brief flash. It was an image of Soffen that jolted him from his hopelessness. It reflected her gentle face, outlined by the strong, full moon. She was beckoning him, a half-smile on her lips, waiting patiently for him to come. The gentle sonnet she sang stirred a haunting emotion within his heart. But eventually even this image flickered and died.
"NOOOOOOO!" Brock's anguish rang out into the still air, echoing back from an emptiness that matched his mind. He screamed again, with a renewed resolution. He would regain control of his mind, wrest his soul back from the darkness. Digging deep, he discovered a firm determination, which he used to bolster his fight for survival — and suddenly he was free!
The dark aura rose, stronger now, its voice more powerful, almost painful in its intensity. "It is useless, Brock. Give this up."
As the two essences struggled for domination of one mind, Brock, fortified by the image of his love, fought with a ferocity he didn't realise he had. He fell, limbs flailing the ground with such force it almost broke his bones. Regaining his feet, he staggered, struggling with the unseen darkness trying to pervade his intellect. Clinging to Soffen's image, filled with her love, he fought off the tentacles swirling inside his head. Slowly, layer by layer, he reasserted himself, taking back control, pushing the dark aura back to the depths from which it came. Brock's senses returned: first sound, and the soft, piping wheeb of a distant bullfinch; then smell, and the earthy aroma of fresh worm casts; then taste, and the saltiness of his mouth; lastly touch, and the springiness of grass beneath his feet.
But at the pinnacle of his triumph, it cast Brock back through a swirling kaleidoscope of images, locking his mind inside a colourless, silent prison, from which there would be no escape. He screamed a soundless plea to the Prime Mover, but knew there was no escaping the dark aura now holding his mind in its grip.
*
Skelda's invasion of Brock's body marked another successful step in his stratagem. Stretching the strong limbs that were now his, he nodded in satisfaction as powerful muscles rippled beneath his skin. It was a fine body, one that would serve him well. He scented the cool air; sharp smells, stirring memories of better times. His legs trembled when he shifted them warily, first one then the other, until he could coordinate his movements. His blood, powered by a powerful heart, thrummed through his veins with a vibrancy not felt since cubhood, and his eyes flicked here and there with renewed pleasure, picking out colours he'd forgotten existed. This was better than he'd ever imagined. Lowering his head, he celebrated with a silent elegy to the Guardian of Blackness, who'd made it all possible. It took a little practice before he could make his new body obey him, but eventually he was gambolling about like a young cub. There was no shortage of breath, or searing pain in muscles deformed by the use of the Dark Healing. His new back was wonderfully flexible, which meant he could walk properly, no longer forced to scurry about like a crab. 
Skelda looked up at the clouds and smiled, his lips moving at his command, instead of hanging slack as usual. His brilliant success brought a lightness to his heart, a new determination to his being. This was his duty, his future, and he would bear it well. First, he must get back to Brockenhurst Sett and deal with Grindel, and accomplish it without Soffen and Slikit realising what he doing, or they'd try to thwart his plans.
Scenting the air, Skelda began an exploration of the area. He searched for a particular odour; dead flesh, a scent well familiar to him. Locating what he sought at the base of a gorse bush, he dug, his sharp claws quickly stripping the clods of earth aside. Pulling the dead vixen from her lair, he smiled. She'd suffered a broken leg and starved to death. By her side were three dead cubs. Working quickly, he chewed off four pieces of the vixen's pelt and wrapped them around his feet. Nodding at his own cunning, he made his way across the stony ground, knowing the trail he left would confuse even the best hunter, let alone an ancient badger like Slikit and a Healer as inexperienced as Soffen.

Chapter 19

Grindel inspected his fortifications with an air of accomplishment. Cherva had turned his vague orders into a reality. It protected the sett from all sides. Using badgers drafted in from the surrounding districts, they built tall banks of earth in front of the entrance, filling side entrances with large stones and packed earth. Two tunnels remained open. One faced the large semi-circular clearing between the front of the sett and the new earthworks. The other, a much smaller tunnel, led into the rear of the sett. This tunnel acted as a vent, allowing air to circulate through the various levels. Closing down all side entrances made the lower chambers hot and uncomfortable, but this was a small price to pay for security. To ensure the loyalty of his guards, he ordered chambers set aside for their use in the fresher upper levels. The rest made do with the discomfort of the lower ones. Grindel nodded happily. Cherva would see they accepted the new arrangements with no complaints.
They filled Brockenhurst Sett to overflowing with conscripted badgers brought in from the smaller setts scattered about the forest, so space was at a premium. They even plugged the internal latrines to make room for more badgers. However, the Grand Chamber was for Grindel and Cherva's personal use, a fact frequently commented on behind the guard's backs by badgers forced to live in the discomfort of the deeper chambers. The earthworks laid out around the main entrance formed a complicated maze that required negotiating before gaining admittance to the large semi-circular clearing in front of the sett itself. Its walls were thick, with walkways of packed earth fashioned along the tops. At regular intervals along these walkways, piles of stones were ready for tossing down on any invader. As an additional precaution, they cleared the undergrowth around the sett for a considerable distance.
Grindel covered every eventuality he could imagine and felt confident, that should a group decide to attack the sett, they would quickly die. There was only one weak point — the air vent at the rear of the sett. Unlike the main entrance, this had no labyrinth as protection, so Cherva and his minions built an enormous mound of rocks on a ledge over it. A single small keystone held the mound in place. Removing this would cause the whole pile to crash down, killing any badger below. Two badgers were on permanent guard duty, with two more posted nearby.
Grindel looked out over his domain, grinning happily. As yet it was small, only reaching the periphery of Brockenhurst Forest, but soon he would expand his influence to encompass all of Boddaert's Realm. His well-trained fighters, keen to follow Cherva's lead, could win any attack thrown at them. Grindel frowned, pondering the power he'd given the boar. He needed a hold over Cherva, something to keep him compliant. Chewing the remains of a small hedgehog, he considered his next move. Badachro Sett was the key; he would have to destroy it.
*
The name, Badachro Sett, was a misnomer. In the strictest sense it wasn't a sett, but a scattered collection of separate tunnels and chambers, making use of a cave system at the base of the Badachro Mountains. A frightened sow and her tail-less cub, chased from their sett many generations earlier, discovered the caves and made it their home. It was this same tail-less cub who'd grown up to become the fabled Bawsen, who fought so bravely to save Boddaert's Realm when Evaert threatened to destroy it.
Over time, other badgers joined the embryonic sett, and now, except for Brockenhurst Sett, was home to the largest cete of badgers in Boddaert's Realm. But its population was unlike other setts, most being refugees, outcasts with nowhere to go. Some had missing or misshapen limbs, others deformed ears or eyes, many variations not easily spotted. Whatever their differences, they found a home in Badachro Sett, amongst badgers of their own kind. Over generations the sett had grown so large and sprawling that most left it well alone, even Evaert giving it a wide birth during his attack on Boddaert's Realm — a decision that cost him dearly when Bawsen and her ragbag collection of followers rose against him.
Grindel, determined not to make the same mistake, knew it would be necessary to crush Badachro Sett if he wanted to gain control of the lands surrounding Brockenhurst Forest. Letting his gaze sweep the clear sky, he studied the stars for a favourable sign. They shimmered back at him with a comforting brightness, connecting to his innermost core. Closing his eyes, he began a chant of laudation to the Guardian of Darkness, gathering his strength for the coming battle.
*
Brokin took life seriously, tackling even the smallest tasks with a pride and dedication that set him apart from others. He stood on a small ledge far above Badachro Sett, fighting the shadows cast on the rocky cliff by the moon. Small of stature and softly spoken, many assumed he was also weak, not realising until too late he was a gifted fighter, justifiably proud he could beat any badger in a fight, fair or otherwise. Turning aside from his shadow-fighting, he took a rest, staring at the sett below. It was unlike any other in Boddaert's Realm, its tunnels short and shallow. The ground was thin and hard to dig, so most badgers lived in the caves extending into the rocky outcrop. Most other setts considered them to be deviants, Brokin being no exception. However, it wasn't until he took up his fighting stance, you might notice he carried an extra claw on each foot.
The sound of an argument reached him. He chuckled quietly when he recognised the voices. Checta had strayed into Root's hunting grounds again, something she often did. Her having only three legs and finding it hard to hunt, held little sway with Root. Once again, the bad-tempered boar was chasing her off. Brokin shook his head. They all had their burdens to bear.
*
Badachro Sett was a loose conglomeration of smaller communities, each group mistrusting the other. A Council of Elders kept an uneasy peace between the factions, setting down the laws and mores of the sett. Meeting infrequently, usually when a crisis arose, they promulgated their decisions, which most badgers accepted.
Drac, the leading Elder, scowled at Brokin as he entered the cave. "You've heard the rumours?" he asked abruptly.
"Yes," Brokin answered with a curt nod. The rumours had been circulating for some time. Stories of kidnappings and killings.
Drac nodded, throwing the other Elders a meaningful look. "During the last full moon we sent Elka to Brockenhurst Sett to check out these rumours." The Elder paused, looking uncomfortable for a moment. "He hasn't returned."
This was no surprise to Brokin. Any badgers found in Brockenhurst Forest were set to work on some crazy earthworks they were constructing. Wild stories of badgers being trained as fighters were also circulating. A large boar named Cherva was in control of the fighters and known to be ruthless in his dealings with any dissidents.
"We wondered if you might go to Brockenhurst Sett and find out what's going on." The Elder cocked his head, uncertainty wrinkling his snout, unsure of what the young boar's reaction might be. Sighing heavily, he stared down at the floor. "To be truthful, we need your help, Brokin," he finally admitted. "We need to know what's happening, because if these rumours are true, and the Preceptor is planning to take over Boddaert's Realm, it's inevitable that he'll attack us in the future."
Brokin's breath caught, and his eyes narrowed. "But I've heard nothing of this. What makes you think the Preceptor of Brockenhurst Sett is aiming to take over Boddaert's Realm?"
The Elder shifted uncomfortably, glancing at the others before answering. Two of them nodded for him to continue. "Well," Drac answered slowly, "when I told you just now that Elka hadn't returned from his trip to Brockenhurst, that wasn't strictly true. They found him a half-moon walk from here, dying from his wounds. He had a high fever and wasn't making much sense, but he told the badgers who found him that the Preceptor was taking over control of all the setts in Brockenhurst Forest, and had plans to expand his power into all of Boddaert's Realm. Unfortunately, he died before he could tell us anything more useful."
Brokin stared hard at Drac. The Elder looked away, then down at the floor again. The dark shadows cast by the uneven walls of the cave hid the fact that the old badger had one blue eye and one brown. "We know how skilled you are at stalking. If any badger can get into Brockenhurst Sett and out again without being caught, it's you."
"What wounds?" Brokin asked in a sharp voice.
"Wounds?" Drac responded, shaking his head.
"You said that Elka had died of his wounds. What wounds? I want to know what I'd be up against if I went."
A small involuntary shiver ran down Drac's back. "Stomach ripped open, snout crushed, and leg broken. But he somehow dragged himself all the way back here before he died. The Prime Mover knows how!"
"I'll agree to go on one condition," Brokin stated flatly.
They waited expectantly, but Brokin just stared at them silently. Before training himself to such a high degree in the art of fighting, some of these very badgers had made Brokin's life a constant misery, taking great delight in baiting him about his size and the way he spoke. Now he wanted them to beg for his favours, make them realise how much they needed him.
"What condition?" Drac finally asked.
"That I'm put in charge of training our fighters, because the Preceptor will surely launch this attack."
After a brief pause and a surreptitious glance at the other Elders, Drac nodded his consent.
Brokin left the cave deep in thought, already planning his strategy. Later that moon, he ate a meal of worms, then set out on the journey to the Brockenhurst Mountains, happy with the way things were turning out. From a small insignificant badger, constantly taunted about his appearance, he'd turned into a boar from who the highest authority sort help. Not bad.
*
Cherva watched the Preceptor standing atop the fortifications. He was staring at the stars, and even though Cherva was too far away to hear, he instinctively knew Grindel was talking to them. The breeze was warm, the moon bathing the forest in a bright white light, bringing everything into sharp relief. It was well into the summer-cycle, and soon life would slow as the winter-cycle approached. If the Preceptor left his planned attack on Badachro Sett much longer, he'd have to postpone it until after the cold winter winds had relinquished their hold on the forest.
Cherva checked on his guards, who were becoming slack of late, leaving the Preceptor to his communion with the stars. He heard their voices long before reaching their position. A bad sign, lax guards were a danger to the sett. These two obviously needed a sharp lesson, and he looked forward to giving them one.
With a stealth surprising for his size, Cherva crept through the undergrowth, circling the boars. They were eating worms and chatting animatedly, a short distance from the pathway they were supposedly guarding. Taking his time, he moved nearer, hardly disturbing the ferns as he moved through them.
"I don't care what Lish says, I've had enough of all this." The guard's disgruntled complaints carried to Cherva as he moved into position above them.
Cherva smiled in anticipation.
"Don't talk so loudly, Cros! If any badger overhears us, we'll be in deep trouble."
Cherva poked his snout over the edge of the ridge, studying the guards carefully. He didn't recognise either of them, but that was no surprise, given the large influx of badgers into the sett lately.
The first guard spoke again. "All I'm saying is, now's the time to leave. If we're going to do it, it has to be now. We can't wait any longer. Our relief will be here soon, and when they come, it'll be too late to do anything. Do you really want to spend the rest of your life stuck in this place?"
Cherva growled low in his throat when the rebellious words reached him. Rising to his feet, he made ready to attack.
"Don't move, not one muscle, not so much as a whisker." A sharp claw pressed into the large artery under Cherva's jaw accompanied the whispered order.
Cherva knew the badger at his side had only to make the slightest movement to spill his lifeblood onto the forest floor. He kept still, hardly breathing.
Moving carefully, Cherva's assailant kicked a small stone over the edge of the ridge. "Hey you two," he called. "Get up here now." The softly spoken words stirred the two guards. One cursed loudly.
Cherva waited patiently, aware that, for the moment, the small badger at his side was in complete control. The two guards scrambled their way up onto the ridge and stared in fascination at the scene greeting them. Cherva, their taskmaster head bowed to the ground, held there by a diminutive figure half his size.
The stranger smiled a greeting at them and nodded at the big boar. "This badger was about to attack you. I thought you'd like to know."
Cherva growled quietly, grimacing when the small badger pressed his claw harder into his neck.
"By Homer badger!" The nearer of the two guards protested. "What are you doing? That's Cherva."
The stranger looked at his captive with a quizzical expression. "You're Cherva?" he asked, quickly releasing his hold.
Cherva grunted as the pressure on his neck eased. He turned to face the small badger who'd attacked him, his eyes smouldering with rage. "You just gave up your life, stranger," he snarled. Turning to the two wide-eyed guards, he pointed at his assailant. "Kill this interloper and report to me when your replacements arrive." So saying, he stalked off.

Chapter 20

The journey to Brockenhurst Forest had been uneventful, which made Brokin's present situation even more awkward. He realised he should have stayed hidden after spotting the large badger preparing to attack the guards, but he'd hoped to use the situation to win favour and gain entrance to the sett.
Brokin studied the two guards, who were nervously glancing at each other. They were unsure of themselves, which was dangerous His slightest movement might make them attack in a panic. So he did nothing, just smiled, trying to ease the tension. The badger on his left moved closer to his companion, keeping a wary eye on Brokin.
"What do you think?" he whispered.
The other guard responded with a grunt, looking about nervously. Brokin kept his equanimity when they began arguing, waiting to see what they would do. He was confident that should they try to kill him, they'd die a quick death. Hopefully that wouldn't happen, but he surreptitiously flexed his claws in readiness.
Reaching their decision, one glared at him. "Stay where you are and don't move. We're going to get help. If you move, one of us will come back and kill you!"
Brokin kept a straight face at the guard's audacity, but only just. He nodded slightly, letting them know he understood. These two idiots had no intention of going for help, they were about to take off as fast as their cowardly legs would carry them. After they scrambled down onto the path, still arguing as they went, he slipped into the air vent they'd been guarding. He squeezed himself along the narrow passage, keeping alert for any guards posted along the way, thankful his small size made the going easy.
The deeper into the sett he went, the stuffier the tunnel became, the scents invading his sensitive nose making him gag. Moving quickly, he followed the twists and turns, trying to keep track of the direction he was travelling. Gradually a sound made itself heard, a soft rumbling that got steadily louder the further he went.
Voices! Hundreds of voices echoing along the tunnel towards him! Slowing his pace, he moved with greater caution, his excitement building. Reaching the end of the tunnel, he stopped just short of the exit, tentatively poking his snout over the sheer drop. The noise and stench hit him like a physical blow and he quickly withdrew, trying not to gasp too loudly. When he was ready to take another try at breathing the feted air without vomiting, he took another quick peek, discovering the tunnel was situated high on one wall of an enormous chamber.
Looking upwards, Brokin saw a gigantic root pierced the roof, snaking down to disappear into the floor far below. High in the root, he spotted a large chamber. Eyes widening, he realised this was the fabled Grand Chamber of Brockenhurst Sett. Badgers filled the space to overflowing, so tightly packed they could hardly move. As they jostled for room, an occasional fight broke out.
The unbearable noise quietened and Brokin saw a boar enter the taproot chamber and stare down at the assembly. He studied the seething mass far below, the corner of his lips upturned in an unconscious sneer. Brokin guessed this was Grindel, the Preceptor of Brockenhurst Sett.
"Badgers," the boar's harsh voice boomed out, bringing every eye in the Grand Chamber to his position. "We are almost ready. I have built our defences. We have captured females for our pleasure, and together, we have crushed those setts standing in the way of what is coming. Only one obstacle remains, Badachro Sett." He paused for a moment, studying the crowd. "When we finally destroy Badachro Sett, Boddaert's Realm will be ours for the taking, and every badger living in it will bow to our power."
The badgers assembled in the Grand Chamber exploded into a cheer that almost deafened Brokin, and it was well they did, because the shock of hearing the Preceptor's words had wrung a loud cry from his throat. Withdrawing back into the vent, Brokin tried to steady his pounding heart. He must get back to Badachro Sett at once and warn the Elders.
As he struggled to turn around in the tight tunnel, the Preceptor's voice boomed out again. "Winter is almost upon us, so we have to wait. But after it has shed its icy embrace, we will attack Badachro Sett. Under Cherva's command, our fighters will search out and kill every malformed deviant living in that cesspit. We will leave no misfit to contaminate our future. Not one boar. Not one sow. Not a single cub. Then my badgers, we will be free to restore the splendour that once dwelt in every sett throughout Boddaert's Realm. Once this curse has gone, our cubs will inherit a land of plenty. No more winters so cold the lowest levels freeze. No more summers so wet that our setts flood. We will live in a land of abundance, a land with a future, fit for all who hold true to the mores. What say you, my badgers? Is this not just? Is this not our right?"
The noise of the baying crowd echoed along the vent to Brokin as he negotiated the tight turn and set off along the tunnel as fast as his legs would carry him. Reaching the welcome fresh air, he hesitated, checking whether the coast was clear. Breaking from the vent at a fast run, he hoped the guards hadn't yet been replaced.
*
Brock knew he wasn't mad; a badger named Skelda had invaded his mind, somehow taking over his body, imprisoning him in a deep recess of his consciousness. With the realisation, came a determination to wrest back control and throw out the invader. There must be a way. What one badger could do, another could undo. Thinking about Soffen had given him the strength to fight back once before, so it should do so again.
Tentatively sending out his anima, Brock let it slither through the pathways of his mind like a slow-worm, wriggling along the edges — slyly, stealthily, so Skelda was unaware. Concentrating on Soffen's image, he drew her essence into his mind's-eye. It was a slow process, but he persevered, building the icon piece by piece.
Taking every opportunity Brock dipped into Skelda's thoughts as he crept by, learning how, through the use of the Dark Healing, the boar had flipped his persona into Brock's mind at the moment of his death; how the loathsome, twisted badger had wrapped their feet in the fox's skin to throw Soffen and Slikit off the scent.
Brock's body now felt like a dirty receptacle, filled with the purulent entrails of another badger — not his anymore, defiled as it was by Skelda's persona. The invasion of his body was so complete and intimate, every nerve ripped away by the evil boar's carnality.
Skimming Skelda's thoughts, Brock felt the boar's pleasure in their body, the new liberation the powerful muscles gave him. He continued, moving from thought to thought, desperately searching for any weakness, but found none. He discovered Skelda had lived under Fire Rock for many seasons, using the powers of the Dark Healing to keep himself alive, while he developed and improved his warped plan to conquer Boddaert's Realm. Brock understood at last that nothing could stop this cunning boar from completing his plans. Brock's greatest shock came when he learnt Skelda was not only Soffen's father but also Darkburst's and Broshee's.
As the duality set out towards Brockenhurst Sett, Brock, forced to lie in the darkness of his prison, felt a deep despair which ate away at his spirit. The thought of spending the rest of his life as an observer, unable to take part in life, except through the eyes and ears of another, overwhelmed him, sending a shudder to the very core of his being.
Skelda continued to push his new body to the limit, eager to be back in Brockenhurst Forest. In his imagination he was already running along its sweet smelling paths. He would kill Grindel, take a new mate, raise many cubs. Together they would sweep out into the surrounding countryside and conquer every sett in Boddaert's Realm. Still lost amid these dreams of what was to come, Skelda climbed to the top of a steep escarpment and stopped to rest. Standing at the very edge of a deep precipice, eyes glazed with excitement, he surveyed his imagined forces gathered on the plain below.
Brock's anger erupted almost beyond his control. Seeing one slim chance, though success would mean his death, he acted; for what was life without the freedom to choose? No, in the circumstances, death would be a welcome release. Concentrating every atom of his anger into a bright point of light, Brock used its power to force his body forward. It was only a small step, hardly noticeable, but enough to cause a stumble.
The loose earth at the edge of the escarpment crumbled under their weight and they fell, plummeting downwards, bouncing and tumbling over the steep slope with an ever-increasing speed. Even as they plunged, the two personae fought for control — Skelda desperately trying to stop the fall, Brock doing all in his power to continue it. The descent was long and painful, sharp rocks tearing unmercifully at their flesh. The snapping of bones heard, even over the howls and screams torn from their throat.
Through all pain, Brock remained elated, because he knew he had won.
Their body came to rest at the base of a tree in a cloud of dust.
The rest of the cycle passed slowly. The sun reached its zenith, and after bathing the scene in a powerful light, disappeared behind flat-topped clouds, sheared by a high wind. The body lay unmoving, its fur occasionally ruffled by a gentle breeze. The unseeing eyes, dull and glazed, continued to stare at nothing. As the sun finally set, and the moon made ready to wash the precipice with its gentle radiance, the sky darkened, casting long shadows over the landscape.
Other creatures stirred, crawling and scurrying out into the moonlight. From beneath the stones scattered about the plain, from small openings in the ground, they emerged, their antenna waving as they scented the air. The blood that had oozed from a torn ear, long dried now into a crusty dark-brown patch, attracted the foraging insects.
*
Brokin was on the sixth moon of his journey back to Badachro Sett when he spotted the body at the bottom of a deep ravine. A badger had fallen from the top of the high ridge opposite. He almost turned aside, reasoning no badger could survive such a fall, but curiosity made him hesitate, some uncertainty playing at the back of his mind.
Carefully making his way down the side of the ravine, Brokin reached the rocky floor and hurried to the body. Now he was nearer, he could see one leg was bent at an odd angle. Definitely broken, a bad sign. Reaching the badger's side, it amazed him to discover the boar was still alive. He'd helped Smint, their Healer, frequently, so knew a little about the art of Healing. This boar was near to death and there was little he could do to save him. Casting about the ravine, he found some Ugly Milk-Cap growing next to a birch tree. The mushroom had a dark olive-brown cap with a central depression in it. When he broke it open, it oozed a hot-tasting, milky juice. Dribbling the juice between the badger's lips, he waited. The boar breathed a little easier, even managing a painful half-smile.
In the three pain-racked moons they'd lain at the base of the ravine, the personae that were Brock and Skelda had melded into one consciousness, and together were now far more than their single entities. They looked out from the broken body that had been their battleground with a peace neither had experienced before. The Dark Healing had met with The Way and was now one, cancelling and complementing each other — two opposite energies become whole. Through Brock and Skelda, the Prime Mover had brought together these primitive forces, melding them into something far more powerful. The dual life essence flickered weakly. The body holding them was dying, but that certainty held no fears for either of them. Brock's skills in The Way, combined with Skelda's knowledge of the Dark Healing, had shown them a different path, a new direction to take, and Brokin's palliative administered at just the right moment, had given them the strength to take this one last journey.
As Brokin watched, life flickered and died in the stranger's eyes. Before leaving the ravine, he dug a shallow grave for the boar he'd tried to help. He stood for a moment beside the fresh mound of earth, feeling he'd been part of something far greater than the last moments of a dying badger. An air of mystery hung over the valley, and he glanced around uneasily, shivering slightly in the growing coldness.
On his journey back to Badachro Sett, Brokin's thoughts returned often to the boar he'd buried in the ravine. Something about the dying badger had touched him deeply, leaving him with the feeling all was not well with the world.

Chapter 21

Darkburst rested beneath a gnarled elder, eating the worms he'd gathered earlier. He yawned loudly, his breath forming a halo in the frigid air. The breeze carried a chill, and flurries of soft snow danced between the bare branches of the trees. A fox slipped quietly passed in the distance, single-minded in its search for a winter lair. All about, animals were preparing for the coming cold season.
Darkburst shook off his lethargy, got to his feet, stretched and continued to follow the spoor he'd discovered earlier that moon-cycle. The scent told him a sow had made it, and he wondered what she looked like. Whatever, he would follow her scent until he found her sett and ask for help. It was sometime later, as he emerged from a dense patch of tangled undergrowth, that he spotted the sett beneath a tall ash tree on the edge of a large meadow. He paused for a moment, studying the mound of earth thrown up around the entrance, surprised at its smallness. Surely only one or two badgers could live here? Strange, because badgers preferred living in large groups. He approached the sett warily, but could detect no other scent than the female's around the entrance.
Darkburst shouted into the tunnel "Hello, is any badger there?" His words echoed back unanswered. He tried again. "Hello, can you hear me?" He shrugged. Perhaps the sow was out hunting for food? Yet his nose told him she was definitely down there. Cautiously making his way inside, he looked around. The main chamber was deep and snug. A good place to spend the coming winter. But would the badger living here let him stay?
Searching for signs of life, he looked in every chamber, puzzled when he found no sign of life. The sett was empty, yet the sow's scent was strong, very strong, as if she was standing right beside him. Wrinkling his snout, he cast about in ever-growing confusion, eventually giving up on the conundrum. Accepting the evidence of his eyes, he gave a drawn-out yawn. The long journey had exhausted him. Settling down on a bed of dried leaves spread out in one corner, he contemplated his next move. He'd travelled a considerable distance over the past few moons, but he still had a long way to go. On clear moon-cycles the stars had twinkled their message to him — on overcast ones they'd used their strong, almost ethereal force on his mind, pulling him forward. But now it was time to rest, time to find a safe place in which to spend the cold cycle. Perhaps the female living here would allow him to stay once she got to know him. Closing his eyes, he made himself more comfortable amongst the leaves, sighing contentedly. The sett was warm and relaxing and his eyes grew heavier as sleep crept up on him. Perhaps just a short nap, he thought. After all, he'd come a long way. For a short time he fought the tiredness, but finally gave in, his gentle snores filling the chamber.
In the meadow above, the sun rose, lighting the low clouds with a red glow. The snow eased, then turned to drizzle. As the temperature rose, creatures began scurrying about, using this last opportunity to collect winter stores. Tucked snugly in the warm chamber below, Darkburst missed the dawn's display as it drove his stars away. Time passed, and the snow returned, gathering its strength to send heavy flakes scurrying around the slender trunk of the ash. The tree, sensing the coming winter, as it had for many generations, nestled itself into the ground, its great roots creaking in protest. In the tree's slow continuum, winter was but a small blip in temperature, a regular occurrence that came and went, cycle on cycle; a short period of rest and recovery before sending out fresh young shoots to welcome the warmth of the returning sun.
Deep in the earth, beneath the ash's roots, Darkburst opened one eye and listened intently. What had woken him? He'd heard something? A cough? Yes, there it was again. Looking around, his eyes widened when he discovered he was alone. Settling back down, he feigned sleep, snoring loudly, but staying alert, every sense quivering with expectation.
Another soft cough from across the chamber. Very faint, but unmistakable. Getting up, he stealthily crossed to the far wall and studied it. There, just visible, was a lighter patch of soil on one side of the entrance tunnel. He smiled, nodding his head in admiration. It was brilliant.
"You'd better come out now," he cried. "I know you're in there."
After a brief pause, a few grains of soil trickled down from the patch on the wall, then a few more, then an unbroken stream as the lighter coloured section collapsed onto the floor in front of him. The soil had blocked a short tunnel dug into the side of the chamber.
"Please, don't hurt me," a tremulous voice pleaded from the darkness.
"It's alright," he called softly. "Come on, come out. I won't hurt you."
Darkburst's eyes widened when a frightened sow scrambled out over the loose pile of earth. She was completely white. Backing away awkwardly, fear alive in her pink eyes, the terrified badger looked about apprehensively, every nerve taught.
Realising how frightened she was, Darkburst's reached out a paw. "No, it's alright," he said, trying to reassure her. "Really, I won't hurt you." He stepped back a few paces. "What's your name?"
The sow glanced at the entrance tunnel, making ready to flee, but when Darkburst made no move towards her, she relaxed a little. "My name's Brightness," she replied, her voice subdued, her eyes lowered.
Darkburst smiled reassuringly. "Do you live here by yourself, Brightness?"
Her eyes widened, as though an admission would be dangerous. He moved further away. "Come on, it's all right," he coaxed. "Really, I promise I won't hurt you."
Slowly crossing the chamber, Brightness settled herself on the leaves, her nervousness causing the shimmering white guard hairs on the tips of her ears to quiver.
Darkburst smiled again, cocking his head in a friendly gesture. When he spoke, he was careful to keep his voice low and friendly. "I've a story I'd like to tell you, Brightness," he said. "If you'll listen?" She nodded.
Taking his time, he told Brightness the story of his life. How he was born an albino, just as she was. How his mother, using her exceptional skills as a Healer, made him as other badgers. And how the Preceptor of his sett had given him a significant task to carry out. He talked far into the sun-cycle, reliving his encounters with danger — telling her how, twice, he'd nearly died, saved by creatures appearing as if by magic.
Brightness listened to his story with rapt attention, her pink eyes following every move as he paced back and forth across the chamber, lost in his description of the bright ball of light emerging from the Sacred Roots, and the wonderful image it had contained. As she listened, she relaxed, uncovering a store of worms. Continuing his narration, he took quick bites, swallowing rapidly so he could continue. Brightness lay back down, nibbling delicately at each morsel.
Darkburst didn't know how long he talked, but when he stopped, the sun was high in the sky. They stood together, under the shade of the ash, two very different badgers sharing a common heritage. Darkburst, his coat a sleek grey, and close by his side, Brightness, her white coat reflecting the weak winter sun.
Shaking the snow from his back, he frowned. "Brightness," he asked quietly, "do you think I could stay here for the winter-cycle?"
"Yes," she replied without hesitation.
*
During the following long moon-cycles, Darkburst and Brightness lay snug within their cosy chamber, serenaded by the sounds of the ash tree's roots as the winds swayed its slender trunk back and forth. They mostly slept, but occasionally one would venture forth to grub around the base of the tree for an insect or two. On these occasions they would talk or mate, or just share each other's company before returning to the somnolent state that marked the passage of winter. 
It was during these occasional wakeful periods that Darkburst learnt how, because Brightness was born with white fur, the Elders forced her mother to abandon her on an exposed hillside. Ignoring convention, her mother crept back to feed her every moon-cycle, moving her to different locations so no badger would discover the hiding place. She became used to being left alone, but always looked forward to her mother's visits — until one moon they stopped. Brightness worried something had happened to her mother. Perhaps she was lying injured somewhere, or worse still, dead? After four moons with no sign of her, she set out on a search.
During her brief visits to the hide-away on the hillside, Brightness's mother had repeatedly warned her, no matter what happened she must not go down to the sett below, because the badgers there would kill her. When she asked why, her mother looked uncomfortable, but finally told her it was because she was different. They would hate her white coat and pink eyes. Even though pressed, her mother would say no more about the matter, so she eventually stopped asking.
Having convinced herself that her mother only told her this to stop her wandering off and getting lost, she pushed the warnings aside and set out for the sett. Following her mother's faint scent through the undergrowth, Brightness waddled down the hillside under a bright moon, eager to see her once more. After losing herself in a dense thicket, she heard faint voices. Forcing her way through the tangled undergrowth, she tumbled out in front of four young cubs playing catch-as-catch-can. She laughed when they shrieked their surprise at her sudden appearance. But to her dismay the youngsters backed away, a deep fear clear in their eyes as they scattered in panic, screaming for their mothers.
It shocked Brightness. Why were they so frightened of her? She had done nothing to threaten them. Hearing a low growl, she turned, confronted by a large boar, top lip curled back over his teeth in a threatening gesture. The boar's coat was erect, adding to his impressive size. Without warning, he swiped Brightness across the snout, raking her from eye to nose. Shocked at this unprovoked attack, she turned and fled, terrified the boar would hurt her again.
She ran back through the thicket and up the hillside to her hiding place, but was only there a short time when the murmur of voices reached her. Peeking out from behind a large rock, she saw a band of badgers heading up the hill, the boar who'd attacked her leading the way. Brightness fled. Her mother had been right, she should have kept well away from the sett. The badgers living there were horrible.
During the following moon-cycles her snout swelled alarmingly, one eye closing so tightly she couldn't see out of it. She felt hot and weak, vomiting each time she ate. For five moons she lay under a thick bush, shivering violently, even under the scorching sun beating down on her. Brightness thought she was dying, but slowly recovered, regaining more strength with the passing of each moon, until all she had left of her brush with death, was a jagged black scar running from eye to nose, marring the whiteness of her fur. It was a permanent reminder of the hatred directed at her. She'd always be an outcast.
It took a long while before Brightness accepted she would never see her mother again. Not knowing what to do, she stayed near the hillside until a new moon rose, hoping she might be wrong and her mother would appear out of the darkness, a bundle of worms in her mouth and a soft smile on her lips. But it wasn't to be, and finally she left the hillside for the last time, turning her back on the small burrow with a heavy heart.
Brightness tried approaching other setts during her lonely wanderings, but these attempts always ended in her being driven away. The last time the assault was more verbal than physical, but it hurt her just as deeply. She ran from the encounter, tears stinging her eyes, determined no badger would hurt her again. One moon, stumbling upon a slender ash on the edge of a large meadow, she felt she'd arrived home. Digging herself a small, comfortable sett beneath the tree's protective roots, she decided she'd spend the rest of her life here.
Brightness spent many seasons living out a quiet existence on the edge of the meadow, snug in her sett during the winters, roaming the nearby copse during the summers. Not happy, but content as she had any right to be. Time passed and her life settled down into a reassuringly dull routine. Late one moon, she heard a badger's pawsteps approaching her sett. In a rising panic, she rushed back, hurriedly digging a short tunnel into the side of the sleeping chamber. Backing into it, she carefully packed the earth back in place, hoping the stranger would not find her.
How long she lay in her self-imposed prison, trembling with fright, she didn't know, but it seemed forever. Laying close to the floor, breathing slowly to preserve air, Brightness tried ignoring the stuffiness that quickly built up. To keep calm, she concentrated on memories of her mother and the hillside that had been her playground, but the air quickly became so foul she could scarcely breathe.
She coughed, then again, waking the snoring badger from his sleep. Forced to emerge from her hiding place, Brightness saw Darkburst waiting for her — not the monster she'd expected. Instead of an attack, he'd shown only kindness and understanding. For the first time in her young life, she discovered what friendship was. He proved to be a badger who could accept her for who she was and not care about the colour of her fur.
During the long winter-cycle, Brightness fell deeply in love with the puzzling badger. And now, laying snuggled into his side, watching the gentle rise and fall of his breathing, she wondered if the future might hold some happiness for her after all.
*
Brightness stood forlorn, heart beating wildly as Darkburst moved out across the meadow under the weak sun. Last moon he'd told her he was leaving. In a low, faltering voice, he explained how he must continue his search for Boddaert's Magic now winter had ended. All her entreaties were in vain; he remained adamant. He gave her a keepsake before he left — a small piece of root he said would keep her safe until he returned. She touched it, feeling its warmth flood through her paw as she watched her love make his way to the summit of the far hill. Scenting the air, she sighed heavily. The warm cycle was returning and everywhere plants were thrusting up fresh growth, creatures stirring from their winter lairs. It was a time of new beginnings, not a time for such sad partings.
As Darkburst grew smaller in the distance, Brightness thought back over what he'd told her. Over the past few moons a powerful urge came upon him, giving him no rest. He was out hunting beetles by a large tumble of rocks when the Talisman hanging about his neck flashed brightly, reflecting the moonlight into his eyes with a piercing intensity. Thoughts of Grindel and the unfinished search for Boddaert's Magic flooded his mind, and no matter how hard he tried, he couldn't still them. He told her he'd never been happier than during the past winter-cycle spent with her beneath the ash tree, and wanted nothing more than to stay, but he'd find no peace until he completed the task Grindel had set him. It was his destiny, his reason for being, and he must do it alone.
Darkburst turned to look at her, giving a last wave before topping the hill and disappearing from sight. Brightness lowered her gaze, wondering if she'd ever see him again. Not since her mother's disappearance had she felt so desperately unhappy and abandoned. "Come back to me quickly, my love," she whispered.

Chapter 22

Soffen gazed at the old badger, sadness misting her eyes. "I shall miss you, Slikit."
Slikit smiled and nodded slowly. "And I shall miss you too," he replied quietly. "But I really don't want to go to Brockenhurst Sett. You understand that, don't you?" When Soffen shrugged, he looked into the distance. "I'm used to living on my own, you see." His voice took on a defensive quality. "My future is out there somewhere, in the wide spaces and lonely hills. Not in the busy tunnels and crowded chambers of Brockenhurst Sett, as grandiose as they probably are."
"I know, Slikit," Soffen assured the old badger.
They stood quietly for a moment, neither moving, both reluctant to break the mood. Then Slikit awkwardly touched his nose to Soffen's neck, turned his back and pushed his way into the undergrowth. She could follow the old badger's progress, his cracked old voice mumbling and grumbling at everything that got in his way.
When silence finally fell over the landscape, Soffen shook her head forlornly, turning back towards the burrow. Now that Slikit had left, there was little reason to delay making preparations for her journey to Brockenhurst Sett, where she would wait for news of Brock and Broshee. Humming a sonnet from her cubhood, she cleaned the burrow for the last time, leaving it tidy for the next badger who might happen along. Once everything was spick and span, there were no more reasons to dally, so she set out beneath a bright moonlit sky, her spirits already back in Brockenhurst Forest. Travelling by moonlight, making temporary shelter beneath a bush or thicket of ferns during the sun-cycle, Soffen made excellent progress. The weather was turning cold, but she was confident she would reach Brockenhurst Forest before the chill winter winds descended and forced her to dig a burrow to wait out the snowy cycle.
The journey was mainly uneventful, only two things stood out; reaching the tree they used to cross the rushing torrents of the Andith River, and her arrival at the tunnel where Darkburst drowned. She stopped for a rest at the tree and ate a small meal. Before continuing, she stood on the riverbank, paying a last homage to a gentle old badger. Tenderly dropping holly leaves onto the rippling water, she watched them swirl away on the current, picturing again the rotund proportions of the old Custodian. Wiping a tear from her eye and bidding Grey a last farewell, she resumed her journey.
Reaching the dark tunnel where her cub drowned, Soffen was reluctant to enter its dark entrance, but there was no other way of reaching the opposite bank. A shiver ran down her back. Would she drown as she tried to swim through, or perhaps stumble across her cub's bloated body floating in the water? The thought provoked such a deep horror, she almost turned aside. After much dithering, she rushed inside.
The long hot summer had dried the tunnel, and now only a slick layer of mud remained. There was no sign of Darkburst's body, and that raised a small hope in her heart. Perhaps he hadn't drowned after all? Perhaps he'd survived to make it back to Brockenhurst Forest? She hurried through the tunnel, constantly slipping on the sticky mud, breathing a heart-felt thanks when she emerged on the far bank. The sun was spearing the morning sky with long slim claws of brightness, but she decided not to rest during the sun-cycle. She was so near Brockenhurst Forest it made little sense to wait for the next moon before continuing.
The sun had long passed its zenith when Soffen reached the outskirts of Brockenhurst Forest. She quickened her pace in anticipation of seeing Darkburst, Broshee and Brock — having convinced herself they would be there when she arrived. Her heart pounded at the thought, and it was as much as she could do not to break into an undignified run at every step.
*
"Stop right there, female!"
Soffen stumbled to a halt, startled by the unexpected command. Two rough-looking boars stepped out from behind a thicket and confronted her, their gaze roaming her body with barely suppressed lust. She stared back at them, nerves taught. One approached, thrusting his snout under her tail in a most ill-mannered way, laughing when she jumped back and squealed her indignation.
"Who are you? What do you want here?" his companion demanded of her.
"My name is Soffen," she answered with as much dignity as she could muster. "This is my home."
The boar's demeanour changed when he heard her name. "Soffen, the Healer?"
When she nodded, both guards took up position at her side. Keeping close, so she could not escape, they began shepherding her along the path towards Brockenhurst Sett. The larger of the two boars wore a huge grin. He was contemplating the reward Cherva would give him for bringing in such a valuable prize. A bigger chamber certainly, and perhaps — He leered at the female stumbling along beside him. What would she be like, he wondered? Certainly better than the skinny sow that he'd had last summer.
As they hurried along the forest path, Soffen kept silent, aware of the surreptitious glances she was receiving from one of her guards. His constant leers were making her uncomfortable. The dull faced, lethargic badgers they met along the path shocked her. Without exception, everyone cast their eyes to the ground as the trio bustled by. Rounding a sharp bend, she couldn't help but gasp aloud at the sight greeting her. Massive earthworks defiled the once beautiful Brockenhurst Sett!
Entering the earthworks through a small opening in the wall, Soffen and her guards passed into a confusing labyrinth of passageways which twisted and turned, splitting and rejoining in such confusing patterns it made her senses reel. Before they'd taken more than a hundred paces, she got hopelessly lost. They'd scooped alcoves at regular intervals along the twisting passageways, and here large boars stood guard, nodding silently as they passed. The passageway narrowed, and they fell into a single line, one guard leading the other in the rear. They finally reached a large semi-circular clearing fronting the entrance tunnel. The walls, smoothed mud, would be impossible to climb.
As they entered the clearing, the guards took up position at her side, guiding her at an angle across the packed earth clearing, where they stopped in front of the main entrance.
"Wait here," one guard barked, hurrying off to speak to a large boar guarding the opening. After talking animatedly for a moment, he returned. "Cherva is in the Grand Chamber," he told his companion, prodding Soffen into motion again. The stench engulfing her as they entered made Soffen gag. It was some time before she could see through the tears stinging her eyes.
One guard barked a short laugh at her reaction. "You'll get used to that," he growled, nudging her further into the sett. "We all do, eventually."
Soffen was in familiar territory now, and her heart beat faster at the thought of seeing Brock again. He would explain what was happening to Brockenhurst Sett, and where all these rough badgers had come from. Reaching the entrance to the Grand Chamber, the trio halted and for the first time the two guards seemed unsure of themselves. The air being less repugnant here, Soffen took a deep breath to steady her pounding heart. The smaller guard swallowed loudly, looking at his companion. Getting no reaction, he shrugged, then walked into the chamber.
He quickly reappeared "In you go," he said, pushing Soffen forward.
Soffen took a few tentative steps into the Grand Chamber, then stopped in surprise. Facing her was a badger she recognised. Her heart beat faster. It was Grindel, the Preceptor, leader of the Custodians and Guardian of the Sacred Roots. He glared at her, his feelings of contempt obvious in his dark eyes. Standing off to one side was a giant hulk of a badger. Soffen had never seen him before, but guessed it must be Cherva, the boar the guards had talked about in hushed voices on their journey back through the forest.
"Come forward, female," the Preceptor ordered. Soffen moved further into the chamber, casting her eyes to the floor in respect. "This is our fabled Healer," Grindel told Cherva in an aside, not taking his gaze from her. "One of those who stole the Sacred Roots."
"But I can explain…"
"Be quiet sow," the Preceptor cut short Soffen's protest with a harsh growl. "Speak only when you're spoken to." He turned to the giant boar, continuing the conversation as though no interruption had occurred. "Now why do you suppose she did that Cherva? What reason could our Healer have to steal such a precious item from us? Perhaps she took them to help heal a sick cub? Or maybe ward off an attack by some marauding badgers? What do you think, Cherva? It would need to be something pretty important, wouldn't it? After all, stealing the Sacred Roots is not something you would undertake lightly, is it?" The Preceptor turned his dark eyes on Soffen. "Well, Healer?" he prompted.
Soffen explained how she had gone with the others to search for Boddaert's Magic, hoping to save Brockenhurst Sett. How she believed that all the badgers living in Brockenhurst Forest would die if Brock's vision was true. She told of the tragedies that had befallen her on the journey; of Grey's death; the drowning of Darkburst, and the disappearance of Broshee. Finally, in a painful voice, she told of Brock's sickness and ultimate disappearance.
Throughout the Healer's narration, the Preceptor listened intently, nodding his head occasionally, as though encouraging her to continue. When she finished he stood quietly, staring at her, his silence adding to the tension.
Cherva moved his considerable bulk slightly, and the Preceptor barked a short laugh. "Healer," he said, shaking his head in disbelief, "you certainly tell a wonderful tale. So tell me, who thought up this preposterous story? Was it you, or Brock? Or perhaps Grey? Yes, probably Grey. He was always too sharp for his own good." Shaking his head again Grindel chuckled his amusement, laughter dancing in his eyes.
"But it's all true, Preceptor," Soffen protested softly. "I promise you."
"No female," Grindel retorted. "I'll tell you what's true. You and your little gang of followers went looking for Boddaert's Magic — not to save Brockenhurst Sett — but to destroy it. You planned to use it's magic for your own twisted ends, but things went wrong, didn't they? The others sent you back with this ridiculous tale, hoping they could persuade me to turn a blind eye to your misdeeds. Well, we'll see about that later. First tell me about your cub, Darkburst. You say you never found his body in the tunnel under the river?"
Soffen shook her head, and Grindel nodded. "I see. Then perhaps there's a chance he still lives."
Glancing at Cherva, Grindel wrinkled his snout as though an unpleasant smell had entered the chamber. "Take this away somewhere and put a guard on it," he ordered. But as Cherva herded Soffen from the chamber, Grindel stopped him momentarily. "Make sure no badger touches it," he added in a low, harsh growl. "You understand my meaning?"
Cherva nodded and turned away, pushing Soffen before him, wondering why the sow rated such special treatment. Guiding the Healer through the tunnels towards the chamber below Fire Rock where they kept prisoners, Cherva pondered on the reasons the Preceptor might be so interested in the Healer's cub. He was missing something important here and would do well to question the Healer about this himself, but how to do it without the Preceptor finding out was a problem.
Cherva pushed Soffen into a small chamber already overcrowded with badgers. They looked weak and emaciated, with dull, sunken eyes. A few heads turned as she stumbled about, looking for somewhere to lie down, but mostly they just stared vacantly at the floor. She noticed all the badgers in the chamber were avoiding one corner, even though this meant that there was less room for everyone else.
Soffen pushed her way to the corner, weaving through the crowded badgers. To her horror, she found three dead bodies piled on top of each other. One, just a cub, was scarcely a season old. She looked at her fellow prisoners for an explanation, but none would meet her gaze. Hurrying back through the press of bodies, she crossed to the low archway and confronted the badger guarding the entrance.
"There are three dead badgers in here," she protested angrily. "How can you just leave them laying there? Haven't you got the decency to take them out and bury them? What's wrong with you?"
The guard turned and raked Soffen's snout with sharp claws. She fell back with a cry of pain, her sensitive nose dripping blood. She stood motionless for a moment, her heart beating fast, not really believing what had just happened. When no badger came to her aide, she angrily pushed her way to the nearest wall and lay down facing it, her sobs lost amongst the constant moans and whimpers of those around her. A short time later, three large boars pushed their way into the crowded chamber and dragged the dead bodies out. She lay facing the wall, curled into a tight ball, her stumpy tail covering the tip of her nose. She sobbed to herself, claws clenching and unclenching as she cried. Time passed, and she breathed more easily, her tiredness dulling her misery.
Soffen slipped into that misty place between sleep and wakefulness, where troubles seemed to dissolve away and the harsh world become unreal. Her memories took her back to the forest that she knew so well, along paths bathed by golden moonlight, beneath trees that spread their protective canopies over all badgers, no matter how horrid. She fell into a deeper slumber and dreamt of Brock. Together they ran along riverbanks, jumping in and out of the sparkling water as they chased fish from their hiding places on the stony bottom. Then they were flying through the cool air like two owls hunting mice, and for the first time since Grey's death, her lips formed a smile, her eyelids flickering as her eyes darted back and forth.
Soffen, jerked awake by a gentle shake and whispered words, looked about in confusion. The familiar face of Moss, Raffen's friend, looked down at her.
"That was a very brave thing you did. Getting those brutes to remove those poor badger's bodies," Moss whispered.
"What's happening, Moss?" Soffen asked despondently. "Has the whole sett gone mad?"
Moss settled herself down, flicking her tongue over dry lips. She looked tired, her fur unkempt and her claws dirty. Talking in an undertone, she told Soffen about the changes that had taken place since she'd left on her search for Boddaert's Magic. Though weak and thirsty, the young sow talked for a long time. The details she shared shocked Soffen so much that she scarcely drew a breath as she listened to the terrible account. She felt a new respect for the exhausted badger. Unlike many of her peers, this young sow had refused to give in to the demands made upon her by the badgers now controlling Brockenhurst Sett: the fighters and guards who considered it their right to receive food and water, and mate whenever the fancy took them. Like most of the others packed into the small chamber, Moss had refused to cooperate and was now paying dearly for her stubbornness. After Moss finished, she fell into a restless sleep, leaving Soffen to ponder what she'd heard.
Rising, Soffen shook the knots from her body, being careful not to disturb her sleeping friend. She looked around at the miserable scene, sighing despondently. She moved through the crowd, asking any who'd listen a question, persevering until she'd spoken to every badger she could. After the last badger answered her question with a negative shake of the head, she slumped back down beside Moss, losing herself to a feeling of utter desolation.
As Soffen fell into a fitful doze, a badger standing nearby nodded at her. "What did she ask you?"
"She asked me if I'd heard anything about some badger called Brock," came the disinterested reply.
"Yes. She asked me that too."
*
The cold weather fell on Brockenhurst Forest with an unexpected ferocity. Because of the large numbers of badgers over-wintering in the sett, food — always scarce at this time of the cycle — was even scarcer. Deaths from illness and malnutrition quickly mounted until those living in the lower chambers became restless. The less frightened mumbled their discontent more audibly, which forced Cherva's guards to keep up a constant patrol. When the Preceptor realised how bad things were becoming in the lower tunnels, and fearing the Yellow Cough might decimate his fighters, he ordered Soffen's release and return to her healing responsibilities. Knowing the Preceptor had ordered Cherva to throw any badger with fever out onto the deep snow banks to die, even though sick herself, she agreed.
Soffen smuggled some of the worst afflicted to her old burrow in Bluebell Clearing, where she could tend to their illness and hopefully save their lives. By convincing Cherva she needed help in collecting plants and herbs to treat the sick, and using the sick badgers as her helpers, she fooled the guards. Returning after they had changed for the cycle, none suspected when she returned alone.
During the long winter cycle, Soffen kept busy tending the constant stream of sick badgers being sent to her chamber. Her trips into the forest to collect the few herbs that survived the harsh weather also gave her the opportunity to familiarise herself with the labyrinth guarding the entrance to the sett. By pretending to get lost from time to time she took full advantage, memorising every detail of the complicated layout. When no guards were in sight, she made small marks at the intersections which would act as a guide through the tangled web of corridors. Soffen planned to escape Brockenhurst Sett when the weather warmed. Badgers needed to know what was happening. There had to be some badger somewhere in Boddaert's Realm, who could put an end to this madness. In the meantime, she'd continue helping the sick as best she could.
Soffen never got the chance to put her scheme into action. At the first signs of warmer weather, Cherva withdrew her privileges and once again she found herself confined to the overcrowded prison. Until she lost her freedom again, she hadn't appreciated how much she relied on her trips out into the snow-covered forest to keep her sane. Now she fell into a dark depression.
One moon, Cherva came to tell her the Preceptor wanted to see her in the Grand Chamber immediately. Before going to the meeting, she made her way down to the lowest levels, hurrying towards the large drinking pool at the very bottom of the sett. If she wanted to take advantage of this opportunity, she'd need to make herself presentable. She had to persuade the Preceptor to let her out on one last collecting trip so she could slip away.
Standing over the shimmering pool, she stared into its depths, shocked at how thin she was. Her reflection stared back, almost a stranger. Leaning closer, she studied the deep furrows in her snout, the grey hairs liberally sprinkled through the black stripes on her cheeks. She looked so old, so worn. What would Brock make of her now, she wondered? As Brock's image flooded her mind, leaping at her from the distant past, something stirred under the rippling water. Deep down at the bottom of the pool, in the murky layers where the past and the present merged — where the netherworld permeated the badger's world — something ancient awoke.
Stretching up from the mud, it tentatively tested the water, undefined and insubstantial, but intensifying as it became more confident. It probed further, then rested. Gathering itself again, it quickly expanded outwards, slithering over and through itself, cleaving rapidly upwards with coils of brightly coloured tendrils, until it filled the pool.
Soffen gasped as a stream of light exploded upwards from the water, spraying her with such force she stumbled backwards. Shading her face with a trembling paw, she watched in awe as points of brightness bobbed and weaved about the roof of the chamber. Greens and blues swirled urgently around her head, chasing each other like young cubs playing in a forest glade. Round and round they swirled, laced here and there with blood red and moon yellow, the colours contracting and expanding before merging into a bright point of light which exploded outwards again in a breathtaking display of energy. The short bristles on her snout tingled as she watched the colours swirl through each other with such speed they appeared solid.
A sphere formed, which flattened into a large disc. The disc hovered in the air for a moment, then tilted sharply, presenting its circular face to her, its mid-section flashing and shimmering as it expanded outwards towards its circumference. The boundary flickered, pulsing faster and faster, ruffling her fur with its energy, drawing her gaze to its very centre, where she stared through a portal into another world.
She took a step forward.

Chapter 23

Darkburst was ravenous. His last meal, an adder he'd stumbled across four moons earlier, was long digested. He found it hidden amongst pine needles. The whitish spots marking its back reflecting the dim moonlight gave it away. He approached cautiously, knowing the danger. It reared at him, fangs extended, ready to strike. Twisting to one side, he darted forward, seizing the snake just below the head, biting down hard. Its tail whipped back and forth, but he brought its suffering to a quick end with a flick of his head. The unexpected meal filled the void gnawing away at his belly, but all too soon he was hungry again. Locating food in the pine forest was becoming a never-ending struggle.
Darkburst's constant hunger made him light-headed, and he found it hard to concentrate, his thoughts constantly straying. What was he doing here in this gloomy place where the moon never shone? Why were the trees packed so tightly together, blocking out the sky? Shaking his head, he tried to focus. He was searching for something. Yes, he was searching for something, but what?
