Suddenly the tree nearest Darkburst shifted. It lunged forward, towering right over him, threatening to engulf him with its branches. He panicked, looking about in desperation, searching for a way out of the forest. But he saw only trees — tree, upon tree, upon tree, upon tree, growing from each other's trunks, like a gigantic shrub which had suddenly sprouted thousands of claws, reaching out for him with rattling branches.
Closing his eyes, he shook his head, taking deep breaths to steady himself. When he opened them again, the trees were still there, ranked before him in their thousands, stretching away into a heavy mist. His world had condensed into a swirling kaleidoscope of shifting trunks.
Darkburst broke and ran, weaving between the trunks when he saw them, bouncing off when he didn't. Onwards he ran, the pine needles beneath his feet swirling about his belly as he kicked them high. Gaining the top of a rise, he raced down the far side, eyes wide, lips pulled back across his teeth in terror. In his panic he saw nothing, constantly banging his sensitive snout and bruising his body. Then tripping on a root, he twisted sideways, instinctively tucking his head into his flank to protect it. He landed with a thump that forced the last of his breath from his lungs, but it shook some sense into him and his panic subsided.
What was he doing? Why was he running like some crazed youngster being chased by a dog? Then he recalled the trees reaching out for him, wanting to hold him in an inescapable embrace. He spun round, trying to catch a tree moving, but they stood silently — tall and majestic, mocking him. He spun again, then again, chasing his tail until he could spin no longer, and collapsed.
When Darkburst regained consciousness, he was weak. If he didn't find some nourishment soon, he'd never find his way out of this confusing place. After staggering to his feet, a movement caught his eye; a pine marten, running up the trunk of a nearby tree, its body undulating over the rough surface. He watched its prominent eyes flicking side to side in a constant search for danger. Pine martens sometimes reared their young in discarded crow's nests, so maybe the female was on her way to feed her kits.
As a cub, one of Darkburst's favourite pastimes was tree climbing, and he now put that experience to good use. Digging strong claws into the rough bark, he took a deep breath and followed the pine marten's musky scent. Wrinkling his snout in concentration, he scaled the trunk, knowing this was the easy bit. Getting down was going to be a lot harder. When he finally reached the crow's nest, a ferocious pine marten faced him. Intent on protecting her young, she hissed angrily, flattening her broad, rounded ears against her skull as she arched her slender body protectively over her kits.
Moving quickly, Darkburst swiped the nest from the branch, watching the pine marten and her three kits tumbled to the ground below. Although some would survive the fall, he hoped at least one dead kit would be there when he made it back down.
*
Darkburst studied the rippling reflection of the moon in the dark waters of Migaro Lake. It shone back up like a single large shimmering eye. Gazing at the reflection, his eyes widened in wonder as the silvery light coalesced into an image of his mother's face. Holding his breath, he leant closer for a better view, and his heart went out to her. She looked so weary and forlorn. Reaching out, he gently touched the surface of the water with the tip of one claw, caressing his mother's face. At his touch the likeness disintegrated, expanding outwards into ever widening ripples. Sighing heavily, he shook off the feeling of tiredness that suddenly overcame him. Turning from the lake, he began eating the hedgehog he'd killed earlier. In the calm, the churring call of a nightjar floated through the tall pine trees.
Finding a small pool of water in a nearby hollow, Darkburst took a deep drink. Hunger sated and thirst slaked, he moved in a circle, clearing a depression in the pine needles. Having journeyed such a long distance since leaving the safe confines of Brightness's sett, he felt totally worn out. Curling up on the forest floor, he closed his eyes and instantly fell into an exhausted sleep.
Darkburst stirred in his sleep, the short whiskers on his snout quivering, feet twitching. He growled quietly, lips drawing back across his teeth. He dreamt, stirring half-awake, but quickly settled again, his growls giving way to long, shallow breaths. The thick canopy far above allowed little light to penetrate, so the hollow in which he lay remained shaded and dark. As he slept, he continued to dream. Dreams of monsters; of his search for Boddaert's Magic; of Grindel and his promises; but mostly his mother.
*
Awaking from his sleep, Darkburst stretched languidly, shaking the knots from his muscles. Getting to his feet, he looked around, deciding that he must leave this confusing wood. There was no point in continuing his useless search. There was nothing here for him. First, he needed food. He would go back and check the remains of the crow's nest. He might have missed one of the pine marten's kits.
A short while later Darkburst was raking through the remains of the nest, grunting his disappointment as the search proved fruitless. A glint caught his eye — something deep in the bottom of the nest twinkling up at him. Curiosity aroused, he picked at the mixture of twigs and grasses until he freed it. The object dropped clear, bouncing onto the forest floor, rolling in ever decreasing circles. It dropped onto its side, and the world suddenly tilted, his mind reeling, every hair on his back standing erect. Lying at his feet was the legendary Circle of Claws!
Breathlessly stretching out a paw, he touched it. Thoughts of his sister sprang to mind, and a shudder ran down his spine. Ignoring the sensation, he picked up the prize, holding the magical object, studying it under the little sunlight struggling through the dense canopy. Five badger claws, the tips fused together, formed a perfect star shape. There was no doubt in his mind. This was what he'd been searching for all this time. Laying it back on the ground, Darkburst closed his eyes, raised his snout to the sky, and gave thanks to the Prime Mover for choosing him as the recipient of such a powerful possession.
Overhead the air grew heavy, the sound of thunder rumbling menacingly in the distance. Darkburst looked about uneasily as the few drops of rain turned into a sudden downpour. The storm grew closer, and the charged atmosphere brought the guard hairs on his coat erect, crackling with static energy. Building until it came from everywhere — an unexpected silence, then the brightest, almost blinding light.
Darkburst cowered as the lightning bolt seared downwards through the canopy, striking the ground in front of him. Thrown backwards, he careened into a tree and lay stunned. Shaking his head, he struggled to his feet, turning to face the shaft of sunlight now pouring through the hole burnt in the canopy. The tight beam lit the forest floor in a perfect circle.
Staggering into the circle, Darkburst saw a darkened patch of pine needles, a great scorch mark made by the lightning bolt. His heart froze. The Circle of Claws had been laying right there — right where the bolt had struck. A muted cry escaped his lips, and he rushed forward, stumbling to a stop, paw half-raised.
The Prime Mover may well have destroyed the Circle of Claws, but in its place, She had left a greater gift.
At the very centre of the circle lay a small black stone, its scintillating surface reflecting the sun's radiance in a breathtaking array of colours. Locked into the stone's flat surface was a perfect image of the Circle of Claws. It sparkled up at him invitingly, like a twinkling star stirring primitive emotions in his chest. Reaching out a tremulous paw, he picked up the stone and studied it. At the centre, where the tips of the claws met, was a small hole surrounded by a rim of tiny crystals. It was these that reflected the sunlight with such intensity.
Finding a length of stout grass, he quickly threaded it through the stone and hung it about his neck. It burrowed deeply into his fur, as though it belonged there — as though it had always been there. Its fiery warmth caressed his skin, and he felt whole.
Darkburst headed off through the trees towards Migaro Lake, full of renewed energy. He would spend some time beside the lake, resting and eating, then set out for Brockenhurst Sett with his prize.

Chapter 24

Brokin glanced over his shoulder, marvelling at how such a large body of badgers had moved into the fringes of Brockenhurst Forest without disturbing the local wildlife. Worrying at his lower lip, he wrinkled his snout. A large part of his force still lingered out beyond the boundary of the forest, gathered in a low meadow that swept down from the edge of the mountains, waiting for his order to move forward. He needed to get them under cover quickly before being spotted.
As Brokin waited for his forward scouts to report, he tapped the claws of one foot against a large stone. His impatience was obvious to those around him and they talked quietly, expectantly, their voices a soft drone in the background. His gaze wandered over the lines of badgers spread out around him. It had been hard work getting them trained to such a high standard so quickly, but somehow, against all the odds, he'd managed it.
*
On the journey back from his undercover mission to Brockenhurst Sett, Brokin had planned a scheme to meet the threat posed by Grindel. On reaching Badachro Sett, he put his proposals to the Council, who then held a private session to discuss it. More than half a moon passed before they called the young badger — so long he wondered if they ever would. Had they dismissed his plan out of order?
But finally, just as the sun began staining the sky, the message came. Brokin moved across the chamber towards the group of sombre Elders. Drac, their leader, studied him intently, searching for some enigmatic answer in Brokin's eyes.
"Brokin," Drac said in a grave tone, "the Council of Elders cannot agree on this issue and have left the final decision to me." The old badger looked uncomfortable, his one brown eye appearing almost black in the half-light. Staring out across the rocky valley floor, he continued in a quiet voice, "But I must admit right now that I'm reluctant to agree to such a proposal. It would mean the loss of so many lives."
"Far more if we don't act first," Brokin answered abruptly. "Do you really want to wait until we're attacked before you do anything? Think about what will happen if we lose this fight, and we will if we let them attack us here. We can't defend the sett, it's too spread out for that. "You know what the outcome will be, don't you? They will enslave survivors, make them work until they drop from exhaustion. How long do you think you'd last at your age? And what about your cubs? With such oddly coloured eyes, do you imagine for one moment that the Preceptor will let them live? Are you really saying you're just going to abandon all those who look to you for their safety to a murdering tyrant like that?"
Shaking his head, Drac stared at the ground. "I know, I know," he replied in a tight voice. "What you say may well be true, but think about the loss of life. How can I condone that?"
Brokin took a deep breath. Losing his temper would only anger the Elder. He needed to win him over, not alienate him.
"Badgers are going to die either way, Drac," he answered quietly. "But at least my way will give them a chance at success." Nodding at the tight group gathered around them, he continued. "Look around you. You hold all these badgers' lives in your grasp. Are you really going to let them die for no other reason than your misplaced morality? Let me take a force out to Brockenhurst Forest and attack Grindel and his hoard before they attack us first. It's the only way. We can't defend our sett here. Please listen to me."
The Elder wrinkled his snout, considering the points Brokin had made, his old mind a whirlpool of jumbled emotions. "We could always leave. Move somewhere else," he said half-heartedly. "That's a suggestion that I would find more acceptable."
"And go where!" Brokin snapped, his temper breaking through. "What badger would allow us to live anywhere near them?"
"Yes, I suppose you might be right," Drac admitted reluctantly, accepting the inevitability of the young badger's arguments. "But there'll be no unprovoked attack, understand that Brokin. Choose your fighters and train them well, but when you go to Brockenhurst Sett, it must be to negotiate, not to fight. Is that understood?"
*
The abrupt appearance of Thesa brought Brokin back from his reveries. This most trusted scout was completely black, even the skin on the inside of his ears and mouth so heavily pigmented they matched his fur. This anomaly gave the scout a distinct advantage when he was out patrolling in the darkness of a moonless sky, moving through the undergrowth like a phantom until he spoke quietly into an unsuspecting ear.
"How many?" Brokin asked quickly, referring to the number of guards posted along the track leading into Brockenhurst Sett.
The badger's sombre eyes flashed excitedly as he reported his findings. "Four, spread evenly along the main pathway. Three more nearer the sett itself," The black head swung round and his eyes focused on Brokin. "What's that?" he asked, nodding toward a body lying amongst the roots of a nearby tree.
Brokin wrinkled his snout. "He was hiding behind the tree. He jumped out and attacked me as I passed by."
It was the first time Brokin had killed a fellow badger, and loath though he was to admit it, the experience had left him shaken. Forced to fight for his life, he'd quickly countered the unexpected assault, leaving his attacker with little choice but to parry the frenzied blows being rained upon him from every direction. Stumbling backwards, Brokin's assailant did his best to dodge the swiftly moving claws as they repeatedly raked across his snout, but with little success. Sensing triumph, Brokin kept up the pressure, giving the boar little chance to recover, pushing him further backwards until he finally lost his footing on a slick stone. As the badger stumbled, Brokin darted forward, jamming his snout between the boar's front legs, powering upwards, flipping his attacker over onto his back, exposing his vulnerable belly. The hapless badger thrashed about in a vain attempt at righting himself, but Brokin made the final cutting-thrust with fully extended claws.
Killing the boar left Brokin completely deflated. When he'd been practising the killing thrust, high on his favourite ledge above Badachro Sett, he'd always imagined he would experience jubilation when he finally used it – that he would be more alive, nearer to Her. Instead, he felt cold and empty.
"Have you noticed how few guards there are about?" Thesa asked, interrupting Brokin's thoughts.
Brokin snapped the unpleasant memories away and studied the sky. "The sun will rise soon," he observed. "Perhaps they don't expect us to attack while the sun is high."
"Perhaps," the scout agreed, his voice reflecting his doubts.
Shaking off his feelings of ambivalence over the killing of the boar, Brokin gave the scout his orders. "Prepare our forces to attack at sunrise. Make sure they know what's expected of them. After that, take three of our best fighters and clear the pathway ahead of any guards you find. Wait for me in the clearing by the broken oak tree, this side of the main earthworks."
Thesa nodded, then hurried off towards the edge of Brockenhurst Forest, where the main body of Brokin's forces rested. As he disappeared, Brokin settled down to wait for the first rays of the sun, pondering the colossal responsibilities he'd undertaken, and whether he was right to go against the express wishes of the Elders.
*
Cherva made himself more comfortable in the fork of a gnarled elder tree and smiled. He'd settled in the high perch earlier, after one of his scouts reported the movement of many badgers crossing Low Meadow, amongst them boars with unusual markings. Cherva correctly surmised this was the long awaited attack from Badachro Sett.
When winter finally broke its hold on Brockenhurst Forest, the Preceptor cautioned patience when Cherva suggested they launch an attack on Badachro Sett as soon as possible. The Preceptor assured him that, given time, the troublesome badgers would come to Brockenhurst Sett, saving their own fighting force the trouble of a long trek out to Badachro, and he'd been right. Here they were, the poor fools, walking straight into a well-prepared trap. He smiled contentedly, knowing he would soon rout the invading force and raise his credibility even further in the eyes of the Preceptor. Studying the movements of the attacking force carefully, he tried to determine a pattern.
On reaching the outskirts of the forest, the long column had settled down amongst the thin covering of trees, sending a small party sent forward to scout the land. Whoever was in charge of this ragtag band of losers was certainly taking no chances. A moment of doubt clouded Cherva's eyes as it became apparent the leader of these boars wasn't stupid.
Cherva's eyes widened when he spotted the boar directing operations. It was the same badger who'd attacked him during the last summer-cycle! He'd escaped from the two guards ordered to kill him. Cherva's anger rose, but he pushed it from his mind. He needed to keep a clear head for the coming battle. Guile, not anger, was required.
As time passed, Cherva developed a grudging admiration for the diminutive leader of the opposing force. He posted guards at all the access points to the encampment, so a surprise attack would not work. Shifting his bulk to a more comfortable position, Cherva nonchalantly shrugged his shoulders. All the worry and planning undertaken by this badger and his harum-scarum band — the hard march from Badachro Sett, and the time spent training — were to no avail, because soon after they attacked, they would die. Every one of them. No badger could survive an attack on Brockenhurst Sett.
The clear liquid call of a skylark marked sun-break and Cherva nodded when the badgers encamped amongst the trees stirred and began massing behind their leader. After a few moments of confusion, the force set off in a column of threes. Better and better, Cherva thought as he watched the sudden activity. They were going to attempt a direct frontal assault during the sun-cycle. As the large band of badgers marched towards their destiny, the column passed directly beneath Cherva's hiding place and he stared down at them in contempt, picturing their lingering deaths in the coming battle.
*
Brokin halted his column when the forward scouts returned to report. The path ahead was clear, the sentries having withdrawn back to the sett at sun break. Brokin's heart lightened when he realised he'd arrived at the precise moment Cherva had changed his guards. He must use of this piece of luck. The fighters hurried along the forest pathway behind their leader, their tramping feet swirling the dry surface sky-wards. As the sky lightened and the first rays of sunlight pierced the trees with long, slender slivers of light, the wakening birds fell silent, disturbed by the activity in their midst, and throughout the forest, creatures paused, sensing some exceptional event was taking place. The more timid bolted for their holes, or quickly crawled beneath the litter on the forest floor, where they waited in silent anticipation.
In the undergrowth lining the sides of the path; in foliage topping the graceful old trees; in shallow pits dug in the forest floor — from all these places glinting eyes watched the passing badgers with a mounting excitement. As the attacking boars passed by on their way towards battle, these hidden defenders slipped quietly out of their hiding places to join with those already stalking the column from the rear. When Brokin halted his badgers at the broken oak tree, unknown to him, it trapped them between Grindel's superior forces in the sett and Cherva's boars in the rear.
When the sun finally broke free of the horizon, Brokin ordered the storming of Brockenhurst Sett, watching proudly as his fighters streamed into the openings in the high walls of the earthworks. He was confident that under Thesa's command, his brave boars would put up a strong fight. Brokin divided his forces at this point: the main body of his fighters launching a frontal assault, while a small band of specially trained boars, under his direct command, would enter the sett through the air vent at the rear.
When Thesa's force entered the ramparts, they quickly found themselves lost in a network of confusing passageways. Blundering about in a vain attempt at finding the right path out of the maze, they disorientated themselves even further. Stumbling to a halt, they looked about in confusion. Suddenly, triumphant shouts filled the air and the sett's defenders, hidden along the tops of the walls, showered rocks down on them.
The Preceptor ran back and forth amongst his garrison, striking them in his excitement, forcing them to greater efforts, even joining in the melee by rolling several stones over the edge onto the badgers below, shouting his delight when one particularly large rock smashed onto the back of a three-legged boar.
Thesa flitted into view, his black body making him almost invisible in the shadows of the high walls. Bending over the injured badger, he examined the terrible wounds, and with a thrusting slash from his sharp claws, put a swift end to the boar's unbearable pain. Thesa glared up at the figure standing on the parapet high above, hatred and anger dancing in his black eyes.
The Preceptor stared back down at the apparition, a sudden chill running along his spine. Shaking off the feeling, he frantically rolled another rock up to the edge, heaving it over with a grunt, but he was far too late. His target had already slipped away.
Thesa looked about as the stones and rocks hurtled down all around him. Already many badgers lay injured or dying, and in their panic, the rest were milling around aimlessly, which only added to their confusion and injuries. Pressed against a wall under a slight overhang, he desperately sought a way out of their plight. Staying confined in this exposed position would mean the death of them all. He must find a way out, and quickly.
Hearing a shout from an intersection further along the passageway, he hurried forward, stopping beside a bloodied boar who looked as though he was about to collapse. Too exhausted to speak, the badger pointed at a spot on the wall above his head. Rearing up on his hind legs for a closer look, Thesa's hopes revived. A small footprint scratched into the hardened surface.Dashing to the next intersection, he quickly discovered another. Could it be that some badger had marked a way through the maze?
Having little choice but to trust his deduction, Thesa stopped a passing badger and shouted above the melee, "Follow the footprints, there on the walls. Tell the others, Quickly now."
Word spread through the labyrinth that a way through had been found, and those still able to, followed the black figure along the twisting passageways, dodging the rocks falling from above. After negotiating a series of twists and turns, they finally burst out of the convoluted corridors into a large semi-circular space fronting the main entrance of Brockenhurst Sett. Unnerved by the sudden silence that had descended, Thesa looked about.
The defenders had disappeared from the walkways on top of the walls, which made him wonder what they had in store for him next. Looking over his tattered force, he realised most of the fighters who'd entered the sett were dead, or so seriously injured they couldn't fight. Those who could stood around him in a dejected group. The heavy burden of responsibility almost weighed him down. Even now, after all they'd been through, these brave badgers were looking to him to lead them to victory. They trusted him totally, and he'd let them down badly. To make matters worse, not one of Grindel's defenders had so much as received a scratch. The whole attack was an unmitigated disaster. He hoped Brokin was having better luck.
As that thought formed in Thesa's mind, the air filled with the rumble of falling rock. Brokin had breached the rear of the sett — they had a chance, after all! But all hope evaporated when an enormous group of badgers spewed from the entrance of the sett, reinforced by a yelling mob charging from the labyrinth behind, leaving them hopelessly outnumbered.
*
Early in his plans, Brokin realised that a successful attack on Brockenhurst Sett would depend far more on stealth than numbers. The defences surrounding the sett would be impossible to storm successfully without an enormous loss of life, if at all. Their only hope of success lay in, 'biting off the snake's head'. If he could infiltrate the sett and kill the Preceptor while his major force was fighting at the front, then the headless snake would quickly wither and die.
When he outlined his plan, the Elders were less than enthusiastic, preferring to negotiate. Brokin argued long and hard, pointing out the difficulties they would face in trying to defend the caves, or negotiate with such a strong force. He also faced the further problem of keeping his fighters in top form. They'd expected the Preceptor to launch his attack as soon as the winter snows melted, but it was well into summer now, and no attack had materialised. Brokin's fighters were losing their edge. If he waited much longer, they might well lose the will to fight altogether. Eventually the Elders agreed he could go Brockenhurst, but only to negotiate.
From his previous visit, Brokin knew the only weakness in the Preceptor's defences lay in the air vent he'd already penetrated. He planned to take a small group of badgers through this vent while Thesa kept the defenders busy at the main entrance. Once inside, he would find the Preceptor and kill him. That was the only form of negotiation Brokin would offer — the only form of negotiation the Preceptor would understand.
As the shouts and screams of the badgers fighting in the labyrinth echoed to him from the thick canopy overhead, Brokin moved his small group through the undergrowth parallel to the pathway leading to the air vent. This was familiar territory, and they made excellent progress. Spotting two sentries lurking in the bushes, he waved his party to a halt. Narrowing his eyes, he studied them carefully. There was no way of bypassing the guards without being seen, so they had to die — or perhaps not.
Waving his group back out of sight, Brokin readied himself with a few deep breaths. Then, when his mind was calm, stepped from the undergrowth onto the path. He walked towards the guard's position, humming loudly, as though he hadn't a care in the world. When he drew level with the guards, one broke cover and hailed him. Jumping in simulated surprise, he stumbled to a stop, and adopting his most ingratiating smile, said, "Oh, thank goodness I've found you!"
The guard, taken by surprise at the badger's apparent innocence, stared at him suspiciously. "Who are you? What are you doing here?" he demanded.
"Cherva sent me," Brokin replied, sounding hurt at the guard's gruff tone. "We're under attack at the front of the sett. Listen, can't you hear all the noise?" Hopping from foot to foot, Brokin pulled at his ear in agitation. "You must come quickly," he pleaded. "Cherva sent me to get you, and if you don't come straight away, he'll punish me horribly. You too, probably. You know what he's like."
"But we're guarding the pathway to the vent," the badger protested, wrinkling his snout at the unpleasant image Brokin had raised in his mind.
"I don't care, and nor will Cherva if you don't do as you're told. The badgers from Badachro can't possibly know about the vent back here, so there's no point in you staying here to guard it, when you're needed to help fight at the front, is there? Quickly, you're to go at once. You go on ahead and I'll let the other guards know what's happening."
The badger glanced back over his shoulder to where his companion was still standing half hidden in the undergrowth. He looked back and nodded warily. "Yes, I suppose that makes sense," he agreed reluctantly, not savouring the prospect of having to join the fighting, when he'd far rather remain at his present comfortable post.
"Well, then?" Brokin urged. "Go on, hurry, or Cherva will be down here himself. Quickly. Quickly now!"
The guard walked over to his comrade and after much pointing and gesturing at Brokin, the pair finally rushed off. Heaving a sigh of relief that his act had worked so well, he hurried back to his fighters, and the group moved off. He led the way through the trees and out across the same embankment on which he'd attacked Cherva during the last summer-cycle. It already seemed like a lifetime ago!
A short time later, the small band halted while Brokin studied the lone guard stationed just off the pathway. He shook his head in frustration, because unlike the first two, this one appeared alert. Standing behind a large rock, the guard's position gave him an unrestricted view of any approaching badger, and it was only because they'd cut across the embankment the guard hadn't spotted them.
Brokin didn't think it he could fool this guard. Unfortunately, he would have to die!

Chapter 25

Darkburst travelled for many moons, the journey becoming a dull routine. Wake from a restless sleep, get up and search for food, check which direction to take from the stars, then walk, walk, walk. Moon after moon, with no variation. But he also found a soothing comfort in these numbing patterns. While his body carried out the action of walking, his mind was free to roam, reliving his time with Brightness. It was his misfortune that this same monotony also proved his undoing. If he'd been more focused on where he was going, instead of what he'd left behind, he would have spotted the telltale sparkle of moonlight reflecting from the half-hidden object on the pathway ahead.
The first sign Darkburst knew something was wrong, was a sharp spasm of pain shooting through his leg. Shouting in surprise, he fell forward, his leg caught tightly in some creature's jaws. Blinking back tears of pain, he gasped as its grip tightened. Growling low in his throat, he curled his lips, swinging his head round to confront his attacker. To his astonishment, he found he was alone!
Rolling onto his side, he bent double to see how he'd trapped his leg. There was a strong, pliable plant stem, wrapped just above his hock. The end of this strange-looking stem was attached to a stout root buried in the ground, and no matter how hard he pulled, he couldn't free himself. Doing so only made the stem tighter until it disappeared into his flesh. He tried biting the stem, but its slippery surface was too hard for his teeth to penetrate. It was unlike any plant he'd seen — coloured starlight, cold to the touch. In desperation, he sat back on his haunches and began tugging with strong lunges backwards. The stem cut deeper, blood oozing from the wound. He stopped struggling when the thin stem sliced right into the muscle of his leg.
Licking the bloody injury, Darkburst stared at the plant stem holding him captive. How could he free himself? He'd already tried pulling the root from the ground with no success. He would have dug it out, but the slightest movement now caused so much pain he doubted he could. There was only one option.
Closing his eyes and gritting his teeth against the coming pain, Darkburst threw his full weight backwards, at the same time twisting from side to side, trying to pull the root from the ground. As a deep blackness engulfed him, stars of unbelievable agony exploded in his head.
*
Slowly regaining consciousness, Darkburst winced, trying to ease the pain coursing through his leg. Groaning, he cracked open his eyes and looked at the wound, wishing he hadn't. The movement caused the cloud of flies on the wound to buzz round his head in angry circles before settling back into the brown incrustations again. He examined the deep cut, lips curling in disgust. It was full of small white eggs!
Settling down on his side, he took deep steady breaths, letting his mind return to the ash tree and his time with Brightness. It eased the pain a little. A small smile formed on his lips. Then, sighing heavily for what might have been, he prepared for death.
*
Darkburst forced his eyes open. The sun was setting once more. It had blasted down on him relentlessly, adding to his pain. In the cool fading light of a new moon, he sought for some small hope, knowing there was none. For the first time, he noticed several small loops, similar to the one holding his leg, scattered along the pathway ahead. Other creatures had suffered the same fate. Two rabbits, one caught by the neck, obviously long dead. Further on, what looked like the remains of a chewed-off forepaw, giving mute testimony to a fox's gruesome struggles. He shuddered. Would he have the same courage when the time came?
Pushing the unpleasant image from his mind, Darkburst shook his head. It would not come to that. Already saved twice, he knew The Prime Mover was protecting him. She would save him this time, too.
But as the sky slowly darkened on yet another sun, his conviction wavered. His foot, and most of his leg, was now so swollen that the skin had split. Thankfully, it had stopped hurting some time ago, but as the moon slid its slow way across the sky, it finally dawned on him he might die in this lonely place. Belatedly wishing he'd stayed with Brightness in the safety of her sett instead of chasing his wild dreams, he plummeted into a deep depression. His thoughts turned to his mother, and he wondered if he would ever see her again. Stretching out his neck, he laid his head on the ground, closed his eyes and tried to sleep.
Just before dawn, a noise in the undergrowth brought Darkburst out of his stupor. With an effort, he raised his head, listening intently, trying to detect what had disturbed him. A faint rustling came from some nearby bushes. The rustling grew louder, and his heart beat faster. He squinted into the darkness but could see nothing in the heavy shadows. Then a new musky odour wafted towards him on the damp air. His eyes widened, the stubby whiskers on his snout standing erect in recognition. Rats! A pack of rats was moving through the undergrowth towards him. Help had come. The Prime Mover had sent the rats to help him.
As the first rat loomed out of the thick undergrowth, Darkburst struggled to his feet. The animal was enormous, its yellow eyes gazing at him. It stopped a short distance away, testing the air with quivering whiskers, its long tail curled forward, the tip slightly raised. Other rats joined it, crowding in behind. In its excitement a latecomer rushed past the others, but the lead rat snapped at it viciously, sending it squealing back into the pack where it sat licking its wound.
The larger rat moved nearer, tentatively scenting the air. Darkburst kept perfectly still, waiting to see what it would do. It moved closer, head darting side to side, constantly alert for danger. It did not approach directly, staying off to one side. It stopped a short way off, staring at him with unblinking eyes. Darkburst settled back on his haunches, relieving the pressure on his leg. As he moved, the rat flattened itself along the ground, the tips of its ears quivering as it studied him warily. It raised its rump, curling claws into the earth. Darkburst could see the tension building in its body, but was taken by surprise when the rodent unexpectedly launched itself at him.
The rats were not here to help him. They were foraging for food!
As the rat sank its teeth into his snout, its companions moved in, flanking him on either side. With a violent shake of his head, Darkburst flipped the rat away, roaring in pain as it ripped out a sizeable chunk of his skin. Back on its feet in an instant, it charged in again. Darkburst tried buffeting it away, but the rat twisted its body in mid-air, landing on Darkburst's back, its feet scrabbling in the soft fur. The other rats crowded closer, waiting for their chance.
Before the rat on his back could get a good purchase, Darkburst reared up, trying to dislodge it. His injured leg gave way, and he crashed onto his side, landing on the rat with a thump that blasted the air from his lungs. The rat squealed, scurrying away a short distance before turning back to face him again.
An excruciating pain stabbed through Darkburst's injured leg and his vision blurred. He shook his head to clear it, knowing if he fainted now, he was dead. Groaning loudly, he rolled onto his belly, panting deeply. The movement caused an immediate attack from the pack, and a vicious flurry of bodies overwhelmed him. Pulling against the plant stem in desperation, he gritted his teeth against the pain, twisting and turning this way and that, rolling over and over in his attempt to free himself. The stem cut deeper, and he screamed his rage. The rats kept up the attack, dashing in to bite him whenever the chance arose.
Then suddenly, against all expectations, he was free!
Turning on his attackers, he lashed out at the lead rat with a slashing blow. The rodent squealed loudly, the skin and muscle along its spine parting to expose the ribs beneath. It swayed on shaky legs, fear flaring in its yellow eyes. Mortally wounded, it quietly mewled to itself, slowly collapsing to the ground. The rest of the pack stopped their attack, lifting their sharp snouts, scenting their leader's demise.
Taking advantage of the confusion, Darkburst tucked his injured leg up and ran as fast as he could, pushing his way through the tangled undergrowth. He could hear excited, high-pitched squeals behind him as the pack fought over their dead leader, but it wouldn't be long before they finished their meal and set out after him.

Chapter 26

After killing the lone sentry guarding the pathway, Brokin returned to his group of fighters and together they moved up the stony track leading to the air vent at the rear of the sett. When they reached the edge of a small clearing, he called a halt, ordering them to hide in the undergrowth and wait for him. Setting off, he moved around the edge of the clearing until he spotted the air vent. Three guards were defending it.
One guard lounged inside the small tunnel; another was off to one side gathering worms; a third lay on a rock ledge next to the keystone that kept the rock pile from collapsing. He studied the situation: it was impossible to reach the tunnel without being spotted by at least one guard. Withdrawing a short distance, he considered his next move. How to get into the tunnel before the guard at the rock pile spotted him and released the keystone. A plan formed in his mind; a plan that might get him into the air vent — but it was risky.
Back at his fighters, Brokin whispered his orders. The signal to attack was the call of an injured weasel; they must distract the sentry at the keystone long enough for him to enter the tunnel, then trip the keystone. It would ensure no badger could follow and take him by surprise.
Brokin led the way back to the vantage point he'd discovered.. Keeping low, the group crawled under a narrow rock overhang. While two of the fighters gathered ferns, he took a quick look. The guard at the vent had joined his companion searching for worms. They were digging at the base of a nearby tree. He licked his lips, readying himself for the next move. A slight gesture told two badgers to arrange the ferns over his back, tying them in place with long twists of grass. Then, using the cover of the long grass, he slowly crawled towards to the vent. If the boars kept their attention on their digging, he should reach the vent with no trouble. 
Stopping often to take stock, Brokin's heart hammered so hard he could scarcely breathe. One guard gave a loud laugh, and he jumped, almost giving himself away. After a few deep breaths to control his panic, he set out again. Reaching the point where the long grass ended, he stopped and settled down for a closer look. He would have to make a dash for the vent and hope he reached it before the rocks came crashing down.
Raising his head, he made ready to give the signal, but only managed a hoarse croak. His mouth was so dry his tongue had stuck to the roof of his mouth. The boar guarding the keystone sensed something and turned, studying the undergrowth where Brokin lay hidden.
Was he spotted? Too late to worry now. Wetting his lips, he tried again and the shrill, high-pitched shriek of an injured weasel rang out across the clearing. On his signal, Brokin's fighters attacked the guards by the tree, yelling at the top of their voices to distract the badger posted at the rock pile. Breaking his cover, Brokin ran headlong towards the air vent. Everything going as planned.
 The sentry on the ledge hadn't spotted him yet… almost there… just a few more paces… his heart beat even faster… he was going to make it.
What he didn't know was another guard lounged inside the tunnel. On hearing the yelling, he lumbered to his feet and wandered outside, spotting Brokin just before he hit him headlong in the flank. Gasping for breath, the guard bellowed in surprise. Brokin grabbed the guard's ear, biting down hard, twisting his head. The guard let out another roar as his ear ripped off. Leaping backwards, he shook his head wildly, splattering Brokin with blood. Recovering his composure, the guard backed further into the tunnel, favouring his damaged ear. Brokin sensed a movement and side-stepped as one of the other guards ran in to attack him from behind.
Warily circling his attacker, Brokin cursed his luck at having lost the element of surprise. He must finish this quickly, before the guard above released the keystone. He continued moving to his left, searching for an opening, gasping in surprise when another badger landed on his back. Before he could react, the badger jumped off again. Using Brokin as a springboard, one of his fighters had jumped over his head, landing squarely on the boar in the tunnel. With a blood-curdling yell, Brokin's fighter took on an opponent twice his size with no thought for his own safety. The pair rolled over and over in the entrance, teeth and claws flashing as they grappled for a hold.
Brokin turned to the guard circling him, his thoughts on the badger guarding the keystone. Sensing his distraction, the boar lunged, catching him a stunning blow above his eye. Twisting, Brokin used the guard's own momentum to toss him aside. The boar roared, turning back to the attack. Brokin darted to one side, snapping at his adversary. Locking his jaws around the badger's leg, he threw his weight forward, twisting his head savagely, breaking the guard's leg. As the boar fell, exposing his stomach, Brokin ripped the badger's abdomen from flank to flank, dodging the steaming entrails as they slid from the fatal wound. Moving in again, he thrust a sharp claw through the badger's eye into his brain, cutting short the terrible screams.
Turning, Brokin threw a glance upwards, spotting two badgers locked in a fierce battle on the narrow ledge by the rock pile. One of his fighters had reached the keystone before the sentry had fully released it. From where he stood at the base of the rock face, he saw the dislodged keystone trembling under the weight of the rocks bearing down on it. At any moment, the entire edifice would come crashing down. There was no time left, it was now or never!
Dodging around the fighters in the vent entrance, Brokin threw himself into the narrow opening, just as a long drawn-out rumble signalled the final collapse of the rock pile. Covering his head, he cowered down, making himself as small as possible. The crashing of falling rocks went on for a long time; the air so choked he could scarcely breathe. Finally, the terrible noise subsided, and he got to his feet, spitting dust, his eyes watering. Heaving a sigh of relief, he thanked the Prime Mover he'd survived the rock fall.
Catching a movement from the corner of his eye, he glanced upwards, just as a large rock crashed down on him.
*
The Preceptor's forces charged, screaming at the tops of their voices – one group from the front, another from the rear.
"Hold fast, badgers. Think of your families and sett." Thesa's steady voice rang out above the triumphant shouts of his enemies.
Caught between the two groups, Thesa and his remaining fighters had nowhere to retreat. Hurriedly ordering his boars to form a double circle, with the strongest fighters on the outside, Thesa watched the attacking badgers thunder across the ground towards them. The charge almost overwhelmed them, but Thesa's bravery was a spur to those around him, and they repelled the first assault. The air rang with the screams and shouts of fighting boars, their changing fortunes marked by the growing bloodstains on the soil.
Thesa's courageous group continued to fight off the attacking hoard as best they could, but eventually the enemy's superior numbers won out. The heady scent of fear hung heavy in the air, as one by one, they isolated and butchered Thesa's fighters. As the first shards of sunlight touched the sky, Thesa's remaining badgers found themselves backed against a wall, a multitude of baying enemies surrounding them. They waited for the final onslaught, but it never came.
Grindel's voice boomed across the clearing. "Hold! Stand back from them. Let me through." The bellowing crowd quietened and parted.
Thesa growled low in his throat, every muscle tense, every thought aimed at killing this evil badger. Grindel stopped a short distance away — Cherva stood to one side, eyes narrowing as he studied the black apparition.
Grindel pointed to the dead bodies strewn about him. "Badger, you have proved yourself a worthy opponent. You killed many of my guards." Glancing to one side, he nodded at his fighters. "But you can't hope to win against such a force as this. Why fight to the death, when I can offer you an honourable solution?"
"I want no offers from you," Thesa growled.
"That may be true badger, but what about your fighters? Does such valiant defiance hold true for them too?" Grindel's dark eyes bored into Thesa's. "Go ahead," he continued. "Ask them. Ask them if they want to die right here, right now, knowing that they'll be throwing their lives away for nothing." Grindel shook his head and sighed gently. "See sense, my friend. It's over. You've done all you can."
Thesa looked at his remaining fighters, seeing the weariness in their eyes, the defeat in their stance. They had fought well, had suffered heavy losses, had given everything they could. "You will let us go?" he asked. The Preceptor nodded. "How do I know you're telling the truth?"
"Why should I lie?" Grindel countered. "Your fighters are no threat now. They can return to their sett."
"And me?" Thesa's disdain suggested that he already knew the answer.
Grindel laughed lightly, wrinkling his snout. "Well friend, you're a little different," he admitted. "You'll always be a threat to me, won't you? Badgers like you don't forget. No, if I let you go, you'd eventually grow dissatisfied and try to challenge me again." A meaningful pause followed. "At least, as you are now!"
"As I am now?" Thesa's stomach churned, wondering what the Preceptor meant.
Grindel held out a paw, extending the claws. The sunlight reflected from their burnished surfaces as he flexed them. "You're too good with these," he whispered throatily. "Far too good. However, should you agree…?" he let the sentence hang, watching Thesa's reaction closely. Would the black badger accept his offer, or would he choose a hero's death? "Declawing?" he prompted.
There had been no declawing in Brockenhurst Sett for generations, and Grindel wasn't sure how his fighters might react if he carried out the threat — another problem for Cherva. It was worth the risk, however. Such an impressive punishment would ensure no badger ever challenged him again. It would be a suitable mark of his new authority over Boddaert's Realm, giving him the respect he deserved.
Thesa's mind was a maelstrom of emotion as he considered the Preceptor's offer. If he allowed this depraved badger to de-claw him, his remaining fighters would live. If he didn't, they would all die right now. A feeling of utter hopelessness swept over him. Thesa slowly nodded — the pain would be good; its brightness would cleanse him. His friends had fought valiantly at his side, had done far more than he could have possibly hoped for. This would be his tribute to them. His pain would be his homage to their bravery.
Grindel cast the defeated boar a look of utter disdain, and without a backward glance, headed for his chambers. Cherva stalked forward to carry out the Preceptor's wishes.
Thesa's heart beat even faster, and with a renewed determination, he struck out.

Chapter 27

Brightness lay beneath the canopy of the slender ash tree that had been her only companion throughout the long, lonely moons since Darkburst left. She smiled a soft, secretive smile and touched her swollen belly lightly, aware that now, no matter where her love went, there would always be a small part of him here. Rising slowly, she made her way into the sett, negotiating the short tunnel into the sleeping chamber slowly, for she was heavy in cub. Crossing to the pile of fresh leaves she'd dried over the past few moons, she lay down with a contented sigh. She was tired and closed her eyes, letting her thoughts lull her into a comforting sleep. Soon the rhythmic sound of her breathing filled the cosy chamber.
As Brightness slept, she tossed and turn restlessly, causing the keepsake Darkburst had hung about her neck to sway back and forth across her chest. She flicked her head sharply, as though trying to dislodge an annoying insect. The movement caused the Talisman to swing in a shallow arc. It landed on her head with a soft thump. Not awakening, she fluttered her eyelids, then turned her head and fell into a deeper sleep.
Brightness began dreaming, moaning softly as vivid scenes filled her mind — Darkburst trapped by his leg; fighting off a pack of rats; shrieking in agony as a large yellow-eyed beast tore his flesh. She whickered urgently, her paws trembling as she ran to help him, throwing herself onto the creatures. But the phantoms were as insubstantial as any mist, and she fell, landing awkwardly on the hard ground, twisting her leg beneath her. The sharp pain woke Brightness instantly. Her heart pounded, and her breath pumped through her open mouth. The images persisted for some time, and it took her a moment to realise that it had been a dream.
Standing up, she gasped as her leg almost collapsed beneath her, sending a lancing pain down to the tips of her claws. When she examined it, she could see nothing wrong, no reason for it to hurt like it did. She decided it was cramped. Taking a moment to let the last vestiges of the dream to slip away, she tested her leg again. Good, the cramp had subsided, so she headed for the surface.
Brightness hunted up some food, hoping that it would take her mind off the disturbing dream that still circled at the edges of her mind.
*
Darkburst collapsed to the ground, unable to run any further. Seeing the rats were no longer chasing him, he gave a grateful sigh. They were hopefully still too busy devouring their unexpected meal to bother about him. As he rested, thoughts of Brightness teased the edges of his mind. He pushed them aside. There was still too much danger to let his mind wander.
Lying on his side, he examined his injured leg carefully. What he saw horrified him. The loop that trapped him so painfully had stripped the skin and muscle from the lower part of his leg, leaving the bone exposed. Breath hissing through gritted teeth, he studied the terrible wound, realising just how bad it was. Feeling a little light-headed, he closed his eyes and took a few deep breaths, steadying his churning stomach. He tried licking the encrusted surface, but that proved too painful. If only his mother was here, she would know what to do, how to treat such a terrible wound.
After a long rest and a few mouthfuls of grass, Darkburst decided he must press on back to Brockenhurst Sett. Gathering his strength, he struggled to his feet and resumed his journey, hobbling on three legs as best he could. He made slow progress, cursing frequently. Taking direction from the stars, he limped through the rest of the moon and half of the next sun without resting. Finally forced to stop, he collapsed beneath a thicket, unable to stagger another step; his leg throbbing with such intensity he could scarcely think of anything else.
Darkburst lay for two moons before struggling on with the journey, stopping often to assuage his growing thirst. On the third moon he tried eating a fat worm he stumbled across, but vomited so violently the stars span wildly about his head. As the infection raged through his body, he became delirious, his thoughts wandering off in all directions. Twice he became convinced he'd backtracked, and retraced his footsteps, only to lose himself again.
Another moon passed — another sun – another moon – on and on. Half-crazed, he topped a ridge and fell down the far side, screaming when he landed on his injured leg. Rolling over, he staggered to his feet, laughing when he saw the ridiculous appendage attached to his body. Twice the size of a normal leg, the bare skin stretched to bursting and tinged a soft green. He poked it, grinning when the skin split further. He felt extremely weak, just about able to keep standing. A memory nudged him. He grabbed frantically, urging it to grow and replace the constant pain. And there it was — an image of Brightness as he'd last seen her, standing by her sett beneath the slender ash tree.
Trying to clear his head, Darkburst looked around and spotted the remains of an old tree stump on top of the rise. Gritting his teeth, he struggled up the steep slope. There was rotting wood up there, and where there was rotting wood, fungi grew. Reaching the top, he rested for a moment, then staggered his way along the brow of the hill. He'd almost reached the stump when the ground became waterlogged. He struggled on, eyes fixed on the stump, feet pulling from the muddy morass with soft squelches. Before he'd gone far, he began sinking, sucked into the clinging mire. The cold mud invaded the soft under-fur of his belly, dragging him deeper. He screamed for help, knowing there would be no badger to hear him. He'd sunk up to his chest, and each time he moved, sank a little further, but it was impossible not to struggle., adding to his demise.
Out of nowhere, two badgers appeared at the edge of the waterlogged hollow. "Thank Homer you've come! Help me get out of here," he shouted, but the entreaties drew no response from the pair. "Quickly. I'm sinking. Don't just stand there, help me!" Shocked, he suddenly realised they had no intention of helping. "What is it? What do you want? Why won't you help me?"
"Why should we?" one badger answered, his lips twisted into an ugly grin. "If we did that, then we'd only have to kill you afterwards. Far better you drown right there, it'll save us a lot of trouble."
They were going to watch him drown! The realisation brought a deep sadness and overwhelming anger. He would never see his beloved Brightness again, nor spend another winter cycle snug beneath the ash tree, safe in her small sett. Lowering his head, Darkburst gave up his struggles and closed his eyes.
Something nudged him under his jaw. He glanced down. It was the Circle of Claws floating on the surface of the thick mud. Biting through the grass cord, he ripped the enigmatic object from his neck and lobbed it onto the ground in front of the two badgers. "Then at least take this to Grindel. He's been waiting for it. Tell him Darkburst found it in the Dead Forest."
Picking up the stone, one badger examined it carefully, turning it over between his paws. He passed it to his companion and walked nearer to the edge of the mud pit. "Did you say your name's Darkburst?" When he nodded, the pair burst into activity. Collecting twigs and leaves from around the edge of the mire, they threw them on top of the mud. One badger then held his companion's tail, while the other edged his way towards Darkburst. "Here take hold of this in your teeth," he said, holding out a stout branch. Once Darkburst had a firm grip, they pulled him out.
"I'm Rooten, and this is Comfrey. We're guards from Brockenhurst Sett. We were patrolling around the meadow here when we heard your shouts."
Comfrey studied the muddy boar suspiciously. "And you say your name is Darkburst?" he asked.
Darkburst nodded his head urgently. "Yes." Why did they doubt him? And why had they been prepared to let him die in the mud pit? His mind was a whirl of confusing questions.
Comfrey beckoned his companion to one side, then keeping a wary eye on the bedraggled, mud splattered stranger, whispered in an undertone. "But this can't possibly be the Darkburst the Preceptor was talking about. Look at his fur."
Rooten nodded his agreement. "Yes, I know," he whispered back. "Did you see what happened? When he took this thing from around his neck, his coat turned white. It's unbelievable!" Poking the stone with an extended claw, the bewildered badger shook his head, concern lining his snout. "I don't like this. There was no talk of this badger having such powers. If this really is him, we could be in great danger. Who knows what he'll do after the way we treated him."
As the two guards talked in heated whispers, Darkburst removed the mud from around his wound. His leg smelt terrible, like decaying flesh left too long in the sun. He cleaned it as best he could with long licks, but had only been working for a few moments when he paused, his eyes widening in surprise. Lowering his leg, he stared at it, then urgently parted the coarse outer hairs with a trembling claw, peering closely at the soft undercoat beneath. His heart skipped a beat and his breath faltered. His coat was pure white!
His mind raced, and he scrabbled about on his flanks, checking everywhere he could reach. There was no mistake, his fur was now a brilliant white. He knew he was born an albino, but it was still a thorough shock to realise that somehow he'd reverted. How had this happened? It made no sense. Closing his eyes, he nipped his skin with his front teeth, just in case he was hallucinating, but when he opened his eyes the white fur was still there.
Comfrey came back, ill at ease to be standing so close. He nodded at the wound. "What's wrong with your leg? Can you walk?"
Darkburst nodded. "I think so. If you help me."
The trio set out along the winding path towards Brockenhurst Sett, the two guards supporting Darkburst, even though they were reluctant to touch him, afraid that having contact with the stranger might somehow taint them. He limped along between the two guards, his spirits rising considerably when they finally reached the outskirts of Brockenhurst Sett.
Darkburst stopped, taking it all in, giving the guards a moment's panic before they realised he was taking a brief rest. It was a bright, clear night; moonlight shimmering between the trees, reflecting from the damp bark in a thousand tiny sparkles. The grass heads nodded at him, welcoming him back, undulating away in silver-green wavelets as the gentle breeze caressed them. His heart soared as he finally stepped beneath the moon-speckled canopy, scenting the trees with deep breaths. He was home; safe in the forest's embrace. Having done as Grindel asked, he could rest.
Comfrey swore loudly when the stranger collapsed into an untidy heap between them. Leaning over, he put his ear to the badger's chest and listened carefully. Shaking his head, he looked up at his companion and wrinkled his snout.
"What's the matter with him?" Rooten asked, even though he knew the answer.
"He's dying," Comfrey responded. "We may as well leave him here and take what he gave us back to the Preceptor. There's no sense in dragging him all the way back to the sett when he'll be dead before we get there."
*
In the chambers below Fire Rock, Grindel paced back and forth with angry strides. "Where is he?" he growled.
Cherva shook his head, favouring the ragged slash extending down the length of his snout with his paw. "I don't know, Preceptor. After he did this to me, he ran off towards the sett entrance, killing two of my guards on the way." Cherva's voice shook with indignation, and he took a deep breath to steady it. "I have every spare guard searching the sett right now. They have orders to kill the boar on sight."
"NO!" Grindel's voice rebounded from the smooth walls of the strangely shaped chamber. "I want him alive. I have plans for that boar. Do not kill him."
As Cherva left the chamber to carry out his orders, Grindel sat back on his haunches, thinking about the satisfaction he would have killing Thesa. Declawing was too easy for him. He smiled slowly. No, he would revive the old punishment and bury him alive under rocks. Picking over a pile of fat worms collected for him earlier, he chose the most succulent. Eating, he made plans for the completion of his takeover of Boddaert's Realm.

Chapter 28

Without a second thought, the guards abandoned Darkburst to his fate and hurried back to Brockenhurst Sett, eager to receive the reward for the curious stone they carried. As they hurried along the moon dappled pathways, they nodded at the occasional badgers they met, glad to hear the news Cherva's fighters had beaten the attackers from Badachro. Perhaps now things would get a little better. They were excited, seeing the opportunities for advancement, discussing whether to volunteer for the fighting forces. Such a move would bring many advantages. There had been talk of new tunnels being dug to cater for the greater numbers living there, but nothing had come of it yet. Rumours circulated fighters would get the pick of these tunnels when they were dug.
It was Rooten's first guard duty with Comfrey, and they'd certainly struck lucky. Cherva would recompense them well for what they'd found. When the two friends reached the sett, they made their way to the Grand Chamber, where Comfrey handed the stone to the guard at the entrance, requesting an audience with the Preceptor. As they waited, Rooten looked around the roomy chambers, wrinkling his snout, wondering what it would be like to wield such power. He smiled, if they were lucky and fought well, they would find out.
The guard returned and ushered them through a short tunnel into the Grand Chamber. Comfrey and Rooten crossed the enormous expanse of floor, stopping before the most powerful badger in Boddaert's Realm. The ever-present giant, Cherva, stood at the Preceptor's side, staring at them. His snout had a fresh scar running down one side, still outlined in congealed blood. His right eye was closed and sunken, as though the socket was empty.
The pair jumped when the Preceptor's gravelly voice boomed out at them. "Where did you find this?" He prodding the stone with his paw.
Rooten glanced at Comfrey, but his friend didn't respond. He coughed uneasily and licked dry lips. "From a badger drowning in the marsh, Preceptor. Out beyond the hawthorn stand, across Low Meadow."
Grindel turned the object over and studied the reverse side. It was a duplicate of the first. The delicate outlines of the claws easily discernible against the darker background of the stone. His heart beat faster as he took in the significance of what he held, but he hardly dared let himself hope. He needed further proof!
He glowered at the frightened badgers standing before him. "Who was this badger?" he snarled.
Comfrey moved uncomfortably under the Preceptor's glare, keeping his eyes cast to the floor. "He said his name was Darkburst, Preceptor."
Grindel smiled and nodded. So the young badger had succeeded after all, but he'd never doubted that he would. Then a wrinkle distorted his snout as a sudden thought clouded his mind. Why hadn't the youngster come to present this remarkable stone to his benefactor himself?
"Where is this badger?" Grindel snapped, a tight fear gripping his heart.
Rooten flinched at the Preceptor's tone and looked to Comfrey for support. Finding none, he noisily swallowed his fear. "We left him on the forest path, Preceptor." Sensing they had somehow made a terrible mistake, he hurried on, tripping over his words. "The boar was dying. We saw no sense in dragging him all the way back here."
"You left him to die?" It was an accusation, not a question. The almost tearful Rooten nodded miserably. Grindel's shouts reverberated around the Grand Chamber. "Guards," he yelled at the top of his voice. "Get in here right now and take these two idiots out of my sight."
Two guards quickly appeared at the entrance, but as they crossed the chamber and began dragging the unfortunate pair out, Grindel stopped them. "No, wait. Better still, confine them to a chamber. I'll take them to the marsh in Low Meadow later and throw them in myself." Having dismissed the pair from his mind, Grindel turned his attention to Cherva. "Get a message to Soffen," he instructed. "Tell her I want to see her here, right away. Quickly now, it may already be too late."
Cherva pushed his way passed the two burly guards, who were still dragging the pair of terrified badgers from the chamber, heading off towards the lower levels of the sett where Soffen had her tiny sleeping space. As he hurried along, he replayed the scene he'd just witnessed in his mind's eye, trying to work out what significance the stone might have. From the way Grindel handled it, the object had significant importance.
Cherva entered Soffen's small chamber and looked about. It felt cold and empty, as though unoccupied for a while. Shuddering, he hurried out, searching the small living spaces spread along the tunnel, questioning every badger living there. He got the same slow shake of the head. No, they hadn't seen her for quite some time, and didn't know where she might be.
Cherva's search became more and more frantic as he ran from chamber to chamber, his heart pounding when he realised she'd disappeared. Gathering some guards together, he sent them out to scour the sett, pacing back and forth in agitation. Where had the sow got to? She had to be here somewhere. No badger could have left the sett without his knowledge.
*
Brokin tried to open his eyes, but failed. Gunk glued them shut. Trying again, he opened them part way, and groaning softly, ran his tongue around the inside of his mouth. Slowly his eyesight returned, and the rocky floor shimmered into view. He lay with his head twisted back at an awkward angle. It pounded as though some badger was jumping up and down on it. It felt like it was being hit with a big branch. Wait, something had hit him. A rock.
Suddenly it all came rushing back — the fight with the guards; the collapse of the stone pile above the entrance; the flying rock that struck him. No wonder he felt so bad! How long had he been lying here? His stiffness told him a long time.
He tried sitting up, but stopped when the floor swam in and out of focus. After resting awhile, the pounding in his head eased, and he stumbled to his feet. He was alone, which meant none of his fighters had made it through. Shaking the dust from his coat, he winced and leant against the wall, letting his eyesight catch up with his movements. Gradually things stopped rolling and he could move without feeling his head was about to fall off. Raising a paw, he examined the wound, wincing at the sharp pain lancing down his neck. He could feel the dried blood matting his fur, and the long jagged cut left by the rock.
Feeling a lot steadier, he set out along the tunnel, hoping he still had time to complete his plan.
*
Brokin looked down into the Grand Chamber from his high perch in the air vent. Dare he jump? No, it was too far. If he jumped from this height, he would seriously injure himself.
Somehow he had to find a way down. He had no choice. He couldn't return through the vent because stones blocked the way out. Looking over the edge, he tried to see some way to descend. Hearing approaching voices, he withdrew, keeping the chamber in view. As Grindel and Cherva entered, the giant taproot trembled. All three looked towards the roof.
"That's some storm building up out there," Cherva observed above the noise of the crashing thunder penetrating the sett with hollow rumbles.
Brokin realised that being able to hear the storm in the chamber meant it was directly overhead. The next peal of thunder brought a fine layer of dust drifting down from the roof. The next shook the walls.
"I've sent three badgers to fetch Darkburst, as you instructed. They should be back soon," Cherva told Grindel when the thunder quietened a little.
"I hope it's not too late," Grindel replied angrily. "How could those two idiots have been so stupid? I mean, to leave him alone like that?" He slapped the ground with his paw. "And now this storm. I want those two to die slowly, Cherva. Slowly, do you understand?" Cherva nodded as the Preceptor continued. "I want them to suffer a great deal before they die!"
"As you wish, Preceptor," Cherva agreed. "But what is it…" He faltered, leaving an uneasy silence
"Carry on," Grindel growled, sensing his guard's discomfort.
"Forgive me, Preceptor," Cherva apologised in his most ingratiating tone, "but I was wondering why this badger is so important to you?"
Grindel stared at his second-in-command. For a long moment, the air was heavy with tension. He gave a slight nod. "I suppose there's no harm in you knowing. I'll need your help anyway, so it's best I tell you now." Grindel paused, unconsciously sucking air through his teeth as he considered his next words. "You'll have heard of Boddaert's Magic?" Cherva nodded. "The youngster, Darkburst, brought that to me. At least an important part." Cherva did his best not to react, but his eyes gave him away. Grindel chuckled. "Yes, he brought me Boddaert's Magic. Imagine that." Grindel stared off into the distance, then refocussed back on Cherva. "Just one more piece of the puzzle and I'll have all the power I could ever want." Curling the claws of one foot, he beamed. "I'm almost ready to put my final plans into action at last." The Preceptor's eyes lit with an inner energy that Cherva had never seen before, and a shiver ran down his back. "I'm on the verge of total domination, Cherva. Total power. I just need that one last piece of the puzzle."
As the Preceptor's hoarse whispers floated up to Brokin, he shifted uneasily. He must stop this evil badger before it was too late.
Cherva's heart beat faster at Grindel's words, and he savoured the power that would come to him once the Preceptor had Boddaert's Magic in his possession. "And the last piece of the puzzle?" he asked in a husky voice. "Do you know where that is, Preceptor?"
"No, but Darkburst will," Grindel answered with certainty.
Once again the Grand Chamber trembled with the force of the thunder crashing overhead, and the giant taproot creaked a protest as the winds roared in from the north.
"I'm going to prepare for Darkburst's arrival. Bring him straight to me when he does. And the Healer, I want her too, I'll need her skills when the youngster gets here. From what those two idiot guards told me, he's probably in a bad way." Chuckling throatily the Preceptor let a slight sneer touch his lips as he turned away, swinging his head back when Cherva mumbled something under his breath. "What was that?" he growled suspiciously.
Cherva licked his lips nervously. "I said the Healer is missing Preceptor. The guards are scouring the sett for her now."
Grindel wrinkled his snout and stared hard at the floor, the large artery in his neck throbbing in time to his quickening heart-rate. Walking towards the entrance tunnel, he stopped and glared back at Cherva for a moment. "Never mistake my generosity as weakness Cherva," he growled, "That would be a big mistake. Find her and quickly." A long pause ensued, during which the two badgers stared at each other, then Grindel abruptly turned and left the chamber. 
With the Preceptor's words still ringing in his ears, Cherva heaved a sigh of relief that he'd taken Soffen's disappearance so well. He hurried away to extend the search.
Finding himself alone in the Grand Chamber, Brokin eased his head out and looked around. Another clap of thunder rent the air, this time shaking the chamber so violently a large piece of rock fell from the roof, hitting the floor with a dull thud. Another thunderclap and Brokin shuddered, watching the taproot writhe as the force of the storm battered the tree's old trunk. From behind him came a loud rumble as part of the vent tunnel collapsed. He had to move or chance being buried alive.
Swinging himself out over the edge, he dug the claws of his back feet into the wall and began easing himself down, trying to ignore the fluttering in his belly as he glanced towards the floor, so far below. If I fall now… He tried not to complete the thought, easing himself down. Part way to the floor, his claws slipped through the packed earthen wall, and before he could react, began slithering down the sheer drop at an ever-increasing speed.

Chapter 29

After rolling a large rock into place across the shallow chamber opening, the guards departed, leaving Rooten and Comfrey in total darkness, their hopes of a reward completely dashed.
"This is your fault." Comfrey protested. "I should never have listened to you. I told you we should leave that stupid badger to die in the mud. But would you listen?"
The guards had taken them to the lowest regions of the sett, locking them in a small, dark chamber. Before they left, they said they'd return before the moon's end to carry out the Preceptor's orders.
"It's as much your fault as mine," Rooten snapped back into the darkness. "If you hadn't frozen like some frightened cub up there. If you'd only supported me, things might have turned out different… that's all I'm saying." Snorting his anger at his friend's behaviour, Rooten took a deep shuddering breath and tried to calm his thrumming nerves. Being treated so roughly by the guards had shaken him. "Anyway," he continued, "it was you that suggested we leave that poor badger to die in the forest, not me. So it's hardly my fault, is it? I told you we should try to get him back here."
Comfrey didn't answer, he was too busy trying to make out what the gentle rustling noise he'd just heard was.
"And another thing. What about that…" Comfrey's ringing scream cut short his complaints. "What's the matter with you?" he shouted, still trembling from the shock.
"S-s-something just t-touched me," Comfrey stammered in an urgent whisper. "There's something else in here with us."
Rooten was about to berate his friend, when something brushed the tip of his ear. It wasn't Comfrey, because his friend was standing on his other side. He tried to warn Comfrey, but could only stammer. "Ah… ah… hah… ahhhh…" His groans of terror grew in direct proportion to his fertile imagination, which quickly pictured all kinds of horrors loose in the chamber with them. Hastily backing away from the unseen danger lurking in the darkness, he finally fetched up against a rock wall and could back away no further.
"It's all right. Don't be frightened. I won't hurt you," a quiet voice said. The voice floated to them out of the darkness, and though they couldn't see the badger who'd spoken, the voice sounded friendly enough. They relaxed a little.
"You're a badger!" Rooten said, stating the obvious, voice rising to an indignant squeak. "Why didn't you say you were here straight away, instead of frightening the life out of us like that? By Homer, you almost scared me to death!"
"Well, I didn't want to frighten you," the voice explained reasonably.
"Didn't want to frighten me?" Rooten exploded. "Didn't want to frighten me? What did you think touching me like that would do?"
"I'm sorry," was the soft reply. "I just assumed that you knew I was here."
"I would have scented you straight away, if Rooten hadn't been complaining so much and it wasn't so damp and stuffy down here," Comfrey complained self-righteously.
"Yes, of course you would," Rooten responded sarcastically.
"What are you doing here, anyway? Are they going to kill you too?" Comfrey asked the stranger in a quiet voice, trying to steer the conversation away from his embarrassing behaviour.
He gave a short, bitter laugh."I slipped in here to hide when I heard you coming. I thought you'd walk right by the chamber, but the guards pushed you in and blocked the entrance. I didn't think it would end with the three of us trapped here."
"Who're you hiding from?" Comfrey responded. "And what are…"
"Be quiet for a moment, Comfrey. Let him speak," Rooten admonished his friend.
Comfrey mouthed a few unintelligible words, then lapsed into a sulky silence.
"Now," Rooten took over, "why not start by telling us your name?"
"Thesa," was the reply.
"Yes, I thought as much," Rooten mused. "You're the badger that escaped after the battle, aren't you?"
"Yes," Thesa said. "I've been hiding down here, wondering what to do. I've been trying to find a way out, but there's been so many badgers coming and going I couldn't take the chance on moving about the upper tunnels. I was exploring along here when I heard you coming."
"You mean you've been hiding down here ever since the battle finished?"
An uneasy silence fell across the chamber as Rooten's question brought back memories of the terrible debacle that Thesa and his fighters had suffered.
*
"What's that?" Comfrey's urgent whisper brought Thesa back to the present. "I can feel something ruffling my fur."
"It's a draught!" Rooten exclaimed.
"Yes, I can feel it too," Thesa agreed. "It's coming from behind us. Come on."
The three badgers stumbled their way across the small chamber, following the air current.
Rooten bumped into Thesa when the boar unexpectedly stopped. Thesa cursed softly and Rooten backed off.
"Look, over there. Can you see it?" Comfrey's voice squealed with excitement.
"What?" Rooten mumbled, still shaken by the smell of blood hovering about Thesa.
"Look straight ahead, it's an opening. Can't you see the light shining through?"
When the trio neared the point of light, the air became fresher.
"Comfrey's right. Look, it is a hole!" Rooten shouted excitedly. "Maybe we can use it to get out."
Thesa shook his head, then realising the others couldn't see him, said, "No, it's much too small."
"Wait." Rooten ran his paw around the small opening. "Maybe. Yes, there's a jumble of stones covering it. If we move them, I think we might make a hole big enough to squeeze through. Come on, help me dig."
Some time later, while they were resting, Thesa heard a gentle, almost tentative cough, followed by Rooten's low voice. "Tell me something, Thesa," he said. "Why did you decide to fight to the end like you did and not take up the Preceptor's offer?"
Thesa considered the question for a time, not really sure why he'd chosen to gamble his life so recklessly. "I don't know," he finally replied. "It just seemed the right thing to do."
