Comfrey picked at a small flint that had become lodged between the pads of his foot and snorted. "You know, I wouldn't admit this to many badgers, but I admire you for what you did up there. Attacking Cherva that way." He chuckled delightedly. "The look on his face. It was really something to see!"
Rooten grunted his agreement in the darkness. "You took me by surprise. I didn't know a badger could move that fast. And the way you killed those two guards when you ran into the sett."
"What happened to the others after I left?" Thesa asked, not sure he really wanted to know.
"Oh, the Preceptor eventually let them go," Comfrey answered. "After de-clawing them first, that is. He said it was a fair punishment in the circumstances."
Thesa shuddered at the pain his friends must have suffered because of his refusal to submit. "What about Cherva?" he asked.
"You really hurt him," Rooten answered with a chuckle. "And a good thing, too. I never have liked that boar. Always telling us what to do. It's about time some badger put him in his place."
"Yes," agreed Comfrey, "it really tore his snout. Ripped right down its length. I heard that he even lost one eye."
"Come on then, let's get back to work," Thesa ordered, not comfortable with the fact he felt so pleased at inflicting such injuries on a fellow badger — even one as sadistic as Cherva.
The chamber quickly filled with soft grunts and the chinking of stone on stone as they worked.
*
"Thesa. Thesa, look out!"
Thesa looked up at the urgent shout, just in time to see a large stone dislodge itself from above him. It struck his head and he staggered, his legs turning shaky. He should have been concentrating on what he was doing, instead of letting his mind wander back to the battle. The thought dimmed, and he slumped to the floor.
Rooten bent over, shaking Thesa's inert body.
"Is he alright?" Comfrey asked.
"I think he's just dazed. Quickly, help me get that stone out of the way," Rooten responded.
Together, they rolled the stone aside, glancing at each other nervously when they spotted the blood oozing from Thesa's ear.
Rooten sat back on his haunches, hardly hearing his friend's words as he watched the red pool of blood growing beside the black badger's head. The boar wasn't just dazed, but seriously injured.
"Come on, leave him there. We can't do anything for him now."
"But…"
"Look," Comfrey berated his friend, "it's not our fault, is it? If he'd been more careful, this wouldn't have happened to him, would it? Come on, the guards might have heard all the noise. Let's get out of here while we can."
With a last glance at Thesa, Rooten tutted, shook his head, then followed Comfrey, squeezing his way through the hole they'd made.
*
Thesa groaned, easing himself to his feet. Standing in the centre of the small chamber, he staggered. His head pounded, and his ear felt like it had been half-torn off. He shook his coat, choking on the dust rising from his matted fur. The echoes of his coughing bounced back to him, overlapping with such complexity it was confusing. When the echoes subsided, he realised they were coming from the hole they'd made. It sounded like twenty coughing badgers waited on the other side, which meant there must be a large chamber there. Poking his head into the opening, Thesa saw a diffused radiance at the end of a short tunnel.
What could make light so far underground? He was frightened and very wary. The shimmering light brought with it cubhood memories; of times spent alone in his sleeping chamber, when he'd been too frightened to stretch out his paw from his bed of leaves in case some hidden monster might grab it. Dismissing such adolescent thoughts, he smiled, pushing into the tunnel.
The hole was small, but so was Thesa. Easing out the other side, he found himself on a narrow ledge. Far beneath was a large pool of water. It was this that lit the chamber with a soft glow. Other than jumping, he could see no way off the ledge. The others must have done so, or they'd still be here.
The surface of the pool pulsed with an eerie glow, looking anything but inviting. He studied it intently, his attention caught by the colours swirling across its surface. He'd seen such colours before, in a bright sunlit sky, following a heavy storm.
He saw a movement deep in the water. Something was down there. It was too hazy to make out with any clarity, but looked like a miniature moon. It rose to the surface. Heart pounding, he watched it clear the surface, spinning on its axis. Blinking rapidly, he tore his gaze from the object, spotting two shapes floating on the far side of the pool. Comfrey and Rooten, obviously dead!
Badgers are excellent swimmers, so why had they drowned? The drop from the ledge to the pool wasn't far enough to kill. Thesa shuddered, wrinkling his snout as one of the floating bodies slowly sank, leaving a gentle ripple. He checked again to see if he could find a way off the ledge. Finding none, he turned towards the hole. Better to wait in the small chamber for the guards to return, than take the chance of ending up like his two dead companions.
"Thesa," the soft whisper came from nowhere and everywhere. Thesa hunched his shoulders, as though expecting a blow to land across his back. When the voice addressed him again, his skin puckered, and his limbs trembled. "Thesa, turn around and look at me," it ordered. Thesa didn't want to look, but turned reluctantly, afraid of what he would see. "Don't be afraid," the voice reassured him. "We mean you no harm."
Thesa opened his eyes and gasped, his breath catching in the back of his throat. As he took in the scene, the blood in his veins pounded so hard his ears sang. A heavy weight filled his stomach, and the tip of his stubby tail trembled uncontrollably.
The surface of the pool was a brilliant blue; the colour of a hot sun-cycle sky. The orb had risen, now hanging near the roof, casting a powerful light into every crevice. Eyes wide, he watched the faint marks on its surface grow more prominent, curling and merging until the face of an attractive badger looked out at him.
She smiled a warm greeting, much as his mother would when particularly pleased with something he'd done She spoke, her voice coming from the surrounding rocks; the depths of the pool; deep inside his head. "We need your help, Thesa." Her voice caressed his fears, and his trembling stopped. "We hoped these two would be powerful enough. It was their misfortune they were not."
Thesa glanced at the pool, in time to see the second body slip into the depths.
"You are a resilient boar. You've proved that in battle. Are you also a moral one, Thesa?"
The unblinking eyes — the colour of the blackest sky — pierced his mind. "We have favoured you, Thesa. Like one of our own. Now it is your turn to favour us. Don't be afraid. "My name is Soffen, I won't harm you."
The orb turned a little, allowing a new face to appear. "And this is Brock — and here, Grey — and here, Skelda." The sphere continued rotating, showing Thesa many other badgers. As each passed, it studied him intently, as though trying to unravel his psyche. "Listen to me carefully," Soffen urged. "You must leave here and search out your Yang. Skelda will guide you."
"My Yang?"
"Yes, Thesa, your sun. You must find your sun, and together with your moon, they will forge a new beginning from the flames of the old."
"I don't understand," he said. "What is it you want me to do?"
"You must help us, Thesa."
The sphere turned until the one called Skelda looked down on him. "You must help me, Thesa. I have done much wrong, made many mistakes, have yearned for things that I should have. It's too late for me to put these wrongs right, but you can, if you have a mind too. I have unleashed forces that threaten the whole of Badgerdom."
Come immerse yourself in us," Soffen's voice said as her face came into view once more.
"You want me to throw myself into the pool?" A raw fear gripped his mind. The very idea locked his body into immobility.
The sphere suddenly dimmed and dropped towards the water, where it disappeared beneath the surface. Thesa looked over the edge of the ledge, staring at the colours far below, his mind and body fused rigid with terror, trying to convince himself that this was a dream, a hallucination, the result of the rock hitting his head.
*
Thesa's fall lasted forever. He hit the water with a resounding splash, knocking the breath from his body. Sinking beneath the surface, the cold liquid washed the scab from his wound, turning the water a translucent red. He reached the surface, gasping for breath, the numbing coldness of the water sucking the air from his lungs and stinging his eyes. He began a desperate swim for the edge of the pool, his feet paddling furiously, long bubbles of air following each stroke.
Behind him the line of blood twisted away, its end swirling down into the depths, where it melded with the slowly turning orb. Unaware that his lifeblood had given power to the forces beneath him, was in fact draining the very essence from his body, Thesa paddled on, his eyes fixed on the edge of the pool.
Halfway there a deep lethargy suddenly gripped him; a weakness he couldn't shake off. His head pounded and fresh gouts of blood flowed from his wound, curling downwards into the black depths, sucked away by the esprit below. He doubted he would make the edge of the pool.
"Keep swimming Thesa." The voice floated up from the nadir below. "Just a little further. It's not far. We will help you. Be brave. Fight the Black Guardian's promises, they are false."
Thesa's paw suddenly scraped against rock, and he realised he'd reached the side of the pool. Scrambling out of the water, he shook his coat, splattering spots of phosphorescent light against the wall of the cavern. He'd made it. He was alive!
"Go to the tunnel ahead of you. Hurry, there's no time left, the storm gathers apace."
Thesa entered the tunnel, the shimmering light emanating from his sodden fur reflecting dully from the surrounding walls. The ground beneath his feet trembled, and far above he sensed the loud clash of thunder ripping from the clouds.
Following the whispered directions in his head, Thesa stumbled his way along the tunnel, dizzy from his wound. He was weak, but found the strength to stagger on. The tunnel smelt outlandish, its walls smoother than they had any right to be. He stopped for a moment to peer closely at the concave surface. No badger had dug this tunnel, some other entity had created it.!

Chapter 30

Brokin slithered down the wall, slamming into the ground with a breath-taking thump. Groaning, he wondered whether he had the strength to carry out his plan. It would be so easy to give up: find some badger to take him to the Preceptor and throw himself on his mercy. Fortunately, apart from a sprained hock and bruised ribs, he seemed to be alright. Standing up, he shook his head, feeling weary. He'd had such grand plans to save Badachro Sett, but all he'd done was nearly kill himself!
A noise from the entrance tunnel caught his attention, so he scurried behind the taproot, crouching low. Cherva appeared, followed by two badgers, dragging a boar with a pure-white coat. They dropped him on the floor. The boar looked almost dead. Was this the badger called Darkburst that the Preceptor had been showing such an interest in?
The Preceptor entered, dismissing the guards with a flick of his paw. After they left, he turned to Cherva. "Is he still alive?"
"Barely."
"Where's Soffen? I said I needed her."
"She's disappeared, Preceptor."
Brokin heard footsteps approaching. When they stopped, he chanced a quick look. Grindel was bent over the unconscious boar, shaking him urgently. "Wake up, badger! Wake up!" There was no response.
"Shall I fetch some water?" Cherva asked.
"No," Grindel snapped back angrily. "Pick him up and follow me. Quickly, we haven't much time."
Flipping the smaller boar onto his broad back, Cherva followed Grindel into a low tunnel, the badger he carried scraping along the roof.
"Be careful with him, you idiot!" Grindel's voice floated down the tunnel to Brokin.
Once the trio were on their way, Brokin cautiously followed at a safe distance. After travelling for some time, they entered another tunnel. Brokin had never seen the like; perfectly formed and straight. He worried they would see him, so he hung back, following at a safe distance. The tunnel ended in an oddly shaped chamber with a roof so high he couldn't see it; the enormous space cowed him.
As Grindel and Cherva moved across the smooth floor, they faded from sight, and all too soon Brokin was alone, lost in a threatening vastness.
"Is that you, Brokin?"
The unexpected question made him jump. Feeling sick, he span round, raising a paw to fend off the expected attack, but it never came. He squinted, trying to focus on the shadowy figure to one side of the entrance. He'd walked right by the badger without noticing. It took a moment for him to recognise who had spoken, and when he did, the world stood still.
Before him stood his friend, Thesa. His eyes were alive with a tranquil inner strength, and he wore a serene expression. His fur twinkled with droplets of phosphorescence that sparkled oddly in the gloom. He carried a deep gash on his head, penetrating to the bone. Smiling, he nodded hello.
"Thesa, is that really you?" Brokin asked, in a shaky voice.
"Yes, it is."
"I was following…" A sudden coldness enveloped Brokin, exploring every part of his body before disappearing again.
Thesa appeared not to notice Brokin's discomfort. "I must join with him," he said. "You will help me."
"Join with whom? I don't understand." Again the coldness swirled through his body.
Thesa raised his paw and pointed. "With him," he said. "The sick one."
Brokin wrinkled his snout and moved away. The coldness settled around him once more, bitingly cold, and with it, a new determination. He'd come here to kill the Preceptor, so why hesitate? Many badgers had fought bravely and died so he could accomplish this task. "Stay here, Thesa," he said, "I'll come back when I've finished."
Thesa's paw shot out, grasping Brokin's tail in an iron grip. "No, I must go. You must stay here."
As Thesa walked out across the wide space, Brokin felt a great pressure lift from his mind, along with the shroud of coldness emanating from the cave deep below Fire Rock, where a beautiful orb span madly, gathering strength as its destiny neared completion.
*
High above Fire Rock, the storm seethed and boiled around itself, shaking the mightiest trees like blades of grass. Great forks of lightning snaked down, their passage picked out in a blinding white light. Majestically, the storm built to a crescendo high above the Brockenhurst Mountains, and sheets of rain scoured the land below, stripping all life from its bedrock, driving even the smallest creature from its nest. Two powerful lightning bolts struck the plateau, hurling substantial chunks of rock skywards, where the rapacious winds scooped them away.
Standing in the middle of Brockenhurst Forest, alone and battered beyond recognition, stood a once proud tree, its branches long gone, stripped by the force of the storm. White sapwood wept from its wounds — huge tears shed for a million unborn seedlings. Deep beneath the ground, where the dying tree's taproot pierced the Grand Chamber, the plant writhed in agony, whipping like an angry snake. Above ground, the wind worried away at the once great trunk until finally it snapped with a crack echoing across the mountain tops.
At the majestic tree's weakest point, where Boddaert and his Magi had carved the magical Taproot Chamber, the mighty root parted with pent-up energy, bringing enormous chunks of rock crashing down into the chamber below, tearing open the heart of Brockenhurst Sett. The once magnificent tree screamed one last, dying protest, and the wind rushed into the immense scar, scouring away every trace of life.

Chapter 31

As the storm pounded its way into Brockenhurst Sett, in the chambers below Fire Rock, the last elements of Boddaert's Magic came together.
Deep beneath the turbulent waters of the pool, four spirits strained against their earthly bonds.
Within the spinning orb, the beings who'd once walked the paths of Brockenhurst Forest, sensing the nearness of the Prime Mover, sent out their anima in a frenzied search for union, impatient for the coming.
In the subterranean bowels of Fire Rock, five badgers held the future of Boddaert's Realm in their paws: Grindel, his claws resting on the jagged edge of the plywood box that had become so much a part of his life: Cherva, at his master's side, glaring intently at the white badger, wondering what secrets lay there and whether he could use them for his own ends: Thesa, unmoving, the air about him shimmering with cold: Between them, Darkburst, head thrown back, the white fur on his throat separated into ruffles, exposing the pink skin beneath: Across the chamber, Brokin, watching the distant tableau, mind a turmoil.
White on Black — Sun on Moon — Yin on Yang.
Grindel slashed a sharp claw across the opening he'd already chewed in the side of the plywood box, parting the oil-impregnated paper lining the inside, allowing them all a brief glimpse into their future. A dull light reflected from the egg-shaped objects packed tightly inside. When the paper parted, one fell out, spinning on the floor in a lazy circle, twinkling in the reflected light from Thesa's fur.
"Don't…" Brokin shouted as Grindel went to pick it up.
Grindel stopped, looking across the chamber at the boar who dared to give him orders. He growled low in his throat, reaching out again. This is the Fire Soul. he was certain of it! He studied each piece of Boddaert's Magic, eyes narrowing. Here they all were — Darkburst, his fur stark against the darker floor – the White Coat; the stone brought back from the shores of Migaro Lake – the Circle of Claws; the strangely shaped egg – the Fire Soul. He had only to bring these three pieces together to release the energy of Boddaert's Magic and realise his dream.
As Grindel's paw touched the egg-shaped object, Brokin ran across the chamber and snatched it away. Roaring in rage, Grindel slashed out at Brokin, knocking him off his feet. The object flew from Brokin's grasp, rolling across the floor until it came to rest at Cherva's feet. The big badger reached down and picked it up, backing across the chamber towards the box of WW II grenades.
This was his chance at last. He held the magic in his paws. Grindel and Brokin fought near the entrance to the chamber, both lost to the depths of their rage, thrusting and parrying with flashing claws as they tried to kill each other.
Thesa smiled, the air from his mouth frosting the fur along his snout. He stepped forward, looking down at Darkburst before extending his paw and touching the white fur on the young badger's injured leg with the tip of a claw. He nodded as a line of ice encased it, then threw himself across Darkburst's body, covering it completely with his own.
Cherva held the ring of the strangely shaped egg between his teeth and pulled, his eyes widening as the clip pinged free and fell to the floor. Holding the object between his paws, he sniffed the strange indentations covering its surface, wondering what they were and how he could release their magic. A flash of light seared through his body.
Shrapnel shredding Thesa's black fur, covering Darkburst with a bloody mess.
The rest of the grenades exploded, blowing Brokin and Grindel along the concrete tunnel, covering them both with tons of debris.
*
Far from Fire Rock, beyond Low Meadow, beneath a slim ash tree, at the edge of an undulating field, a pregnant sow watched the cloudless sky, wondering whether her special boar was also watching the same stars. She hoped with all her heart he was, because it would mean they were sharing something, even though they were so far apart.
Sighing gently, she turned back to her lonely burrow. Perhaps he would come during the next moon-cycle, or maybe the one after that.
*
Much farther away, where the shores of Migaro Lake lapped gently at the surrounding fields, an elderly boar stopped his eternal search for food and raised his head for a moment. Had he heard something or were his old ears finally failing him? No, there on the horizon, he spotted something.
Slikit squinted his eyes from habit, but needn't have bothered this time, because he had no trouble seeing the great fireball that had erupted into the sky. So strong was the blast that even the boiling storm rolled back in reaction to its hot gases, tamed for once by a stronger force.
Slikit blinked back tears as black clouds formed over Brockenhurst Sett. A great sadness filled the old badger's heart, as though he'd just lost a dear friend. He sat back on his haunches, wondering why he suddenly felt so alone. Shaking his head against the coldness that had descended on him, he grumbled his way along the overgrown path, his cracked old voice fading as the westerly wind grew in intensity.
